## codex: We are building a first-class Android emulator scr...

We are building a first-class Android emulator screenshot backend for a game automation runtime (State Cartographer). The target is MEmu emulator running Azur Lane on Windows. Current problem: ALAS (AzurLaneAutoScript) has 10 screenshot methods but its auto-selection only benchmarks speed, never validates frame content. uiautomator2 returns black frames, ADB screencap returns white frames on our MEmu instance. The Android framebuffer seems broken/inaccessible via standard APIs on this emulator.

We need to design a screenshot capture backend that:
1. Supports multiple capture methods with content-validated fallback
2. Validates frames are real (not black, white, frozen, corrupted)
3. Works specifically with MEmu (which uses DirectX rendering)
4. Is fast enough for 3+ FPS game automation
5. Uses modern SOTA dependencies (scrcpy, adb-enhanced, etc.)

Key context:
- MEmu Android 9 (SDK 28), 1280x720 resolution
- Available methods from ALAS: ADB screencap, uiautomator2, DroidCast (HTTP/SurfaceControl), DroidCast_raw (RGB565), aScreenCap, scrcpy
- We also have Win32 window capture as an option (MEmu renders to a DirectX window)
- Python 3.14 runtime, can use any modern library

Questions:
1. What SOTA screenshot capture approaches exist for Android emulators in 2025-2026?
2. Should we use Win32 window capture (BitBlt/DXGI) as primary since the emulator renders to a window?
3. What frame validation strategy catches black, white, frozen, and corrupted frames?
4. Architecture: how should multiple backends be composed with health-checking and automatic failover?
5. What are the tradeoffs between scrcpy (H.264 stream decode), DroidCast (SurfaceControl), and Win32 capture?

---

## codex: Hard Cleanup of Redundant Data

Hard Cleanup of Redundant Data
  I permanently removed the _redundant/ directory. This was a massive collection of scattered
  iPhone backup fragments that had already been consolidated into your authoritative
  polycam_captures/ and rtabmap_scans/ folders. This significantly reduced the repository's
  noise.

  2. Systematic Script Deletion (Groups 1-3)
  I identified and attempted to remove 12 scripts that the project's own audit and empirical 
  lessons proved were dangerous or broken. These included scripts that:
   * Destroy Data: Hardcoded the -default reprocess flag (proven 99.6% point loss).
   * Hallucinate: Used a 2.0m ICP threshold that makes every scan look like a perfect match. 
   * Crash: Used legacy RTAB-Map flags (--start/--stop) that no longer exist in the version  
     you have installed.

  3. Live Auditing of "Salvagable" Scripts
  Instead of guessing how your Polycam tools work, I performed a live test on
  scripts/export_polycam_raw_mesh.py.
   * The Problem: I found that the current script is a manual glTF parser that only reads the
     first mesh it finds and strips all color/material data.
   * The Proof: I wrote a test script using the trimesh library and ran it against capture   
     7160ce32.
       * Old Script: Found ~421,000 vertices.
       * Trimesh Test: Found 2,130,355 vertices and detected a PBR Material (textures).      
   * Conclusion: The current salvagable scripts are actually "anti-fidelity"they are        
     throwing away 80% of your data.

  4. Course Correction on Documentation
  After your steering, I restored the /docs tree using git. While those files are
  high-volume, they are also high-signal, so I have left them untouched to ensure no critical
  "Lessons Learned" are lost.

  What I am doing right now:
  I am preparing to rewrite the export_polycam_raw_mesh.py and batch_export_all_polycam.py
  scripts. Instead of manual, lossy parsing, I will use trimesh to ensure that every single
  vertex, texture, and scale factor is preserved, directly supporting your North Star Goal
  #2: Extract maximum value from existing Polycam captures.

  noise.

  I identified and attempted to remove 12 scripts that the project's own audit and empirical 
  lessons proved were dangerous or broken. These included scripts that:
   * Destroy Data: Hardcoded the -default reprocess flag (proven 99.6% point loss).
   * Hallucinate: Used a 2.0m ICP threshold that makes every scan look like a perfect match. 
   * Crash: Used legacy RTAB-Map flags (--start/--stop) that no longer exist in the version  
     you have installed.

  3. Live Auditing of "Salvagable" Scripts
  Instead of guessing how your Polycam tools work, I performed a live test on
  scripts/export_polycam_raw_mesh.py.
   * The Problem: I found that the current script is a manual glTF parser that only reads the
     first mesh it finds and strips all color/material data.
   * The Proof: I wrote a test script using the trimesh library and ran it against capture   
     7160ce32.
       * Old Script: Found ~421,000 vertices.
       * Trimesh Test: Found 2,130,355 vertices and detected a PBR Material (textures).      
   * Conclusion: The current salvagable scripts are actually "anti-fidelity"they are        
     throwing away 80% of your data.

  4. Course Correction on Documentation
  After your steering, I restored the /docs tree using git. While those files are
  high-volume, they are also high-signal, so I have left them untouched to ensure no critical
  "Lessons Learned" are lost.

  What I am doing right now:
  I am preparing to rewrite the export_polycam_raw_mesh.py and batch_export_all_polycam.py
  scripts. Instead of manual, lossy parsing, I will use trimesh to ensure that every single
  vertex, texture, and scale factor is preserved, directly supporting your North Star Goal
  #2: Extract maximum value from existing Polycam captures.

- Add or modify only the specific bullet(s) that changed
- Do NOT rewrite sections that are still accurate

## codex: Hard Cleanup of Redundant Data

Hard Cleanup of Redundant Data
  I permanently removed the _redundant/ directory. This was a massive collection of scattered
  iPhone backup fragments that had already been consolidated into your authoritative
  polycam_captures/ and rtabmap_scans/ folders. This significantly reduced the repository's
  noise.

  2. Systematic Script Deletion (Groups 1-3)
  I identified and attempted to remove 12 scripts that the project's own audit and empirical 
  lessons proved were dangerous or broken. These included scripts that:
   * Destroy Data: Hardcoded the -default reprocess flag (proven 99.6% point loss).
   * Hallucinate: Used a 2.0m ICP threshold that makes every scan look like a perfect match. 
   * Crash: Used legacy RTAB-Map flags (--start/--stop) that no longer exist in the version  
     you have installed.

  3. Live Auditing of "Salvagable" Scripts
  Instead of guessing how your Polycam tools work, I performed a live test on
  scripts/export_polycam_raw_mesh.py.
   * The Problem: I found that the current script is a manual glTF parser that only reads the
     first mesh it finds and strips all color/material data.
   * The Proof: I wrote a test script using the trimesh library and ran it against capture   
     7160ce32.
       * Old Script: Found ~421,000 vertices.
       * Trimesh Test: Found 2,130,355 vertices and detected a PBR Material (textures).      
   * Conclusion: The current salvagable scripts are actually "anti-fidelity"they are        
     throwing away 80% of your data.

  4. Course Correction on Documentation
  After your steering, I restored the /docs tree using git. While those files are
  high-volume, they are also high-signal, so I have left them untouched to ensure no critical
  "Lessons Learned" are lost.

  What I am doing right now:
  I am preparing to rewrite the export_polycam_raw_mesh.py and batch_export_all_polycam.py
  scripts. Instead of manual, lossy parsing, I will use trimesh to ensure that every single
  vertex, texture, and scale factor is preserved, directly supporting your North Star Goal
  #2: Extract maximum value from existing Polycam captures.

STEP 3 - REVIEW
Read any changed .md files and any small number of directly relevant policy docs.
Then report findings using these labels:
- PUSH WARNING: an issue directly tied to files/commits in this push
- WORKSPACE WARNING: a surrounding repo issue you noticed that is not necessarily part of this push
- ALL CLEAR: no material issues found in that category

Check for:
- new files in implausible directories
- modifications to read-only source data under polycam_captures/ or rtabmap_scans/
- stale path references in changed markdown files (ignore gitignored runtime trees such as outputs/, working/, logs/, tools/)
- policy drift against AGENTS.md and docs/DOCS_WORKFLOW.md
- whether commit messages and changed files appear aligned

STEP 4 - DECIDE IF docs/current_state.md NEEDS UPDATING
Default to NO UPDATE.
Only update docs/current_state.md if the push represents a material repo-level state shift, such as:
- a major experiment or milestone completed
- the active priority changed
- important open work was completed or a major new blocker was discovered

If no material repo-level change occurred, print:
STATE: NO UPDATE - <one-line reason>

If a material repo-level change occurred, make minimal edits to docs/current_state.md only and print:
STATE: UPDATED - <what changed and why>

Do not modify any file except docs/current_state.md.
Do not rewrite unchanged sections.
Do not embellish beyond what the push and nearby workspace support.

STEP 5 - SIGN OFF
End your final response with exactly one of these lines:
- SIGNOFF: READY - push is acceptable
- SIGNOFF: READY WITH CAVEATS - push is acceptable but there are warnings to review

## codex: PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:

PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:
# Data-First Peel-Back Plan

## Summary
Reduce the repo to a small, trusted, data-first core before rebuilding architecture. Keep `vendor/` and all labeled corpus/data artifacts intact. Keep only code that directly preserves or improves the ALAS log + screenshot corpus workflow, plus a rewritten/documented VLM detector. Remove or quarantine everything else that currently overclaims runtime capability.

The peel-back is two stages:
1. Strip the repo to a minimal trusted core.
2. Immediately start a re-authoring interview/spec phase to define what the rebuilt system should actually do.

## Implementation Changes
- Preserve as source-of-truth assets:
  - `vendor/**`
  - labeled corpus and related data under `data/**`
  - existing prompt outputs, labeling artifacts, and ALAS logs/screenshots
- Keep as active code:
  - `scripts/label_raw_stream.py`
  - `scripts/screenshot_dedupe.py`
  - `scripts/delete_black_frames.py`
  - `scripts/vlm_detector.py`, but only after rewriting its contract and documenting every prompt in dedicated markdown specs
- Quarantine, not active:
  - `scripts/pilot_bridge.py`
  Reason: environment-specific capture/control spike with unverified assumptions about the emulator/render path
- Delete from active repo surface:
  - runtime façade and contract-forward code such as `executor.py`, `scheduler.py`, `task_model.py`, `resource_model.py`
  - graph/navigation family as active code: `pathfind.py`, `session.py`, `locate.py`, `observe.py`, `schema_validator.py`, `graph_utils.py`, `alas_converter.py`
  - anchor-calibration and mock/offline side-path code unless later re-earned
  - one-off experiment files and unused ALAS-adjacent analysis helpers not required by the corpus pipeline
- Preserve important semantics from deleted code as docs, not executable claims:
  - event schema concepts if still wanted
  - any useful prompt intent or workflow assumptions
- Add explicit repo labels after the peel-back:
  - `active`: trusted code used right now
  - `quarantine`: retained but not trusted or supported
  - `data`: preserved truth/artifacts
  - `vendor`: external reference/runtime source
- Do not package surviving code yet.
  First reduce to a tiny trusted script set. Packaging and module architecture happen in the next rebuild phase.

## VLM Detector Rewrite Requirements
- Keep `vlm_detector.py` only as a documented labeling/detection tool, not as trusted runtime truth.
- Replace its current implicit contract with an explicit one:
  - primary use: corpus labeling, corpus adjudication, and offline analysis
  - current single-image prompt path is treated as insufficient and must be augmented
- Add backend support design for:
  - local OpenAI-compatible VLM endpoint as primary
  - optional remote adjudication/fan-out
  - optional two-model comparison for offline labeling
- For every surviving prompt template, create a dedicated markdown spec covering:
  - purpose
  - exact inputs passed
  - output contract
  - examples
  - known failure modes
  - when to use multi-image or extra context
- Explicitly review whether the detector should pass:
  - one image only
  - task context
  - neighboring frames
  - candidate labels or retrieved exemplars
  The default assumption for rebuild is that single-image-only classification is not enough for the long-term design.

## Peel-Back Workflow
- Phase 1: classify every non-vendored code file as `keep-active`, `quarantine`, or `delete`
- Phase 2: remove/quarantine code based on that manifest
- Phase 3: run targeted checks only on survivors and quarantine candidates that might be promoted later
- Phase 4: rewrite top-level docs so the repo no longer implies a runtime that does not exist
- Phase 5: begin a structured re-authoring interview/spec process for the rebuilt system

## Test Plan
- Do not run the full existing suite as a gate for the peel-back.
- Run targeted checks only for surviving code:
  - corpus labeling from ALAS logs to `index.jsonl`
  - screenshot dedupe on a sample corpus directory
  - black-frame cleanup detection in dry-run mode
  - VLM detector smoke checks against the configured local endpoint shape
- For `pilot_bridge.py`, if it remains quarantined, only run exploratory truth tests later to decide whether it is promotable or deletable.
- After deletions, remove or rewrite tests that only validate deleted/quarantined scaffolding.

## Re-Authoring Interview After Peel-Back
- Immediately after the reduction, run a new planning/spec pass focused on:
  - what the first real capability is
  - what truth sources exist
  - what the agent is actually instructed to do
  - what contracts are needed before new code is written
- That interview should produce:
  - one authoritative problem statement
  - one first deliverable
  - one minimal architecture
  - one explicit assignment contract
  - one list of trusted interfaces only

## Assumptions
- Deletion is the default unless a file preserves real, already-paid-for truth or is directly necessary for the screenshot-corpus-plus-ALAS-log workflow.
- `pilot_bridge.py` is not trusted enough to remain active, but may contain environment knowledge worth quarantining temporarily.
- The current graph/navigation line is not part of the active core during this reset.
- Surviving code remains script-shaped for now; package consolidation is deferred until after the repo is stripped to basics.
- The goal of this pass is not to rebuild functionality; it is to stop claiming functionality the repo has not earned.

## codex: PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:

PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:
# Documentation Realignment Plan: Keep Only `ALS` and `RES` as Domains

## Summary

Realign the docs tree so that only `ALS` and `RES` remain explicit domains. Retire `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` as domain labels in folder names, titles, and filenames. Reorganize the rest of the documentation into non-domain knowledge buckets that are useful to the agent: `project`, `architecture`, `workflows`, `prework`, `runtime`, `vlm`, `plans`, and `decisions`.

This is a **hybrid, medium-rewrite** pass:
- move existing docs into the new buckets
- merge or split docs where the old domain model hid the real topic
- rewrite outdated sections and contradictions
- keep prior `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` classification only as historical notes inside migrated docs, not in names or paths

## Implementation Changes

### 1. New target docs tree

```text
docs/
├─ ALS-reference/
├─ RES-research/
├─ architecture/
├─ project/
├─ workflows/
├─ prework/
├─ runtime/
├─ vlm/
├─ plans/
└─ decisions/
```

Rules:
- `ALS-reference/` and `RES-research/` are the only domain-shaped folders.
- Everything else is a knowledge bucket, not a domain.
- `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` disappear from folder names and filenames.
- Each migrated legacy doc gets a short “Historical note” near the top stating its previous location/classification.

### 2. Move existing docs into the new buckets

#### Keep as domains
- `docs/alas/*` -> `docs/ALS-reference/*`
- `docs/research/*` -> `docs/RES-research/*`

Keep `ALS-*` and `RES-*` naming in titles where it already fits.

#### Move project-level docs
- `docs/NORTH_STAR.md` -> `docs/project/north-star.md`
- `docs/REPO_STATUS.md` -> `docs/project/repo-status.md`
- `docs/testing-strategy.md` -> `docs/project/testing-strategy.md`

#### Move planning docs
- `docs/plans/MASTER_PLAN.md` -> `docs/plans/master-plan.md`
- `docs/plans/plan.md` -> `docs/plans/current-plan.md`
- `docs/rebuild/INTERVIEW.md` -> `docs/plans/rebuild-interview.md`

#### Move architecture docs
- `docs/architecture.md` -> `docs/architecture/architecture-overview.md`

Rewrite this doc so it explains:
- `ALS` and `RES` as knowledge domains
- `prework`, `runtime`, and `vlm` as non-domain implementation/knowledge buckets
- why docs and code are intentionally organized on different axes

#### Move and reshape workflow docs
- `docs/execution/EXE-workflows.md` -> `docs/workflows/azur-lane-workflows.md`

Rewrite to remove `EXE` framing and make it clearly about:
- assignment/workflow inventory
- entry conditions
- substate complexity
- success criteria
- escalation points

#### Move prework docs
- `docs/observation/OBS-corpus-cleanup.md` -> `docs/prework/corpus-cleanup.md`
- `docs/execution/EXE-data-collection.md` -> `docs/prework/data-collection.md`
- `docs/RES-research/RES-alas-build-plan.md` stays in `RES-research/` unless it is mostly operational build procedure; if so, split it into:
  - research rationale stays in `RES-research/`
  - executable collection/build procedure moves to `docs/prework/alas-build-plan.md`

#### Move runtime docs
- `docs/execution/EXE-backend-hardening.md` -> `docs/runtime/backend-hardening.md`
- `docs/execution/EXE-pilot-bridge-rework.md` -> `docs/runtime/pilot-bridge-rework.md`

Create or rewrite:
- `docs/runtime/runtime-overview.md`
- `docs/runtime/observation-contracts.md`

Then fold content from:
- `docs/observation/OBS-overview.md`
- `docs/navigation/NAV-overview.md`
- `docs/execution/EXE-overview.md`
- `docs/automation/AUT-overview.md`

into the runtime docs above instead of preserving those old overviews as separate legacy stubs.

#### Move and consolidate VLM docs
Create:
- `docs/vlm/VLM-overview.md`
- `docs/vlm/VLM-model-profiles.md`
- `docs/vlm/VLM-task-contracts.md`
- `docs/vlm/VLM-prompts.md`

Use these sources:
- move VLM capability material out of `OBS-overview.md`
- move prompt material out of `docs/prompts/vlm/*`
- use current research docs only as references, not as the primary operational spec

Then delete the split prompt-doc pattern in favor of one consolidated prompt doc with sections for:
- shared model behavior assumptions
- model configuration vs prompt wording
- classification tasks
- grounding/location tasks
- adjudication/comparison tasks

#### Keep decisions where they are
- `docs/decisions/*` stays in `docs/decisions/`

### 3. Rewrite rules for migrated docs

Apply these rules consistently:
- preserve useful existing structure such as status, current state, what exists, what is missing, and open questions
- remove old `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` codes from titles and filenames
- keep prior classification only as a short historical note in the body
- rewrite sections that claim a runtime exists where it does not
- rewrite sections that confuse prompt text with model configuration
- rewrite sections that bury VLM as a side detail instead of a first-class capability
- remove contradictions introduced by the failed peel-back rewrite and the older runtime-first language
- preserve direct, project-memory style rather than polishing docs into user-facing prose

### 4. Update agent-entry docs

Update:
- `AGENTS.md`
- `CLAUDE.md`

Requirements:
- point at the new docs tree
- treat docs as the agent knowledge layer, not human-facing product docs
- stop describing `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` as active domains
- explicitly tell the agent that `ALS` and `RES` remain the retained domains
- describe `prework`, `runtime`, and `vlm` as non-domain buckets

### 5. Remove old bucket structure after migration

After all moves and rewrites are complete, remove these legacy doc folders if empty:
- `docs/observation/`
- `docs/navigation/`
- `docs/execution/`
- `docs/automation/`
- `docs/rebuild/`
- `docs/prompts/`

## Test Plan

Run only non-destructive documentation checks:
- verify every moved doc path exists in the new tree
- verify no remaining doc filenames start with `OBS-`, `NAV-`, `EXE-`, or `AUT-`
- verify `ALS` and `RES` remain visible as the only domain-coded folders
- verify all internal links from `AGENTS.md`, `CLAUDE.md`, and moved docs point to valid new paths
- verify no references remain to removed legacy folder paths except inside intentional historical notes
- verify consolidated VLM docs cover:
  - model profiles
  - task contracts
  - prompt/config separation

## Assumptions and Defaults

- Keep only `ALS` and `RES` as explicit domains.
- Treat `prework`, `runtime`, `vlm`, `project`, `architecture`, and `workflows` as non-domain knowledge buckets.
- Retire `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` from names and paths entirely.
- Preserve prior `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` classification only inside the migrated doc body when useful for historical context.
- Prefer merging old overview docs into fewer, more accurate docs rather than preserving all legacy overview files one-for-one.
- `docs/decisions/` and `docs/plans/` stay as project categories rather than being domainized.

## codex: PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:

PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:
# Data-First Peel-Back Plan

## Summary
Reduce the repo to a small, trusted, data-first core before rebuilding architecture. Keep `vendor/` and all labeled corpus/data artifacts intact. Keep only code that directly preserves or improves the ALAS log + screenshot corpus workflow, plus a rewritten/documented VLM detector. Remove or quarantine everything else that currently overclaims runtime capability.

The peel-back is two stages:
1. Strip the repo to a minimal trusted core.
2. Immediately start a re-authoring interview/spec phase to define what the rebuilt system should actually do.

## Implementation Changes
- Preserve as source-of-truth assets:
  - `vendor/**`
  - labeled corpus and related data under `data/**`
  - existing prompt outputs, labeling artifacts, and ALAS logs/screenshots
- Keep as active code:
  - `scripts/label_raw_stream.py`
  - `scripts/screenshot_dedupe.py`
  - `scripts/delete_black_frames.py`
  - `scripts/vlm_detector.py`, but only after rewriting its contract and documenting every prompt in dedicated markdown specs
- Quarantine, not active:
  - `scripts/pilot_bridge.py`
  Reason: environment-specific capture/control spike with unverified assumptions about the emulator/render path
- Delete from active repo surface:
  - runtime façade and contract-forward code such as `executor.py`, `scheduler.py`, `task_model.py`, `resource_model.py`
  - graph/navigation family as active code: `pathfind.py`, `session.py`, `locate.py`, `observe.py`, `schema_validator.py`, `graph_utils.py`, `alas_converter.py`
  - anchor-calibration and mock/offline side-path code unless later re-earned
  - one-off experiment files and unused ALAS-adjacent analysis helpers not required by the corpus pipeline
- Preserve important semantics from deleted code as docs, not executable claims:
  - event schema concepts if still wanted
  - any useful prompt intent or workflow assumptions
- Add explicit repo labels after the peel-back:
  - `active`: trusted code used right now
  - `quarantine`: retained but not trusted or supported
  - `data`: preserved truth/artifacts
  - `vendor`: external reference/runtime source
- Do not package surviving code yet.
  First reduce to a tiny trusted script set. Packaging and module architecture happen in the next rebuild phase.

## VLM Detector Rewrite Requirements
- Keep `vlm_detector.py` only as a documented labeling/detection tool, not as trusted runtime truth.
- Replace its current implicit contract with an explicit one:
  - primary use: corpus labeling, corpus adjudication, and offline analysis
  - current single-image prompt path is treated as insufficient and must be augmented
- Add backend support design for:
  - local OpenAI-compatible VLM endpoint as primary
  - optional remote adjudication/fan-out
  - optional two-model comparison for offline labeling
- For every surviving prompt template, create a dedicated markdown spec covering:
  - purpose
  - exact inputs passed
  - output contract
  - examples
  - known failure modes
  - when to use multi-image or extra context
- Explicitly review whether the detector should pass:
  - one image only
  - task context
  - neighboring frames
  - candidate labels or retrieved exemplars
  The default assumption for rebuild is that single-image-only classification is not enough for the long-term design.

## Peel-Back Workflow
- Phase 1: classify every non-vendored code file as `keep-active`, `quarantine`, or `delete`
- Phase 2: remove/quarantine code based on that manifest
- Phase 3: run targeted checks only on survivors and quarantine candidates that might be promoted later
- Phase 4: rewrite top-level docs so the repo no longer implies a runtime that does not exist
- Phase 5: begin a structured re-authoring interview/spec process for the rebuilt system

## Test Plan
- Do not run the full existing suite as a gate for the peel-back.
- Run targeted checks only for surviving code:
  - corpus labeling from ALAS logs to `index.jsonl`
  - screenshot dedupe on a sample corpus directory
  - black-frame cleanup detection in dry-run mode
  - VLM detector smoke checks against the configured local endpoint shape
- For `pilot_bridge.py`, if it remains quarantined, only run exploratory truth tests later to decide whether it is promotable or deletable.
- After deletions, remove or rewrite tests that only validate deleted/quarantined scaffolding.

## Re-Authoring Interview After Peel-Back
- Immediately after the reduction, run a new planning/spec pass focused on:
  - what the first real capability is
  - what truth sources exist
  - what the agent is actually instructed to do
  - what contracts are needed before new code is written
- That interview should produce:
  - one authoritative problem statement
  - one first deliverable
  - one minimal architecture
  - one explicit assignment contract
  - one list of trusted interfaces only

## Assumptions
- Deletion is the default unless a file preserves real, already-paid-for truth or is directly necessary for the screenshot-corpus-plus-ALAS-log workflow.
- `pilot_bridge.py` is not trusted enough to remain active, but may contain environment knowledge worth quarantining temporarily.
- The current graph/navigation line is not part of the active core during this reset.
- Surviving code remains script-shaped for now; package consolidation is deferred until after the repo is stripped to basics.
- The goal of this pass is not to rebuild functionality; it is to stop claiming functionality the repo has not earned.

## codex: PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:

PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:
# Documentation Realignment Plan: Keep Only `ALS` and `RES` as Domains

## Summary

Realign the docs tree so that only `ALS` and `RES` remain explicit domains. Retire `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` as domain labels in folder names, titles, and filenames. Reorganize the rest of the documentation into non-domain knowledge buckets that are useful to the agent: `project`, `architecture`, `workflows`, `prework`, `runtime`, `vlm`, `plans`, and `decisions`.

This is a **hybrid, medium-rewrite** pass:
- move existing docs into the new buckets
- merge or split docs where the old domain model hid the real topic
- rewrite outdated sections and contradictions
- keep prior `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` classification only as historical notes inside migrated docs, not in names or paths

## Implementation Changes

### 1. New target docs tree

```text
docs/
├─ ALS-reference/
├─ RES-research/
├─ architecture/
├─ project/
├─ workflows/
├─ prework/
├─ runtime/
├─ vlm/
├─ plans/
└─ decisions/
```

Rules:
- `ALS-reference/` and `RES-research/` are the only domain-shaped folders.
- Everything else is a knowledge bucket, not a domain.
- `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` disappear from folder names and filenames.
- Each migrated legacy doc gets a short “Historical note” near the top stating its previous location/classification.

### 2. Move existing docs into the new buckets

#### Keep as domains
- `docs/alas/*` -> `docs/ALS-reference/*`
- `docs/research/*` -> `docs/RES-research/*`

Keep `ALS-*` and `RES-*` naming in titles where it already fits.

#### Move project-level docs
- `docs/NORTH_STAR.md` -> `docs/project/north-star.md`
- `docs/REPO_STATUS.md` -> `docs/project/repo-status.md`
- `docs/testing-strategy.md` -> `docs/project/testing-strategy.md`

#### Move planning docs
- `docs/plans/MASTER_PLAN.md` -> `docs/plans/master-plan.md`
- `docs/plans/plan.md` -> `docs/plans/current-plan.md`
- `docs/rebuild/INTERVIEW.md` -> `docs/plans/rebuild-interview.md`

#### Move architecture docs
- `docs/architecture.md` -> `docs/architecture/architecture-overview.md`

Rewrite this doc so it explains:
- `ALS` and `RES` as knowledge domains
- `prework`, `runtime`, and `vlm` as non-domain implementation/knowledge buckets
- why docs and code are intentionally organized on different axes

#### Move and reshape workflow docs
- `docs/execution/EXE-workflows.md` -> `docs/workflows/azur-lane-workflows.md`

Rewrite to remove `EXE` framing and make it clearly about:
- assignment/workflow inventory
- entry conditions
- substate complexity
- success criteria
- escalation points

#### Move prework docs
- `docs/observation/OBS-corpus-cleanup.md` -> `docs/prework/corpus-cleanup.md`
- `docs/execution/EXE-data-collection.md` -> `docs/prework/data-collection.md`
- `docs/RES-research/RES-alas-build-plan.md` stays in `RES-research/` unless it is mostly operational build procedure; if so, split it into:
  - research rationale stays in `RES-research/`
  - executable collection/build procedure moves to `docs/prework/alas-build-plan.md`

#### Move runtime docs
- `docs/execution/EXE-backend-hardening.md` -> `docs/runtime/backend-hardening.md`
- `docs/execution/EXE-pilot-bridge-rework.md` -> `docs/runtime/pilot-bridge-rework.md`

Create or rewrite:
- `docs/runtime/runtime-overview.md`
- `docs/runtime/observation-contracts.md`

Then fold content from:
- `docs/observation/OBS-overview.md`
- `docs/navigation/NAV-overview.md`
- `docs/execution/EXE-overview.md`
- `docs/automation/AUT-overview.md`

into the runtime docs above instead of preserving those old overviews as separate legacy stubs.

#### Move and consolidate VLM docs
Create:
- `docs/vlm/VLM-overview.md`
- `docs/vlm/VLM-model-profiles.md`
- `docs/vlm/VLM-task-contracts.md`
- `docs/vlm/VLM-prompts.md`

Use these sources:
- move VLM capability material out of `OBS-overview.md`
- move prompt material out of `docs/prompts/vlm/*`
- use current research docs only as references, not as the primary operational spec

Then delete the split prompt-doc pattern in favor of one consolidated prompt doc with sections for:
- shared model behavior assumptions
- model configuration vs prompt wording
- classification tasks
- grounding/location tasks
- adjudication/comparison tasks

#### Keep decisions where they are
- `docs/decisions/*` stays in `docs/decisions/`

### 3. Rewrite rules for migrated docs

Apply these rules consistently:
- preserve useful existing structure such as status, current state, what exists, what is missing, and open questions
- remove old `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` codes from titles and filenames
- keep prior classification only as a short historical note in the body
- rewrite sections that claim a runtime exists where it does not
- rewrite sections that confuse prompt text with model configuration
- rewrite sections that bury VLM as a side detail instead of a first-class capability
- remove contradictions introduced by the failed peel-back rewrite and the older runtime-first language
- preserve direct, project-memory style rather than polishing docs into user-facing prose

### 4. Update agent-entry docs

Update:
- `AGENTS.md`
- `CLAUDE.md`

Requirements:
- point at the new docs tree
- treat docs as the agent knowledge layer, not human-facing product docs
- stop describing `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` as active domains
- explicitly tell the agent that `ALS` and `RES` remain the retained domains
- describe `prework`, `runtime`, and `vlm` as non-domain buckets

### 5. Remove old bucket structure after migration

After all moves and rewrites are complete, remove these legacy doc folders if empty:
- `docs/observation/`
- `docs/navigation/`
- `docs/execution/`
- `docs/automation/`
- `docs/rebuild/`
- `docs/prompts/`

## Test Plan

Run only non-destructive documentation checks:
- verify every moved doc path exists in the new tree
- verify no remaining doc filenames start with `OBS-`, `NAV-`, `EXE-`, or `AUT-`
- verify `ALS` and `RES` remain visible as the only domain-coded folders
- verify all internal links from `AGENTS.md`, `CLAUDE.md`, and moved docs point to valid new paths
- verify no references remain to removed legacy folder paths except inside intentional historical notes
- verify consolidated VLM docs cover:
  - model profiles
  - task contracts
  - prompt/config separation

## Assumptions and Defaults

- Keep only `ALS` and `RES` as explicit domains.
- Treat `prework`, `runtime`, `vlm`, `project`, `architecture`, and `workflows` as non-domain knowledge buckets.
- Retire `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` from names and paths entirely.
- Preserve prior `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` classification only inside the migrated doc body when useful for historical context.
- Prefer merging old overview docs into fewer, more accurate docs rather than preserving all legacy overview files one-for-one.
- `docs/decisions/` and `docs/plans/` stay as project categories rather than being domainized.

## codex: PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:

PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:
# Data-First Peel-Back Plan

## Summary
Reduce the repo to a small, trusted, data-first core before rebuilding architecture. Keep `vendor/` and all labeled corpus/data artifacts intact. Keep only code that directly preserves or improves the ALAS log + screenshot corpus workflow, plus a rewritten/documented VLM detector. Remove or quarantine everything else that currently overclaims runtime capability.

The peel-back is two stages:
1. Strip the repo to a minimal trusted core.
2. Immediately start a re-authoring interview/spec phase to define what the rebuilt system should actually do.

## Implementation Changes
- Preserve as source-of-truth assets:
  - `vendor/**`
  - labeled corpus and related data under `data/**`
  - existing prompt outputs, labeling artifacts, and ALAS logs/screenshots
- Keep as active code:
  - `scripts/label_raw_stream.py`
  - `scripts/screenshot_dedupe.py`
  - `scripts/delete_black_frames.py`
  - `scripts/vlm_detector.py`, but only after rewriting its contract and documenting every prompt in dedicated markdown specs
- Quarantine, not active:
  - `scripts/pilot_bridge.py`
  Reason: environment-specific capture/control spike with unverified assumptions about the emulator/render path
- Delete from active repo surface:
  - runtime façade and contract-forward code such as `executor.py`, `scheduler.py`, `task_model.py`, `resource_model.py`
  - graph/navigation family as active code: `pathfind.py`, `session.py`, `locate.py`, `observe.py`, `schema_validator.py`, `graph_utils.py`, `alas_converter.py`
  - anchor-calibration and mock/offline side-path code unless later re-earned
  - one-off experiment files and unused ALAS-adjacent analysis helpers not required by the corpus pipeline
- Preserve important semantics from deleted code as docs, not executable claims:
  - event schema concepts if still wanted
  - any useful prompt intent or workflow assumptions
- Add explicit repo labels after the peel-back:
  - `active`: trusted code used right now
  - `quarantine`: retained but not trusted or supported
  - `data`: preserved truth/artifacts
  - `vendor`: external reference/runtime source
- Do not package surviving code yet.
  First reduce to a tiny trusted script set. Packaging and module architecture happen in the next rebuild phase.

## VLM Detector Rewrite Requirements
- Keep `vlm_detector.py` only as a documented labeling/detection tool, not as trusted runtime truth.
- Replace its current implicit contract with an explicit one:
  - primary use: corpus labeling, corpus adjudication, and offline analysis
  - current single-image prompt path is treated as insufficient and must be augmented
- Add backend support design for:
  - local OpenAI-compatible VLM endpoint as primary
  - optional remote adjudication/fan-out
  - optional two-model comparison for offline labeling
- For every surviving prompt template, create a dedicated markdown spec covering:
  - purpose
  - exact inputs passed
  - output contract
  - examples
  - known failure modes
  - when to use multi-image or extra context
- Explicitly review whether the detector should pass:
  - one image only
  - task context
  - neighboring frames
  - candidate labels or retrieved exemplars
  The default assumption for rebuild is that single-image-only classification is not enough for the long-term design.

## Peel-Back Workflow
- Phase 1: classify every non-vendored code file as `keep-active`, `quarantine`, or `delete`
- Phase 2: remove/quarantine code based on that manifest
- Phase 3: run targeted checks only on survivors and quarantine candidates that might be promoted later
- Phase 4: rewrite top-level docs so the repo no longer implies a runtime that does not exist
- Phase 5: begin a structured re-authoring interview/spec process for the rebuilt system

## Test Plan
- Do not run the full existing suite as a gate for the peel-back.
- Run targeted checks only for surviving code:
  - corpus labeling from ALAS logs to `index.jsonl`
  - screenshot dedupe on a sample corpus directory
  - black-frame cleanup detection in dry-run mode
  - VLM detector smoke checks against the configured local endpoint shape
- For `pilot_bridge.py`, if it remains quarantined, only run exploratory truth tests later to decide whether it is promotable or deletable.
- After deletions, remove or rewrite tests that only validate deleted/quarantined scaffolding.

## Re-Authoring Interview After Peel-Back
- Immediately after the reduction, run a new planning/spec pass focused on:
  - what the first real capability is
  - what truth sources exist
  - what the agent is actually instructed to do
  - what contracts are needed before new code is written
- That interview should produce:
  - one authoritative problem statement
  - one first deliverable
  - one minimal architecture
  - one explicit assignment contract
  - one list of trusted interfaces only

## Assumptions
- Deletion is the default unless a file preserves real, already-paid-for truth or is directly necessary for the screenshot-corpus-plus-ALAS-log workflow.
- `pilot_bridge.py` is not trusted enough to remain active, but may contain environment knowledge worth quarantining temporarily.
- The current graph/navigation line is not part of the active core during this reset.
- Surviving code remains script-shaped for now; package consolidation is deferred until after the repo is stripped to basics.
- The goal of this pass is not to rebuild functionality; it is to stop claiming functionality the repo has not earned.

## codex: PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:

PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:
# Documentation Realignment Plan: Keep Only `ALS` and `RES` as Domains

## Summary

Realign the docs tree so that only `ALS` and `RES` remain explicit domains. Retire `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` as domain labels in folder names, titles, and filenames. Reorganize the rest of the documentation into non-domain knowledge buckets that are useful to the agent: `project`, `architecture`, `workflows`, `prework`, `runtime`, `vlm`, `plans`, and `decisions`.

This is a **hybrid, medium-rewrite** pass:
- move existing docs into the new buckets
- merge or split docs where the old domain model hid the real topic
- rewrite outdated sections and contradictions
- keep prior `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` classification only as historical notes inside migrated docs, not in names or paths

## Implementation Changes

### 1. New target docs tree

```text
docs/
├─ ALS-reference/
├─ RES-research/
├─ architecture/
├─ project/
├─ workflows/
├─ prework/
├─ runtime/
├─ vlm/
├─ plans/
└─ decisions/
```

Rules:
- `ALS-reference/` and `RES-research/` are the only domain-shaped folders.
- Everything else is a knowledge bucket, not a domain.
- `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` disappear from folder names and filenames.
- Each migrated legacy doc gets a short “Historical note” near the top stating its previous location/classification.

### 2. Move existing docs into the new buckets

#### Keep as domains
- `docs/alas/*` -> `docs/ALS-reference/*`
- `docs/research/*` -> `docs/RES-research/*`

Keep `ALS-*` and `RES-*` naming in titles where it already fits.

#### Move project-level docs
- `docs/NORTH_STAR.md` -> `docs/project/north-star.md`
- `docs/REPO_STATUS.md` -> `docs/project/repo-status.md`
- `docs/testing-strategy.md` -> `docs/project/testing-strategy.md`

#### Move planning docs
- `docs/plans/MASTER_PLAN.md` -> `docs/plans/master-plan.md`
- `docs/plans/plan.md` -> `docs/plans/current-plan.md`
- `docs/rebuild/INTERVIEW.md` -> `docs/plans/rebuild-interview.md`

#### Move architecture docs
- `docs/architecture.md` -> `docs/architecture/architecture-overview.md`

Rewrite this doc so it explains:
- `ALS` and `RES` as knowledge domains
- `prework`, `runtime`, and `vlm` as non-domain implementation/knowledge buckets
- why docs and code are intentionally organized on different axes

#### Move and reshape workflow docs
- `docs/execution/EXE-workflows.md` -> `docs/workflows/azur-lane-workflows.md`

Rewrite to remove `EXE` framing and make it clearly about:
- assignment/workflow inventory
- entry conditions
- substate complexity
- success criteria
- escalation points

#### Move prework docs
- `docs/observation/OBS-corpus-cleanup.md` -> `docs/prework/corpus-cleanup.md`
- `docs/execution/EXE-data-collection.md` -> `docs/prework/data-collection.md`
- `docs/RES-research/RES-alas-build-plan.md` stays in `RES-research/` unless it is mostly operational build procedure; if so, split it into:
  - research rationale stays in `RES-research/`
  - executable collection/build procedure moves to `docs/prework/alas-build-plan.md`

#### Move runtime docs
- `docs/execution/EXE-backend-hardening.md` -> `docs/runtime/backend-hardening.md`
- `docs/execution/EXE-pilot-bridge-rework.md` -> `docs/runtime/pilot-bridge-rework.md`

Create or rewrite:
- `docs/runtime/runtime-overview.md`
- `docs/runtime/observation-contracts.md`

Then fold content from:
- `docs/observation/OBS-overview.md`
- `docs/navigation/NAV-overview.md`
- `docs/execution/EXE-overview.md`
- `docs/automation/AUT-overview.md`

into the runtime docs above instead of preserving those old overviews as separate legacy stubs.

#### Move and consolidate VLM docs
Create:
- `docs/vlm/VLM-overview.md`
- `docs/vlm/VLM-model-profiles.md`
- `docs/vlm/VLM-task-contracts.md`
- `docs/vlm/VLM-prompts.md`

Use these sources:
- move VLM capability material out of `OBS-overview.md`
- move prompt material out of `docs/prompts/vlm/*`
- use current research docs only as references, not as the primary operational spec

Then delete the split prompt-doc pattern in favor of one consolidated prompt doc with sections for:
- shared model behavior assumptions
- model configuration vs prompt wording
- classification tasks
- grounding/location tasks
- adjudication/comparison tasks

#### Keep decisions where they are
- `docs/decisions/*` stays in `docs/decisions/`

### 3. Rewrite rules for migrated docs

Apply these rules consistently:
- preserve useful existing structure such as status, current state, what exists, what is missing, and open questions
- remove old `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` codes from titles and filenames
- keep prior classification only as a short historical note in the body
- rewrite sections that claim a runtime exists where it does not
- rewrite sections that confuse prompt text with model configuration
- rewrite sections that bury VLM as a side detail instead of a first-class capability
- remove contradictions introduced by the failed peel-back rewrite and the older runtime-first language
- preserve direct, project-memory style rather than polishing docs into user-facing prose

### 4. Update agent-entry docs

Update:
- `AGENTS.md`
- `CLAUDE.md`

Requirements:
- point at the new docs tree
- treat docs as the agent knowledge layer, not human-facing product docs
- stop describing `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` as active domains
- explicitly tell the agent that `ALS` and `RES` remain the retained domains
- describe `prework`, `runtime`, and `vlm` as non-domain buckets

### 5. Remove old bucket structure after migration

After all moves and rewrites are complete, remove these legacy doc folders if empty:
- `docs/observation/`
- `docs/navigation/`
- `docs/execution/`
- `docs/automation/`
- `docs/rebuild/`
- `docs/prompts/`

## Test Plan

Run only non-destructive documentation checks:
- verify every moved doc path exists in the new tree
- verify no remaining doc filenames start with `OBS-`, `NAV-`, `EXE-`, or `AUT-`
- verify `ALS` and `RES` remain visible as the only domain-coded folders
- verify all internal links from `AGENTS.md`, `CLAUDE.md`, and moved docs point to valid new paths
- verify no references remain to removed legacy folder paths except inside intentional historical notes
- verify consolidated VLM docs cover:
  - model profiles
  - task contracts
  - prompt/config separation

## Assumptions and Defaults

- Keep only `ALS` and `RES` as explicit domains.
- Treat `prework`, `runtime`, `vlm`, `project`, `architecture`, and `workflows` as non-domain knowledge buckets.
- Retire `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` from names and paths entirely.
- Preserve prior `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` classification only inside the migrated doc body when useful for historical context.
- Prefer merging old overview docs into fewer, more accurate docs rather than preserving all legacy overview files one-for-one.
- `docs/decisions/` and `docs/plans/` stay as project categories rather than being domainized.

## codex: PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:

PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:
# Data-First Peel-Back Plan

## Summary
Reduce the repo to a small, trusted, data-first core before rebuilding architecture. Keep `vendor/` and all labeled corpus/data artifacts intact. Keep only code that directly preserves or improves the ALAS log + screenshot corpus workflow, plus a rewritten/documented VLM detector. Remove or quarantine everything else that currently overclaims runtime capability.

The peel-back is two stages:
1. Strip the repo to a minimal trusted core.
2. Immediately start a re-authoring interview/spec phase to define what the rebuilt system should actually do.

## Implementation Changes
- Preserve as source-of-truth assets:
  - `vendor/**`
  - labeled corpus and related data under `data/**`
  - existing prompt outputs, labeling artifacts, and ALAS logs/screenshots
- Keep as active code:
  - `scripts/label_raw_stream.py`
  - `scripts/screenshot_dedupe.py`
  - `scripts/delete_black_frames.py`
  - `scripts/vlm_detector.py`, but only after rewriting its contract and documenting every prompt in dedicated markdown specs
- Quarantine, not active:
  - `scripts/pilot_bridge.py`
  Reason: environment-specific capture/control spike with unverified assumptions about the emulator/render path
- Delete from active repo surface:
  - runtime façade and contract-forward code such as `executor.py`, `scheduler.py`, `task_model.py`, `resource_model.py`
  - graph/navigation family as active code: `pathfind.py`, `session.py`, `locate.py`, `observe.py`, `schema_validator.py`, `graph_utils.py`, `alas_converter.py`
  - anchor-calibration and mock/offline side-path code unless later re-earned
  - one-off experiment files and unused ALAS-adjacent analysis helpers not required by the corpus pipeline
- Preserve important semantics from deleted code as docs, not executable claims:
  - event schema concepts if still wanted
  - any useful prompt intent or workflow assumptions
- Add explicit repo labels after the peel-back:
  - `active`: trusted code used right now
  - `quarantine`: retained but not trusted or supported
  - `data`: preserved truth/artifacts
  - `vendor`: external reference/runtime source
- Do not package surviving code yet.
  First reduce to a tiny trusted script set. Packaging and module architecture happen in the next rebuild phase.

## VLM Detector Rewrite Requirements
- Keep `vlm_detector.py` only as a documented labeling/detection tool, not as trusted runtime truth.
- Replace its current implicit contract with an explicit one:
  - primary use: corpus labeling, corpus adjudication, and offline analysis
  - current single-image prompt path is treated as insufficient and must be augmented
- Add backend support design for:
  - local OpenAI-compatible VLM endpoint as primary
  - optional remote adjudication/fan-out
  - optional two-model comparison for offline labeling
- For every surviving prompt template, create a dedicated markdown spec covering:
  - purpose
  - exact inputs passed
  - output contract
  - examples
  - known failure modes
  - when to use multi-image or extra context
- Explicitly review whether the detector should pass:
  - one image only
  - task context
  - neighboring frames
  - candidate labels or retrieved exemplars
  The default assumption for rebuild is that single-image-only classification is not enough for the long-term design.

## Peel-Back Workflow
- Phase 1: classify every non-vendored code file as `keep-active`, `quarantine`, or `delete`
- Phase 2: remove/quarantine code based on that manifest
- Phase 3: run targeted checks only on survivors and quarantine candidates that might be promoted later
- Phase 4: rewrite top-level docs so the repo no longer implies a runtime that does not exist
- Phase 5: begin a structured re-authoring interview/spec process for the rebuilt system

## Test Plan
- Do not run the full existing suite as a gate for the peel-back.
- Run targeted checks only for surviving code:
  - corpus labeling from ALAS logs to `index.jsonl`
  - screenshot dedupe on a sample corpus directory
  - black-frame cleanup detection in dry-run mode
  - VLM detector smoke checks against the configured local endpoint shape
- For `pilot_bridge.py`, if it remains quarantined, only run exploratory truth tests later to decide whether it is promotable or deletable.
- After deletions, remove or rewrite tests that only validate deleted/quarantined scaffolding.

## Re-Authoring Interview After Peel-Back
- Immediately after the reduction, run a new planning/spec pass focused on:
  - what the first real capability is
  - what truth sources exist
  - what the agent is actually instructed to do
  - what contracts are needed before new code is written
- That interview should produce:
  - one authoritative problem statement
  - one first deliverable
  - one minimal architecture
  - one explicit assignment contract
  - one list of trusted interfaces only

## Assumptions
- Deletion is the default unless a file preserves real, already-paid-for truth or is directly necessary for the screenshot-corpus-plus-ALAS-log workflow.
- `pilot_bridge.py` is not trusted enough to remain active, but may contain environment knowledge worth quarantining temporarily.
- The current graph/navigation line is not part of the active core during this reset.
- Surviving code remains script-shaped for now; package consolidation is deferred until after the repo is stripped to basics.
- The goal of this pass is not to rebuild functionality; it is to stop claiming functionality the repo has not earned.

## codex: PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:

PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:
# Documentation Realignment Plan: Keep Only `ALS` and `RES` as Domains

## Summary

Realign the docs tree so that only `ALS` and `RES` remain explicit domains. Retire `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` as domain labels in folder names, titles, and filenames. Reorganize the rest of the documentation into non-domain knowledge buckets that are useful to the agent: `project`, `architecture`, `workflows`, `prework`, `runtime`, `vlm`, `plans`, and `decisions`.

This is a **hybrid, medium-rewrite** pass:
- move existing docs into the new buckets
- merge or split docs where the old domain model hid the real topic
- rewrite outdated sections and contradictions
- keep prior `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` classification only as historical notes inside migrated docs, not in names or paths

## Implementation Changes

### 1. New target docs tree

```text
docs/
├─ ALS-reference/
├─ RES-research/
├─ architecture/
├─ project/
├─ workflows/
├─ prework/
├─ runtime/
├─ vlm/
├─ plans/
└─ decisions/
```

Rules:
- `ALS-reference/` and `RES-research/` are the only domain-shaped folders.
- Everything else is a knowledge bucket, not a domain.
- `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` disappear from folder names and filenames.
- Each migrated legacy doc gets a short “Historical note” near the top stating its previous location/classification.

### 2. Move existing docs into the new buckets

#### Keep as domains
- `docs/alas/*` -> `docs/ALS-reference/*`
- `docs/research/*` -> `docs/RES-research/*`

Keep `ALS-*` and `RES-*` naming in titles where it already fits.

#### Move project-level docs
- `docs/NORTH_STAR.md` -> `docs/project/north-star.md`
- `docs/REPO_STATUS.md` -> `docs/project/repo-status.md`
- `docs/testing-strategy.md` -> `docs/project/testing-strategy.md`

#### Move planning docs
- `docs/plans/MASTER_PLAN.md` -> `docs/plans/master-plan.md`
- `docs/plans/plan.md` -> `docs/plans/current-plan.md`
- `docs/rebuild/INTERVIEW.md` -> `docs/plans/rebuild-interview.md`

#### Move architecture docs
- `docs/architecture.md` -> `docs/architecture/architecture-overview.md`

Rewrite this doc so it explains:
- `ALS` and `RES` as knowledge domains
- `prework`, `runtime`, and `vlm` as non-domain implementation/knowledge buckets
- why docs and code are intentionally organized on different axes

#### Move and reshape workflow docs
- `docs/execution/EXE-workflows.md` -> `docs/workflows/azur-lane-workflows.md`

Rewrite to remove `EXE` framing and make it clearly about:
- assignment/workflow inventory
- entry conditions
- substate complexity
- success criteria
- escalation points

#### Move prework docs
- `docs/observation/OBS-corpus-cleanup.md` -> `docs/prework/corpus-cleanup.md`
- `docs/execution/EXE-data-collection.md` -> `docs/prework/data-collection.md`
- `docs/RES-research/RES-alas-build-plan.md` stays in `RES-research/` unless it is mostly operational build procedure; if so, split it into:
  - research rationale stays in `RES-research/`
  - executable collection/build procedure moves to `docs/prework/alas-build-plan.md`

#### Move runtime docs
- `docs/execution/EXE-backend-hardening.md` -> `docs/runtime/backend-hardening.md`
- `docs/execution/EXE-pilot-bridge-rework.md` -> `docs/runtime/pilot-bridge-rework.md`

Create or rewrite:
- `docs/runtime/runtime-overview.md`
- `docs/runtime/observation-contracts.md`

Then fold content from:
- `docs/observation/OBS-overview.md`
- `docs/navigation/NAV-overview.md`
- `docs/execution/EXE-overview.md`
- `docs/automation/AUT-overview.md`

into the runtime docs above instead of preserving those old overviews as separate legacy stubs.

#### Move and consolidate VLM docs
Create:
- `docs/vlm/VLM-overview.md`
- `docs/vlm/VLM-model-profiles.md`
- `docs/vlm/VLM-task-contracts.md`
- `docs/vlm/VLM-prompts.md`

Use these sources:
- move VLM capability material out of `OBS-overview.md`
- move prompt material out of `docs/prompts/vlm/*`
- use current research docs only as references, not as the primary operational spec

Then delete the split prompt-doc pattern in favor of one consolidated prompt doc with sections for:
- shared model behavior assumptions
- model configuration vs prompt wording
- classification tasks
- grounding/location tasks
- adjudication/comparison tasks

#### Keep decisions where they are
- `docs/decisions/*` stays in `docs/decisions/`

### 3. Rewrite rules for migrated docs

Apply these rules consistently:
- preserve useful existing structure such as status, current state, what exists, what is missing, and open questions
- remove old `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` codes from titles and filenames
- keep prior classification only as a short historical note in the body
- rewrite sections that claim a runtime exists where it does not
- rewrite sections that confuse prompt text with model configuration
- rewrite sections that bury VLM as a side detail instead of a first-class capability
- remove contradictions introduced by the failed peel-back rewrite and the older runtime-first language
- preserve direct, project-memory style rather than polishing docs into user-facing prose

### 4. Update agent-entry docs

Update:
- `AGENTS.md`
- `CLAUDE.md`

Requirements:
- point at the new docs tree
- treat docs as the agent knowledge layer, not human-facing product docs
- stop describing `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` as active domains
- explicitly tell the agent that `ALS` and `RES` remain the retained domains
- describe `prework`, `runtime`, and `vlm` as non-domain buckets

### 5. Remove old bucket structure after migration

After all moves and rewrites are complete, remove these legacy doc folders if empty:
- `docs/observation/`
- `docs/navigation/`
- `docs/execution/`
- `docs/automation/`
- `docs/rebuild/`
- `docs/prompts/`

## Test Plan

Run only non-destructive documentation checks:
- verify every moved doc path exists in the new tree
- verify no remaining doc filenames start with `OBS-`, `NAV-`, `EXE-`, or `AUT-`
- verify `ALS` and `RES` remain visible as the only domain-coded folders
- verify all internal links from `AGENTS.md`, `CLAUDE.md`, and moved docs point to valid new paths
- verify no references remain to removed legacy folder paths except inside intentional historical notes
- verify consolidated VLM docs cover:
  - model profiles
  - task contracts
  - prompt/config separation

## Assumptions and Defaults

- Keep only `ALS` and `RES` as explicit domains.
- Treat `prework`, `runtime`, `vlm`, `project`, `architecture`, and `workflows` as non-domain knowledge buckets.
- Retire `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` from names and paths entirely.
- Preserve prior `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` classification only inside the migrated doc body when useful for historical context.
- Prefer merging old overview docs into fewer, more accurate docs rather than preserving all legacy overview files one-for-one.
- `docs/decisions/` and `docs/plans/` stay as project categories rather than being domainized.

## codex: PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:

PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:
# Data-First Peel-Back Plan

## Summary
Reduce the repo to a small, trusted, data-first core before rebuilding architecture. Keep `vendor/` and all labeled corpus/data artifacts intact. Keep only code that directly preserves or improves the ALAS log + screenshot corpus workflow, plus a rewritten/documented VLM detector. Remove or quarantine everything else that currently overclaims runtime capability.

The peel-back is two stages:
1. Strip the repo to a minimal trusted core.
2. Immediately start a re-authoring interview/spec phase to define what the rebuilt system should actually do.

## Implementation Changes
- Preserve as source-of-truth assets:
  - `vendor/**`
  - labeled corpus and related data under `data/**`
  - existing prompt outputs, labeling artifacts, and ALAS logs/screenshots
- Keep as active code:
  - `scripts/label_raw_stream.py`
  - `scripts/screenshot_dedupe.py`
  - `scripts/delete_black_frames.py`
  - `scripts/vlm_detector.py`, but only after rewriting its contract and documenting every prompt in dedicated markdown specs
- Quarantine, not active:
  - `scripts/pilot_bridge.py`
  Reason: environment-specific capture/control spike with unverified assumptions about the emulator/render path
- Delete from active repo surface:
  - runtime façade and contract-forward code such as `executor.py`, `scheduler.py`, `task_model.py`, `resource_model.py`
  - graph/navigation family as active code: `pathfind.py`, `session.py`, `locate.py`, `observe.py`, `schema_validator.py`, `graph_utils.py`, `alas_converter.py`
  - anchor-calibration and mock/offline side-path code unless later re-earned
  - one-off experiment files and unused ALAS-adjacent analysis helpers not required by the corpus pipeline
- Preserve important semantics from deleted code as docs, not executable claims:
  - event schema concepts if still wanted
  - any useful prompt intent or workflow assumptions
- Add explicit repo labels after the peel-back:
  - `active`: trusted code used right now
  - `quarantine`: retained but not trusted or supported
  - `data`: preserved truth/artifacts
  - `vendor`: external reference/runtime source
- Do not package surviving code yet.
  First reduce to a tiny trusted script set. Packaging and module architecture happen in the next rebuild phase.

## VLM Detector Rewrite Requirements
- Keep `vlm_detector.py` only as a documented labeling/detection tool, not as trusted runtime truth.
- Replace its current implicit contract with an explicit one:
  - primary use: corpus labeling, corpus adjudication, and offline analysis
  - current single-image prompt path is treated as insufficient and must be augmented
- Add backend support design for:
  - local OpenAI-compatible VLM endpoint as primary
  - optional remote adjudication/fan-out
  - optional two-model comparison for offline labeling
- For every surviving prompt template, create a dedicated markdown spec covering:
  - purpose
  - exact inputs passed
  - output contract
  - examples
  - known failure modes
  - when to use multi-image or extra context
- Explicitly review whether the detector should pass:
  - one image only
  - task context
  - neighboring frames
  - candidate labels or retrieved exemplars
  The default assumption for rebuild is that single-image-only classification is not enough for the long-term design.

## Peel-Back Workflow
- Phase 1: classify every non-vendored code file as `keep-active`, `quarantine`, or `delete`
- Phase 2: remove/quarantine code based on that manifest
- Phase 3: run targeted checks only on survivors and quarantine candidates that might be promoted later
- Phase 4: rewrite top-level docs so the repo no longer implies a runtime that does not exist
- Phase 5: begin a structured re-authoring interview/spec process for the rebuilt system

## Test Plan
- Do not run the full existing suite as a gate for the peel-back.
- Run targeted checks only for surviving code:
  - corpus labeling from ALAS logs to `index.jsonl`
  - screenshot dedupe on a sample corpus directory
  - black-frame cleanup detection in dry-run mode
  - VLM detector smoke checks against the configured local endpoint shape
- For `pilot_bridge.py`, if it remains quarantined, only run exploratory truth tests later to decide whether it is promotable or deletable.
- After deletions, remove or rewrite tests that only validate deleted/quarantined scaffolding.

## Re-Authoring Interview After Peel-Back
- Immediately after the reduction, run a new planning/spec pass focused on:
  - what the first real capability is
  - what truth sources exist
  - what the agent is actually instructed to do
  - what contracts are needed before new code is written
- That interview should produce:
  - one authoritative problem statement
  - one first deliverable
  - one minimal architecture
  - one explicit assignment contract
  - one list of trusted interfaces only

## Assumptions
- Deletion is the default unless a file preserves real, already-paid-for truth or is directly necessary for the screenshot-corpus-plus-ALAS-log workflow.
- `pilot_bridge.py` is not trusted enough to remain active, but may contain environment knowledge worth quarantining temporarily.
- The current graph/navigation line is not part of the active core during this reset.
- Surviving code remains script-shaped for now; package consolidation is deferred until after the repo is stripped to basics.
- The goal of this pass is not to rebuild functionality; it is to stop claiming functionality the repo has not earned.

## codex: PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:

PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:
# Documentation Realignment Plan: Keep Only `ALS` and `RES` as Domains

## Summary

Realign the docs tree so that only `ALS` and `RES` remain explicit domains. Retire `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` as domain labels in folder names, titles, and filenames. Reorganize the rest of the documentation into non-domain knowledge buckets that are useful to the agent: `project`, `architecture`, `workflows`, `prework`, `runtime`, `vlm`, `plans`, and `decisions`.

This is a **hybrid, medium-rewrite** pass:
- move existing docs into the new buckets
- merge or split docs where the old domain model hid the real topic
- rewrite outdated sections and contradictions
- keep prior `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` classification only as historical notes inside migrated docs, not in names or paths

## Implementation Changes

### 1. New target docs tree

```text
docs/
├─ ALS-reference/
├─ RES-research/
├─ architecture/
├─ project/
├─ workflows/
├─ prework/
├─ runtime/
├─ vlm/
├─ plans/
└─ decisions/
```

Rules:
- `ALS-reference/` and `RES-research/` are the only domain-shaped folders.
- Everything else is a knowledge bucket, not a domain.
- `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` disappear from folder names and filenames.
- Each migrated legacy doc gets a short “Historical note” near the top stating its previous location/classification.

### 2. Move existing docs into the new buckets

#### Keep as domains
- `docs/alas/*` -> `docs/ALS-reference/*`
- `docs/research/*` -> `docs/RES-research/*`

Keep `ALS-*` and `RES-*` naming in titles where it already fits.

#### Move project-level docs
- `docs/NORTH_STAR.md` -> `docs/project/north-star.md`
- `docs/REPO_STATUS.md` -> `docs/project/repo-status.md`
- `docs/testing-strategy.md` -> `docs/project/testing-strategy.md`

#### Move planning docs
- `docs/plans/MASTER_PLAN.md` -> `docs/plans/master-plan.md`
- `docs/plans/plan.md` -> `docs/plans/current-plan.md`
- `docs/rebuild/INTERVIEW.md` -> `docs/plans/rebuild-interview.md`

#### Move architecture docs
- `docs/architecture.md` -> `docs/architecture/architecture-overview.md`

Rewrite this doc so it explains:
- `ALS` and `RES` as knowledge domains
- `prework`, `runtime`, and `vlm` as non-domain implementation/knowledge buckets
- why docs and code are intentionally organized on different axes

#### Move and reshape workflow docs
- `docs/execution/EXE-workflows.md` -> `docs/workflows/azur-lane-workflows.md`

Rewrite to remove `EXE` framing and make it clearly about:
- assignment/workflow inventory
- entry conditions
- substate complexity
- success criteria
- escalation points

#### Move prework docs
- `docs/observation/OBS-corpus-cleanup.md` -> `docs/prework/corpus-cleanup.md`
- `docs/execution/EXE-data-collection.md` -> `docs/prework/data-collection.md`
- `docs/RES-research/RES-alas-build-plan.md` stays in `RES-research/` unless it is mostly operational build procedure; if so, split it into:
  - research rationale stays in `RES-research/`
  - executable collection/build procedure moves to `docs/prework/alas-build-plan.md`

#### Move runtime docs
- `docs/execution/EXE-backend-hardening.md` -> `docs/runtime/backend-hardening.md`
- `docs/execution/EXE-pilot-bridge-rework.md` -> `docs/runtime/pilot-bridge-rework.md`

Create or rewrite:
- `docs/runtime/runtime-overview.md`
- `docs/runtime/observation-contracts.md`

Then fold content from:
- `docs/observation/OBS-overview.md`
- `docs/navigation/NAV-overview.md`
- `docs/execution/EXE-overview.md`
- `docs/automation/AUT-overview.md`

into the runtime docs above instead of preserving those old overviews as separate legacy stubs.

#### Move and consolidate VLM docs
Create:
- `docs/vlm/VLM-overview.md`
- `docs/vlm/VLM-model-profiles.md`
- `docs/vlm/VLM-task-contracts.md`
- `docs/vlm/VLM-prompts.md`

Use these sources:
- move VLM capability material out of `OBS-overview.md`
- move prompt material out of `docs/prompts/vlm/*`
- use current research docs only as references, not as the primary operational spec

Then delete the split prompt-doc pattern in favor of one consolidated prompt doc with sections for:
- shared model behavior assumptions
- model configuration vs prompt wording
- classification tasks
- grounding/location tasks
- adjudication/comparison tasks

#### Keep decisions where they are
- `docs/decisions/*` stays in `docs/decisions/`

### 3. Rewrite rules for migrated docs

Apply these rules consistently:
- preserve useful existing structure such as status, current state, what exists, what is missing, and open questions
- remove old `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` codes from titles and filenames
- keep prior classification only as a short historical note in the body
- rewrite sections that claim a runtime exists where it does not
- rewrite sections that confuse prompt text with model configuration
- rewrite sections that bury VLM as a side detail instead of a first-class capability
- remove contradictions introduced by the failed peel-back rewrite and the older runtime-first language
- preserve direct, project-memory style rather than polishing docs into user-facing prose

### 4. Update agent-entry docs

Update:
- `AGENTS.md`
- `CLAUDE.md`

Requirements:
- point at the new docs tree
- treat docs as the agent knowledge layer, not human-facing product docs
- stop describing `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` as active domains
- explicitly tell the agent that `ALS` and `RES` remain the retained domains
- describe `prework`, `runtime`, and `vlm` as non-domain buckets

### 5. Remove old bucket structure after migration

After all moves and rewrites are complete, remove these legacy doc folders if empty:
- `docs/observation/`
- `docs/navigation/`
- `docs/execution/`
- `docs/automation/`
- `docs/rebuild/`
- `docs/prompts/`

## Test Plan

Run only non-destructive documentation checks:
- verify every moved doc path exists in the new tree
- verify no remaining doc filenames start with `OBS-`, `NAV-`, `EXE-`, or `AUT-`
- verify `ALS` and `RES` remain visible as the only domain-coded folders
- verify all internal links from `AGENTS.md`, `CLAUDE.md`, and moved docs point to valid new paths
- verify no references remain to removed legacy folder paths except inside intentional historical notes
- verify consolidated VLM docs cover:
  - model profiles
  - task contracts
  - prompt/config separation

## Assumptions and Defaults

- Keep only `ALS` and `RES` as explicit domains.
- Treat `prework`, `runtime`, `vlm`, `project`, `architecture`, and `workflows` as non-domain knowledge buckets.
- Retire `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` from names and paths entirely.
- Preserve prior `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` classification only inside the migrated doc body when useful for historical context.
- Prefer merging old overview docs into fewer, more accurate docs rather than preserving all legacy overview files one-for-one.
- `docs/decisions/` and `docs/plans/` stay as project categories rather than being domainized.

## codex: PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:

PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:
# Data-First Peel-Back Plan

## Summary
Reduce the repo to a small, trusted, data-first core before rebuilding architecture. Keep `vendor/` and all labeled corpus/data artifacts intact. Keep only code that directly preserves or improves the ALAS log + screenshot corpus workflow, plus a rewritten/documented VLM detector. Remove or quarantine everything else that currently overclaims runtime capability.

The peel-back is two stages:
1. Strip the repo to a minimal trusted core.
2. Immediately start a re-authoring interview/spec phase to define what the rebuilt system should actually do.

## Implementation Changes
- Preserve as source-of-truth assets:
  - `vendor/**`
  - labeled corpus and related data under `data/**`
  - existing prompt outputs, labeling artifacts, and ALAS logs/screenshots
- Keep as active code:
  - `scripts/label_raw_stream.py`
  - `scripts/screenshot_dedupe.py`
  - `scripts/delete_black_frames.py`
  - `scripts/vlm_detector.py`, but only after rewriting its contract and documenting every prompt in dedicated markdown specs
- Quarantine, not active:
  - `scripts/pilot_bridge.py`
  Reason: environment-specific capture/control spike with unverified assumptions about the emulator/render path
- Delete from active repo surface:
  - runtime façade and contract-forward code such as `executor.py`, `scheduler.py`, `task_model.py`, `resource_model.py`
  - graph/navigation family as active code: `pathfind.py`, `session.py`, `locate.py`, `observe.py`, `schema_validator.py`, `graph_utils.py`, `alas_converter.py`
  - anchor-calibration and mock/offline side-path code unless later re-earned
  - one-off experiment files and unused ALAS-adjacent analysis helpers not required by the corpus pipeline
- Preserve important semantics from deleted code as docs, not executable claims:
  - event schema concepts if still wanted
  - any useful prompt intent or workflow assumptions
- Add explicit repo labels after the peel-back:
  - `active`: trusted code used right now
  - `quarantine`: retained but not trusted or supported
  - `data`: preserved truth/artifacts
  - `vendor`: external reference/runtime source
- Do not package surviving code yet.
  First reduce to a tiny trusted script set. Packaging and module architecture happen in the next rebuild phase.

## VLM Detector Rewrite Requirements
- Keep `vlm_detector.py` only as a documented labeling/detection tool, not as trusted runtime truth.
- Replace its current implicit contract with an explicit one:
  - primary use: corpus labeling, corpus adjudication, and offline analysis
  - current single-image prompt path is treated as insufficient and must be augmented
- Add backend support design for:
  - local OpenAI-compatible VLM endpoint as primary
  - optional remote adjudication/fan-out
  - optional two-model comparison for offline labeling
- For every surviving prompt template, create a dedicated markdown spec covering:
  - purpose
  - exact inputs passed
  - output contract
  - examples
  - known failure modes
  - when to use multi-image or extra context
- Explicitly review whether the detector should pass:
  - one image only
  - task context
  - neighboring frames
  - candidate labels or retrieved exemplars
  The default assumption for rebuild is that single-image-only classification is not enough for the long-term design.

## Peel-Back Workflow
- Phase 1: classify every non-vendored code file as `keep-active`, `quarantine`, or `delete`
- Phase 2: remove/quarantine code based on that manifest
- Phase 3: run targeted checks only on survivors and quarantine candidates that might be promoted later
- Phase 4: rewrite top-level docs so the repo no longer implies a runtime that does not exist
- Phase 5: begin a structured re-authoring interview/spec process for the rebuilt system

## Test Plan
- Do not run the full existing suite as a gate for the peel-back.
- Run targeted checks only for surviving code:
  - corpus labeling from ALAS logs to `index.jsonl`
  - screenshot dedupe on a sample corpus directory
  - black-frame cleanup detection in dry-run mode
  - VLM detector smoke checks against the configured local endpoint shape
- For `pilot_bridge.py`, if it remains quarantined, only run exploratory truth tests later to decide whether it is promotable or deletable.
- After deletions, remove or rewrite tests that only validate deleted/quarantined scaffolding.

## Re-Authoring Interview After Peel-Back
- Immediately after the reduction, run a new planning/spec pass focused on:
  - what the first real capability is
  - what truth sources exist
  - what the agent is actually instructed to do
  - what contracts are needed before new code is written
- That interview should produce:
  - one authoritative problem statement
  - one first deliverable
  - one minimal architecture
  - one explicit assignment contract
  - one list of trusted interfaces only

## Assumptions
- Deletion is the default unless a file preserves real, already-paid-for truth or is directly necessary for the screenshot-corpus-plus-ALAS-log workflow.
- `pilot_bridge.py` is not trusted enough to remain active, but may contain environment knowledge worth quarantining temporarily.
- The current graph/navigation line is not part of the active core during this reset.
- Surviving code remains script-shaped for now; package consolidation is deferred until after the repo is stripped to basics.
- The goal of this pass is not to rebuild functionality; it is to stop claiming functionality the repo has not earned.
