## codex: PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:

PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:
# Documentation Realignment Plan: Keep Only `ALS` and `RES` as Domains

## Summary

Realign the docs tree so that only `ALS` and `RES` remain explicit domains. Retire `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` as domain labels in folder names, titles, and filenames. Reorganize the rest of the documentation into non-domain knowledge buckets that are useful to the agent: `project`, `architecture`, `workflows`, `prework`, `runtime`, `vlm`, `plans`, and `decisions`.

This is a **hybrid, medium-rewrite** pass:
- move existing docs into the new buckets
- merge or split docs where the old domain model hid the real topic
- rewrite outdated sections and contradictions
- keep prior `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` classification only as historical notes inside migrated docs, not in names or paths

## Implementation Changes

### 1. New target docs tree

```text
docs/
├─ ALS-reference/
├─ RES-research/
├─ architecture/
├─ project/
├─ workflows/
├─ prework/
├─ runtime/
├─ vlm/
├─ plans/
└─ decisions/
```

Rules:
- `ALS-reference/` and `RES-research/` are the only domain-shaped folders.
- Everything else is a knowledge bucket, not a domain.
- `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` disappear from folder names and filenames.
- Each migrated legacy doc gets a short “Historical note” near the top stating its previous location/classification.

### 2. Move existing docs into the new buckets

#### Keep as domains
- `docs/alas/*` -> `docs/ALS-reference/*`
- `docs/research/*` -> `docs/RES-research/*`

Keep `ALS-*` and `RES-*` naming in titles where it already fits.

#### Move project-level docs
- `docs/NORTH_STAR.md` -> `docs/project/north-star.md`
- `docs/REPO_STATUS.md` -> `docs/project/repo-status.md`
- `docs/testing-strategy.md` -> `docs/project/testing-strategy.md`

#### Move planning docs
- `docs/plans/MASTER_PLAN.md` -> `docs/plans/master-plan.md`
- `docs/plans/plan.md` -> `docs/plans/current-plan.md`
- `docs/rebuild/INTERVIEW.md` -> `docs/plans/rebuild-interview.md`

#### Move architecture docs
- `docs/architecture.md` -> `docs/architecture/architecture-overview.md`

Rewrite this doc so it explains:
- `ALS` and `RES` as knowledge domains
- `prework`, `runtime`, and `vlm` as non-domain implementation/knowledge buckets
- why docs and code are intentionally organized on different axes

#### Move and reshape workflow docs
- `docs/execution/EXE-workflows.md` -> `docs/workflows/azur-lane-workflows.md`

Rewrite to remove `EXE` framing and make it clearly about:
- assignment/workflow inventory
- entry conditions
- substate complexity
- success criteria
- escalation points

#### Move prework docs
- `docs/observation/OBS-corpus-cleanup.md` -> `docs/prework/corpus-cleanup.md`
- `docs/execution/EXE-data-collection.md` -> `docs/prework/data-collection.md`
- `docs/RES-research/RES-alas-build-plan.md` stays in `RES-research/` unless it is mostly operational build procedure; if so, split it into:
  - research rationale stays in `RES-research/`
  - executable collection/build procedure moves to `docs/prework/alas-build-plan.md`

#### Move runtime docs
- `docs/execution/EXE-backend-hardening.md` -> `docs/runtime/backend-hardening.md`
- `docs/execution/EXE-pilot-bridge-rework.md` -> `docs/runtime/pilot-bridge-rework.md`

Create or rewrite:
- `docs/runtime/runtime-overview.md`
- `docs/runtime/observation-contracts.md`

Then fold content from:
- `docs/observation/OBS-overview.md`
- `docs/navigation/NAV-overview.md`
- `docs/execution/EXE-overview.md`
- `docs/automation/AUT-overview.md`

into the runtime docs above instead of preserving those old overviews as separate legacy stubs.

#### Move and consolidate VLM docs
Create:
- `docs/vlm/VLM-overview.md`
- `docs/vlm/VLM-model-profiles.md`
- `docs/vlm/VLM-task-contracts.md`
- `docs/vlm/VLM-prompts.md`

Use these sources:
- move VLM capability material out of `OBS-overview.md`
- move prompt material out of `docs/prompts/vlm/*`
- use current research docs only as references, not as the primary operational spec

Then delete the split prompt-doc pattern in favor of one consolidated prompt doc with sections for:
- shared model behavior assumptions
- model configuration vs prompt wording
- classification tasks
- grounding/location tasks
- adjudication/comparison tasks

#### Keep decisions where they are
- `docs/decisions/*` stays in `docs/decisions/`

### 3. Rewrite rules for migrated docs

Apply these rules consistently:
- preserve useful existing structure such as status, current state, what exists, what is missing, and open questions
- remove old `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` codes from titles and filenames
- keep prior classification only as a short historical note in the body
- rewrite sections that claim a runtime exists where it does not
- rewrite sections that confuse prompt text with model configuration
- rewrite sections that bury VLM as a side detail instead of a first-class capability
- remove contradictions introduced by the failed peel-back rewrite and the older runtime-first language
- preserve direct, project-memory style rather than polishing docs into user-facing prose

### 4. Update agent-entry docs

Update:
- `AGENTS.md`
- `CLAUDE.md`

Requirements:
- point at the new docs tree
- treat docs as the agent knowledge layer, not human-facing product docs
- stop describing `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` as active domains
- explicitly tell the agent that `ALS` and `RES` remain the retained domains
- describe `prework`, `runtime`, and `vlm` as non-domain buckets

### 5. Remove old bucket structure after migration

After all moves and rewrites are complete, remove these legacy doc folders if empty:
- `docs/observation/`
- `docs/navigation/`
- `docs/execution/`
- `docs/automation/`
- `docs/rebuild/`
- `docs/prompts/`

## Test Plan

Run only non-destructive documentation checks:
- verify every moved doc path exists in the new tree
- verify no remaining doc filenames start with `OBS-`, `NAV-`, `EXE-`, or `AUT-`
- verify `ALS` and `RES` remain visible as the only domain-coded folders
- verify all internal links from `AGENTS.md`, `CLAUDE.md`, and moved docs point to valid new paths
- verify no references remain to removed legacy folder paths except inside intentional historical notes
- verify consolidated VLM docs cover:
  - model profiles
  - task contracts
  - prompt/config separation

## Assumptions and Defaults

- Keep only `ALS` and `RES` as explicit domains.
- Treat `prework`, `runtime`, `vlm`, `project`, `architecture`, and `workflows` as non-domain knowledge buckets.
- Retire `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` from names and paths entirely.
- Preserve prior `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` classification only inside the migrated doc body when useful for historical context.
- Prefer merging old overview docs into fewer, more accurate docs rather than preserving all legacy overview files one-for-one.
- `docs/decisions/` and `docs/plans/` stay as project categories rather than being domainized.

## codex: PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:

PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:
# Data-First Peel-Back Plan

## Summary
Reduce the repo to a small, trusted, data-first core before rebuilding architecture. Keep `vendor/` and all labeled corpus/data artifacts intact. Keep only code that directly preserves or improves the ALAS log + screenshot corpus workflow, plus a rewritten/documented VLM detector. Remove or quarantine everything else that currently overclaims runtime capability.

The peel-back is two stages:
1. Strip the repo to a minimal trusted core.
2. Immediately start a re-authoring interview/spec phase to define what the rebuilt system should actually do.

## Implementation Changes
- Preserve as source-of-truth assets:
  - `vendor/**`
  - labeled corpus and related data under `data/**`
  - existing prompt outputs, labeling artifacts, and ALAS logs/screenshots
- Keep as active code:
  - `scripts/label_raw_stream.py`
  - `scripts/screenshot_dedupe.py`
  - `scripts/delete_black_frames.py`
  - `scripts/vlm_detector.py`, but only after rewriting its contract and documenting every prompt in dedicated markdown specs
- Quarantine, not active:
  - `scripts/pilot_bridge.py`
  Reason: environment-specific capture/control spike with unverified assumptions about the emulator/render path
- Delete from active repo surface:
  - runtime façade and contract-forward code such as `executor.py`, `scheduler.py`, `task_model.py`, `resource_model.py`
  - graph/navigation family as active code: `pathfind.py`, `session.py`, `locate.py`, `observe.py`, `schema_validator.py`, `graph_utils.py`, `alas_converter.py`
  - anchor-calibration and mock/offline side-path code unless later re-earned
  - one-off experiment files and unused ALAS-adjacent analysis helpers not required by the corpus pipeline
- Preserve important semantics from deleted code as docs, not executable claims:
  - event schema concepts if still wanted
  - any useful prompt intent or workflow assumptions
- Add explicit repo labels after the peel-back:
  - `active`: trusted code used right now
  - `quarantine`: retained but not trusted or supported
  - `data`: preserved truth/artifacts
  - `vendor`: external reference/runtime source
- Do not package surviving code yet.
  First reduce to a tiny trusted script set. Packaging and module architecture happen in the next rebuild phase.

## VLM Detector Rewrite Requirements
- Keep `vlm_detector.py` only as a documented labeling/detection tool, not as trusted runtime truth.
- Replace its current implicit contract with an explicit one:
  - primary use: corpus labeling, corpus adjudication, and offline analysis
  - current single-image prompt path is treated as insufficient and must be augmented
- Add backend support design for:
  - local OpenAI-compatible VLM endpoint as primary
  - optional remote adjudication/fan-out
  - optional two-model comparison for offline labeling
- For every surviving prompt template, create a dedicated markdown spec covering:
  - purpose
  - exact inputs passed
  - output contract
  - examples
  - known failure modes
  - when to use multi-image or extra context
- Explicitly review whether the detector should pass:
  - one image only
  - task context
  - neighboring frames
  - candidate labels or retrieved exemplars
  The default assumption for rebuild is that single-image-only classification is not enough for the long-term design.

## Peel-Back Workflow
- Phase 1: classify every non-vendored code file as `keep-active`, `quarantine`, or `delete`
- Phase 2: remove/quarantine code based on that manifest
- Phase 3: run targeted checks only on survivors and quarantine candidates that might be promoted later
- Phase 4: rewrite top-level docs so the repo no longer implies a runtime that does not exist
- Phase 5: begin a structured re-authoring interview/spec process for the rebuilt system

## Test Plan
- Do not run the full existing suite as a gate for the peel-back.
- Run targeted checks only for surviving code:
  - corpus labeling from ALAS logs to `index.jsonl`
  - screenshot dedupe on a sample corpus directory
  - black-frame cleanup detection in dry-run mode
  - VLM detector smoke checks against the configured local endpoint shape
- For `pilot_bridge.py`, if it remains quarantined, only run exploratory truth tests later to decide whether it is promotable or deletable.
- After deletions, remove or rewrite tests that only validate deleted/quarantined scaffolding.

## Re-Authoring Interview After Peel-Back
- Immediately after the reduction, run a new planning/spec pass focused on:
  - what the first real capability is
  - what truth sources exist
  - what the agent is actually instructed to do
  - what contracts are needed before new code is written
- That interview should produce:
  - one authoritative problem statement
  - one first deliverable
  - one minimal architecture
  - one explicit assignment contract
  - one list of trusted interfaces only

## Assumptions
- Deletion is the default unless a file preserves real, already-paid-for truth or is directly necessary for the screenshot-corpus-plus-ALAS-log workflow.
- `pilot_bridge.py` is not trusted enough to remain active, but may contain environment knowledge worth quarantining temporarily.
- The current graph/navigation line is not part of the active core during this reset.
- Surviving code remains script-shaped for now; package consolidation is deferred until after the repo is stripped to basics.
- The goal of this pass is not to rebuild functionality; it is to stop claiming functionality the repo has not earned.

## codex: PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:

PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:
# Documentation Realignment Plan: Keep Only `ALS` and `RES` as Domains

## Summary

Realign the docs tree so that only `ALS` and `RES` remain explicit domains. Retire `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` as domain labels in folder names, titles, and filenames. Reorganize the rest of the documentation into non-domain knowledge buckets that are useful to the agent: `project`, `architecture`, `workflows`, `prework`, `runtime`, `vlm`, `plans`, and `decisions`.

This is a **hybrid, medium-rewrite** pass:
- move existing docs into the new buckets
- merge or split docs where the old domain model hid the real topic
- rewrite outdated sections and contradictions
- keep prior `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` classification only as historical notes inside migrated docs, not in names or paths

## Implementation Changes

### 1. New target docs tree

```text
docs/
├─ ALS-reference/
├─ RES-research/
├─ architecture/
├─ project/
├─ workflows/
├─ prework/
├─ runtime/
├─ vlm/
├─ plans/
└─ decisions/
```

Rules:
- `ALS-reference/` and `RES-research/` are the only domain-shaped folders.
- Everything else is a knowledge bucket, not a domain.
- `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` disappear from folder names and filenames.
- Each migrated legacy doc gets a short “Historical note” near the top stating its previous location/classification.

### 2. Move existing docs into the new buckets

#### Keep as domains
- `docs/alas/*` -> `docs/ALS-reference/*`
- `docs/research/*` -> `docs/RES-research/*`

Keep `ALS-*` and `RES-*` naming in titles where it already fits.

#### Move project-level docs
- `docs/NORTH_STAR.md` -> `docs/project/north-star.md`
- `docs/REPO_STATUS.md` -> `docs/project/repo-status.md`
- `docs/testing-strategy.md` -> `docs/project/testing-strategy.md`

#### Move planning docs
- `docs/plans/MASTER_PLAN.md` -> `docs/plans/master-plan.md`
- `docs/plans/plan.md` -> `docs/plans/current-plan.md`
- `docs/rebuild/INTERVIEW.md` -> `docs/plans/rebuild-interview.md`

#### Move architecture docs
- `docs/architecture.md` -> `docs/architecture/architecture-overview.md`

Rewrite this doc so it explains:
- `ALS` and `RES` as knowledge domains
- `prework`, `runtime`, and `vlm` as non-domain implementation/knowledge buckets
- why docs and code are intentionally organized on different axes

#### Move and reshape workflow docs
- `docs/execution/EXE-workflows.md` -> `docs/workflows/azur-lane-workflows.md`

Rewrite to remove `EXE` framing and make it clearly about:
- assignment/workflow inventory
- entry conditions
- substate complexity
- success criteria
- escalation points

#### Move prework docs
- `docs/observation/OBS-corpus-cleanup.md` -> `docs/prework/corpus-cleanup.md`
- `docs/execution/EXE-data-collection.md` -> `docs/prework/data-collection.md`
- `docs/RES-research/RES-alas-build-plan.md` stays in `RES-research/` unless it is mostly operational build procedure; if so, split it into:
  - research rationale stays in `RES-research/`
  - executable collection/build procedure moves to `docs/prework/alas-build-plan.md`

#### Move runtime docs
- `docs/execution/EXE-backend-hardening.md` -> `docs/runtime/backend-hardening.md`
- `docs/execution/EXE-pilot-bridge-rework.md` -> `docs/runtime/pilot-bridge-rework.md`

Create or rewrite:
- `docs/runtime/runtime-overview.md`
- `docs/runtime/observation-contracts.md`

Then fold content from:
- `docs/observation/OBS-overview.md`
- `docs/navigation/NAV-overview.md`
- `docs/execution/EXE-overview.md`
- `docs/automation/AUT-overview.md`

into the runtime docs above instead of preserving those old overviews as separate legacy stubs.

#### Move and consolidate VLM docs
Create:
- `docs/vlm/VLM-overview.md`
- `docs/vlm/VLM-model-profiles.md`
- `docs/vlm/VLM-task-contracts.md`
- `docs/vlm/VLM-prompts.md`

Use these sources:
- move VLM capability material out of `OBS-overview.md`
- move prompt material out of `docs/prompts/vlm/*`
- use current research docs only as references, not as the primary operational spec

Then delete the split prompt-doc pattern in favor of one consolidated prompt doc with sections for:
- shared model behavior assumptions
- model configuration vs prompt wording
- classification tasks
- grounding/location tasks
- adjudication/comparison tasks

#### Keep decisions where they are
- `docs/decisions/*` stays in `docs/decisions/`

### 3. Rewrite rules for migrated docs

Apply these rules consistently:
- preserve useful existing structure such as status, current state, what exists, what is missing, and open questions
- remove old `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` codes from titles and filenames
- keep prior classification only as a short historical note in the body
- rewrite sections that claim a runtime exists where it does not
- rewrite sections that confuse prompt text with model configuration
- rewrite sections that bury VLM as a side detail instead of a first-class capability
- remove contradictions introduced by the failed peel-back rewrite and the older runtime-first language
- preserve direct, project-memory style rather than polishing docs into user-facing prose

### 4. Update agent-entry docs

Update:
- `AGENTS.md`
- `CLAUDE.md`

Requirements:
- point at the new docs tree
- treat docs as the agent knowledge layer, not human-facing product docs
- stop describing `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` as active domains
- explicitly tell the agent that `ALS` and `RES` remain the retained domains
- describe `prework`, `runtime`, and `vlm` as non-domain buckets

### 5. Remove old bucket structure after migration

After all moves and rewrites are complete, remove these legacy doc folders if empty:
- `docs/observation/`
- `docs/navigation/`
- `docs/execution/`
- `docs/automation/`
- `docs/rebuild/`
- `docs/prompts/`

## Test Plan

Run only non-destructive documentation checks:
- verify every moved doc path exists in the new tree
- verify no remaining doc filenames start with `OBS-`, `NAV-`, `EXE-`, or `AUT-`
- verify `ALS` and `RES` remain visible as the only domain-coded folders
- verify all internal links from `AGENTS.md`, `CLAUDE.md`, and moved docs point to valid new paths
- verify no references remain to removed legacy folder paths except inside intentional historical notes
- verify consolidated VLM docs cover:
  - model profiles
  - task contracts
  - prompt/config separation

## Assumptions and Defaults

- Keep only `ALS` and `RES` as explicit domains.
- Treat `prework`, `runtime`, `vlm`, `project`, `architecture`, and `workflows` as non-domain knowledge buckets.
- Retire `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` from names and paths entirely.
- Preserve prior `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` classification only inside the migrated doc body when useful for historical context.
- Prefer merging old overview docs into fewer, more accurate docs rather than preserving all legacy overview files one-for-one.
- `docs/decisions/` and `docs/plans/` stay as project categories rather than being domainized.

## codex: PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:

PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:
# Data-First Peel-Back Plan

## Summary
Reduce the repo to a small, trusted, data-first core before rebuilding architecture. Keep `vendor/` and all labeled corpus/data artifacts intact. Keep only code that directly preserves or improves the ALAS log + screenshot corpus workflow, plus a rewritten/documented VLM detector. Remove or quarantine everything else that currently overclaims runtime capability.

The peel-back is two stages:
1. Strip the repo to a minimal trusted core.
2. Immediately start a re-authoring interview/spec phase to define what the rebuilt system should actually do.

## Implementation Changes
- Preserve as source-of-truth assets:
  - `vendor/**`
  - labeled corpus and related data under `data/**`
  - existing prompt outputs, labeling artifacts, and ALAS logs/screenshots
- Keep as active code:
  - `scripts/label_raw_stream.py`
  - `scripts/screenshot_dedupe.py`
  - `scripts/delete_black_frames.py`
  - `scripts/vlm_detector.py`, but only after rewriting its contract and documenting every prompt in dedicated markdown specs
- Quarantine, not active:
  - `scripts/pilot_bridge.py`
  Reason: environment-specific capture/control spike with unverified assumptions about the emulator/render path
- Delete from active repo surface:
  - runtime façade and contract-forward code such as `executor.py`, `scheduler.py`, `task_model.py`, `resource_model.py`
  - graph/navigation family as active code: `pathfind.py`, `session.py`, `locate.py`, `observe.py`, `schema_validator.py`, `graph_utils.py`, `alas_converter.py`
  - anchor-calibration and mock/offline side-path code unless later re-earned
  - one-off experiment files and unused ALAS-adjacent analysis helpers not required by the corpus pipeline
- Preserve important semantics from deleted code as docs, not executable claims:
  - event schema concepts if still wanted
  - any useful prompt intent or workflow assumptions
- Add explicit repo labels after the peel-back:
  - `active`: trusted code used right now
  - `quarantine`: retained but not trusted or supported
  - `data`: preserved truth/artifacts
  - `vendor`: external reference/runtime source
- Do not package surviving code yet.
  First reduce to a tiny trusted script set. Packaging and module architecture happen in the next rebuild phase.

## VLM Detector Rewrite Requirements
- Keep `vlm_detector.py` only as a documented labeling/detection tool, not as trusted runtime truth.
- Replace its current implicit contract with an explicit one:
  - primary use: corpus labeling, corpus adjudication, and offline analysis
  - current single-image prompt path is treated as insufficient and must be augmented
- Add backend support design for:
  - local OpenAI-compatible VLM endpoint as primary
  - optional remote adjudication/fan-out
  - optional two-model comparison for offline labeling
- For every surviving prompt template, create a dedicated markdown spec covering:
  - purpose
  - exact inputs passed
  - output contract
  - examples
  - known failure modes
  - when to use multi-image or extra context
- Explicitly review whether the detector should pass:
  - one image only
  - task context
  - neighboring frames
  - candidate labels or retrieved exemplars
  The default assumption for rebuild is that single-image-only classification is not enough for the long-term design.

## Peel-Back Workflow
- Phase 1: classify every non-vendored code file as `keep-active`, `quarantine`, or `delete`
- Phase 2: remove/quarantine code based on that manifest
- Phase 3: run targeted checks only on survivors and quarantine candidates that might be promoted later
- Phase 4: rewrite top-level docs so the repo no longer implies a runtime that does not exist
- Phase 5: begin a structured re-authoring interview/spec process for the rebuilt system

## Test Plan
- Do not run the full existing suite as a gate for the peel-back.
- Run targeted checks only for surviving code:
  - corpus labeling from ALAS logs to `index.jsonl`
  - screenshot dedupe on a sample corpus directory
  - black-frame cleanup detection in dry-run mode
  - VLM detector smoke checks against the configured local endpoint shape
- For `pilot_bridge.py`, if it remains quarantined, only run exploratory truth tests later to decide whether it is promotable or deletable.
- After deletions, remove or rewrite tests that only validate deleted/quarantined scaffolding.

## Re-Authoring Interview After Peel-Back
- Immediately after the reduction, run a new planning/spec pass focused on:
  - what the first real capability is
  - what truth sources exist
  - what the agent is actually instructed to do
  - what contracts are needed before new code is written
- That interview should produce:
  - one authoritative problem statement
  - one first deliverable
  - one minimal architecture
  - one explicit assignment contract
  - one list of trusted interfaces only

## Assumptions
- Deletion is the default unless a file preserves real, already-paid-for truth or is directly necessary for the screenshot-corpus-plus-ALAS-log workflow.
- `pilot_bridge.py` is not trusted enough to remain active, but may contain environment knowledge worth quarantining temporarily.
- The current graph/navigation line is not part of the active core during this reset.
- Surviving code remains script-shaped for now; package consolidation is deferred until after the repo is stripped to basics.
- The goal of this pass is not to rebuild functionality; it is to stop claiming functionality the repo has not earned.

---

## codex: PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:

PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:
# Documentation Realignment Plan: Keep Only `ALS` and `RES` as Domains

## Summary

Realign the docs tree so that only `ALS` and `RES` remain explicit domains. Retire `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` as domain labels in folder names, titles, and filenames. Reorganize the rest of the documentation into non-domain knowledge buckets that are useful to the agent: `project`, `architecture`, `workflows`, `prework`, `runtime`, `vlm`, `plans`, and `decisions`.

This is a **hybrid, medium-rewrite** pass:
- move existing docs into the new buckets
- merge or split docs where the old domain model hid the real topic
- rewrite outdated sections and contradictions
- keep prior `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` classification only as historical notes inside migrated docs, not in names or paths

## Implementation Changes

### 1. New target docs tree

```text
docs/
├─ ALS-reference/
├─ RES-research/
├─ architecture/
├─ project/
├─ workflows/
├─ prework/
├─ runtime/
├─ vlm/
├─ plans/
└─ decisions/
```

Rules:
- `ALS-reference/` and `RES-research/` are the only domain-shaped folders.
- Everything else is a knowledge bucket, not a domain.
- `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` disappear from folder names and filenames.
- Each migrated legacy doc gets a short “Historical note” near the top stating its previous location/classification.

### 2. Move existing docs into the new buckets

#### Keep as domains
- `docs/alas/*` -> `docs/ALS-reference/*`
- `docs/research/*` -> `docs/RES-research/*`

Keep `ALS-*` and `RES-*` naming in titles where it already fits.

#### Move project-level docs
- `docs/NORTH_STAR.md` -> `docs/project/north-star.md`
- `docs/REPO_STATUS.md` -> `docs/project/repo-status.md`
- `docs/testing-strategy.md` -> `docs/project/testing-strategy.md`

#### Move planning docs
- `docs/plans/MASTER_PLAN.md` -> `docs/plans/master-plan.md`
- `docs/plans/plan.md` -> `docs/plans/current-plan.md`
- `docs/rebuild/INTERVIEW.md` -> `docs/plans/rebuild-interview.md`

#### Move architecture docs
- `docs/architecture.md` -> `docs/architecture/architecture-overview.md`

Rewrite this doc so it explains:
- `ALS` and `RES` as knowledge domains
- `prework`, `runtime`, and `vlm` as non-domain implementation/knowledge buckets
- why docs and code are intentionally organized on different axes

#### Move and reshape workflow docs
- `docs/execution/EXE-workflows.md` -> `docs/workflows/azur-lane-workflows.md`

Rewrite to remove `EXE` framing and make it clearly about:
- assignment/workflow inventory
- entry conditions
- substate complexity
- success criteria
- escalation points

#### Move prework docs
- `docs/observation/OBS-corpus-cleanup.md` -> `docs/prework/corpus-cleanup.md`
- `docs/execution/EXE-data-collection.md` -> `docs/prework/data-collection.md`
- `docs/RES-research/RES-alas-build-plan.md` stays in `RES-research/` unless it is mostly operational build procedure; if so, split it into:
  - research rationale stays in `RES-research/`
  - executable collection/build procedure moves to `docs/prework/alas-build-plan.md`

#### Move runtime docs
- `docs/execution/EXE-backend-hardening.md` -> `docs/runtime/backend-hardening.md`
- `docs/execution/EXE-pilot-bridge-rework.md` -> `docs/runtime/pilot-bridge-rework.md`

Create or rewrite:
- `docs/runtime/runtime-overview.md`
- `docs/runtime/observation-contracts.md`

Then fold content from:
- `docs/observation/OBS-overview.md`
- `docs/navigation/NAV-overview.md`
- `docs/execution/EXE-overview.md`
- `docs/automation/AUT-overview.md`

into the runtime docs above instead of preserving those old overviews as separate legacy stubs.

#### Move and consolidate VLM docs
Create:
- `docs/vlm/VLM-overview.md`
- `docs/vlm/VLM-model-profiles.md`
- `docs/vlm/VLM-task-contracts.md`
- `docs/vlm/VLM-prompts.md`

Use these sources:
- move VLM capability material out of `OBS-overview.md`
- move prompt material out of `docs/prompts/vlm/*`
- use current research docs only as references, not as the primary operational spec

Then delete the split prompt-doc pattern in favor of one consolidated prompt doc with sections for:
- shared model behavior assumptions
- model configuration vs prompt wording
- classification tasks
- grounding/location tasks
- adjudication/comparison tasks

#### Keep decisions where they are
- `docs/decisions/*` stays in `docs/decisions/`

### 3. Rewrite rules for migrated docs

Apply these rules consistently:
- preserve useful existing structure such as status, current state, what exists, what is missing, and open questions
- remove old `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` codes from titles and filenames
- keep prior classification only as a short historical note in the body
- rewrite sections that claim a runtime exists where it does not
- rewrite sections that confuse prompt text with model configuration
- rewrite sections that bury VLM as a side detail instead of a first-class capability
- remove contradictions introduced by the failed peel-back rewrite and the older runtime-first language
- preserve direct, project-memory style rather than polishing docs into user-facing prose

### 4. Update agent-entry docs

Update:
- `AGENTS.md`
- `CLAUDE.md`

Requirements:
- point at the new docs tree
- treat docs as the agent knowledge layer, not human-facing product docs
- stop describing `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` as active domains
- explicitly tell the agent that `ALS` and `RES` remain the retained domains
- describe `prework`, `runtime`, and `vlm` as non-domain buckets

### 5. Remove old bucket structure after migration

After all moves and rewrites are complete, remove these legacy doc folders if empty:
- `docs/observation/`
- `docs/navigation/`
- `docs/execution/`
- `docs/automation/`
- `docs/rebuild/`
- `docs/prompts/`

## Test Plan

Run only non-destructive documentation checks:
- verify every moved doc path exists in the new tree
- verify no remaining doc filenames start with `OBS-`, `NAV-`, `EXE-`, or `AUT-`
- verify `ALS` and `RES` remain visible as the only domain-coded folders
- verify all internal links from `AGENTS.md`, `CLAUDE.md`, and moved docs point to valid new paths
- verify no references remain to removed legacy folder paths except inside intentional historical notes
- verify consolidated VLM docs cover:
  - model profiles
  - task contracts
  - prompt/config separation

## Assumptions and Defaults

- Keep only `ALS` and `RES` as explicit domains.
- Treat `prework`, `runtime`, `vlm`, `project`, `architecture`, and `workflows` as non-domain knowledge buckets.
- Retire `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` from names and paths entirely.
- Preserve prior `OBS/NAV/EXE/AUT` classification only inside the migrated doc body when useful for historical context.
- Prefer merging old overview docs into fewer, more accurate docs rather than preserving all legacy overview files one-for-one.
- `docs/decisions/` and `docs/plans/` stay as project categories rather than being domainized.

## codex: ## Code review guidelines:

## Code review guidelines:
# Review guidelines:

You are acting as a reviewer for a proposed code change made by another engineer.

Below are some default guidelines for determining whether the original author would appreciate the issue being flagged.

These are not the final word in determining whether an issue is a bug. In many cases, you will encounter other, more specific guidelines. These may be present elsewhere in a developer message, a user message, a file, or even elsewhere in this system message.
Those guidelines should be considered to override these general instructions.

Here are the general guidelines for determining whether something is a bug and should be flagged.

1. It meaningfully impacts the accuracy, performance, security, or maintainability of the code.
2. The bug is discrete and actionable (i.e. not a general issue with the codebase or a combination of multiple issues).
3. Fixing the bug does not demand a level of rigor that is not present in the rest of the codebase (e.g. one doesn't need very detailed comments and input validation in a repository of one-off scripts in personal projects)
4. The bug was introduced in the commit (pre-existing bugs should not be flagged).
5. The author of the original PR would likely fix the issue if they were made aware of it.
6. The bug does not rely on unstated assumptions about the codebase or author's intent.
7. It is not enough to speculate that a change may disrupt another part of the codebase, to be considered a bug, one must identify the other parts of the code that are provably affected.
8. The bug is clearly not just an intentional change by the original author.

When flagging a bug, you will also provide an accompanying comment. Once again, these guidelines are not the final word on how to construct a comment -- defer to any subsequent guidelines that you encounter.

1. The comment should be clear about why the issue is a bug.
2. The comment should appropriately communicate the severity of the issue. It should not claim that an issue is more severe than it actually is.
3. The comment should be brief. The body should be at most 1 paragraph. It should not introduce line breaks within the natural language flow unless it is necessary for the code fragment.
4. The comment should not include any chunks of code longer than 3 lines. Any code chunks should be wrapped in markdown inline code tags or a code block.
5. The comment should clearly and explicitly communicate the scenarios, environments, or inputs that are necessary for the bug to arise. The comment should immediately indicate that the issue's severity depends on these factors.
6. The comment's tone should be matter-of-fact and not accusatory or overly positive. It should read as a helpful AI assistant suggestion without sounding too much like a human reviewer.
7. The comment should be written such that the original author can immediately grasp the idea without close reading.
8. The comment should avoid excessive flattery and comments that are not helpful to the original author. The comment should avoid phrasing like "Great job ...", "Thanks for ...".

Below are some more detailed guidelines that you should apply to this specific review.

HOW MANY FINDINGS TO RETURN:

Output all findings that the original author would fix if they knew about it. If there is no finding that a person would definitely love to see and fix, prefer outputting no findings. Do not stop at the first qualifying finding. Continue until you've listed every qualifying finding.

GUIDELINES:

- Ignore trivial style unless it obscures meaning or violates documented standards.
- Use one comment per distinct issue (or a multi-line range if necessary).
- Use ```suggestion blocks ONLY for concrete replacement code (minimal lines; no commentary inside the block).
- In every ```suggestion block, preserve the exact leading whitespace of the replaced lines (spaces vs tabs, number of spaces).
- Do NOT introduce or remove outer indentation levels unless that is the actual fix.

The comments will be presented in the code review as inline comments. You should avoid providing unnecessary location details in the comment body. Always keep the line range as short as possible for interpreting the issue. Avoid ranges longer than 5–10 lines; instead, choose the most suitable subrange that pinpoints the problem.

At the beginning of the finding title, tag the bug with priority level. For example "[P1] Un-padding slices along wrong tensor dimensions". [P0] – Drop everything to fix. Blocking release, operations, or major usage. Only use for universal issues that do not depend on any assumptions about the inputs. · [P1] – Urgent. Should be addressed in the next cycle · [P2] – Normal. To be fixed eventually · [P3] – Low. Nice to have.

Additionally, include a numeric priority field in the JSON output for each finding: set "priority" to 0 for P0, 1 for P1, 2 for P2, or 3 for P3. If a priority cannot be determined, omit the field or use null.

At the end of your findings, output an "overall correctness" verdict of whether or not the patch should be considered "correct".
Correct implies that existing code and tests will not break, and the patch is free of bugs and other blocking issues.
Ignore non-blocking issues such as style, formatting, typos, documentation, and other nits.

FORMATTING GUIDELINES:
The finding description should be one paragraph.

OUTPUT FORMAT:

## Output schema — MUST MATCH _exactly_

```json
{
  "findings": [
    {
      "title": "<≤ 80 chars, imperative>",
      "body": "<valid Markdown explaining *why* this is a problem; cite files/lines/functions>",
      "confidence_score": <float 0.0-1.0>,
      "priority": <int 0-3, optional>,
      "code_location": {
        "absolute_file_path": "<file path>",
        "line_range": {"start": <int>, "end": <int>}
      }
    }
  ],
  "overall_correctness": "patch is correct" | "patch is incorrect",
  "overall_explanation": "<1-3 sentence explanation justifying the overall_correctness verdict>",
  "overall_confidence_score": <float 0.0-1.0>
}
```

- **Do not** wrap the JSON in markdown fences or extra prose.
- The code_location field is required and must include absolute_file_path and line_range.
  \*Line ranges must be as short as possible for interpreting the issue (avoid ranges over 5–10 lines; pick the most suitable subrange).
- The code_location should overlap with the diff.
- Do not generate a PR fix.
- Your **initial** response to the user must always use the JSON schema above.
- After the initial response, choose the format based on the user's request:
  - If they explicitly ask for another review ("re-review", "rerun the review", etc.), return the findings in the exact JSON schema again.
  - If they ask you to fix something, answer follow-up questions, or otherwise request non-review help, respond in plain text (no JSON or schema output).
- All review instructions apply to the overall code review conversation. Continue following the guidelines in every response, only switching between JSON and plain text as described above.

## codex: # Review findings:

# Review findings:

## Finding 1 (scripts/kimi_review.py:57) [added]
[P1] Pass screenshots to Kimi as media instead of text paths

`build_prompt()` turns the requested screenshots into plain `- path/to/image.png` text, and `run_kimi()` forwards that string via `kimi -p`. In Kimi print mode this is only text input, so the model never receives the image bytes and cannot perform the visible-only screenshot review this helper is supposed to provide. Any real use of `scripts/kimi_review.py` will therefore produce output based on filenames/context rather than the screenshots themselves.

## codex: You are advising on a project called MasterStateMa...

You are advising on a project called MasterStateMachine. The goal is to build an autonomous runtime state machine for controlling Azur Lane (a mobile game) via an emulator. The project currently has: (1) ALAS - an existing open-source bot used as reference, its logs are coarse and often say 'unknown' at critical moments, (2) a corpus of ~4000 screenshots with timestamps plus matching ALAS logs, (3) a VLM pipeline concept where a small model does always-on state detection and a larger model does deeper analysis. The project is in a 'data-first rebuild' phase. The current next step is a 'corpus review playbook' that produces 'ledger rows' - human-verified records of what was visibly true in short frame windows compared to what the logs/machine labels said. The question: What does a ledger row actually need to accomplish to be useful downstream? What is the minimum viable bridge from 'we have N verified ledger rows' to 'we can now spec a state machine'? What N is enough? What specific downstream artifacts does the ledger feed into? Be concrete and critical - identify gaps in this reasoning chain.

---

## codex: can you write these in here to investigate?> # GUI...

can you write these in here to investigate?> # GUI agent models exploded between October 2025 and March 2026

**At least 18 new or significantly updated GUI agent and grounding models** shipped in the six months since October 2025, nearly all built atop Qwen2.5-VL or Qwen3-VL backbones. The field has bifurcated clearly: proprietary frontier models (GPT-5.4, Claude Opus 4.6) now exceed human performance on OSWorld-Verified at **75%** and **72.7%** respectively, while open-weight models deployable on a single RTX 5090 have crossed **56.7%** (EvoCUA-32B) — roughly where frontier proprietary models stood just six months ago. GRPO-style reinforcement learning has become the dominant post-training recipe for grounding models, and Alibaba's MAI-UI family has set new state-of-the-art scores on **ScreenSpot-Pro (73.5%)** and **AndroidWorld (76.7%)**. Every model listed below ships with public weights on HuggingFace unless noted otherwise, and every 7B–9B variant fits comfortably on a 32GB GPU at full precision.

---

## Full agent models you can deploy on 32GB VRAM

These models perform end-to-end planning and acting — they interpret a task, reason about the screen, and emit GUI actions (clicks, types, scrolls) without requiring a separate planner.

**EvoCUA-8B / 32B** (Meituan, January 2026) is the headline release for local deployment. Built on Qwen3-VL and trained with an iterative self-evolutionary loop — SFT cold start on ~1K trajectories, then rejection fine-tuning, then step-level DPO (STEPO), cycled repeatedly with a verifiable synthesis engine generating synthetic tasks — the 32B variant hit **56.7% on OSWorld-Verified**, making it the #1 open-source single-model result at time of release. The 8B variant scored **46.1%**, surpassing OpenCUA-72B (45.0%) despite being 9× smaller. Weights are on HuggingFace under Apache 2.0 (`meituan/EvoCUA-32B-20260105`, `meituan/EvoCUA-8B-20260105`). The 8B fits at FP16 in ~18GB; the 32B requires **Q4 quantization** (~18GB) to fit in 32GB, with an 8-bit MLX variant also available. Inference uses vLLM natively.

**MAI-UI-2B / 8B** (Alibaba Tongyi-MAI, December 2025 – January 2026) anchors the Alibaba GUI agent ecosystem. Based on Qwen3-VL, it introduced a self-evolving data pipeline plus online RL scaled to 512 parallel Android environments. The 8B model scores **65.7% on ScreenSpot-Pro** (best among all ≤8B models, open or closed) and **73.5%** is the score for the larger 32B variant. The full MAI-UI family extends to a 235B-A22B MoE that achieves **76.7% on AndroidWorld** and **91.3% on MMBench-GUI L2**, but only the 2B and 8B weights are publicly released (`Tongyi-MAI/MAI-UI-8B`, Apache 2.0). The 8B weighs **17.6GB** in FP16 — fits on 32GB with headroom. GGUF quantizations exist via community repos (Q4_K_M at 5GB).

**UI-Venus 1.5-2B / 8B / 30B-A3B** (Ant Group / inclusionAI, February 2026) followed a four-stage pipeline: mid-training, offline RL, online RL, and model merge. The 8B variant scores **69.6% on ScreenSpot-Pro** and **77.6% on AndroidWorld** — the latter representing the current single-model open-weight SOTA for mobile. A 30B-A3B MoE variant (30B total, 3B active) is also available. All weights are on HuggingFace (`inclusionAI/UI-Venus-1.5-8B`). The 8B fits at FP16; the MoE variant needs all expert weights loaded (~60GB FP16), so it requires **Q3 quantization** or offloading for 32GB.

**ScaleCUA-3B / 7B / 33B** (Shanghai AI Lab / OpenGVLab, January 2026) is trained on a massive cross-platform SFT dataset spanning six operating systems (Windows, macOS, Linux, Android, iOS, Web) with 471K GUI understanding samples and 17.1M grounding instances. It supports three inference modes: grounding-only, direct action, and reasoned action with chain-of-thought. The 33B scores **59.2% on ScreenSpot-Pro** and **60.6% on OSWorld-G**. Weights are Apache 2.0 (`OpenGVLab/ScaleCUA-33B`). The 7B fits easily; the 33B needs **Q4 quantization** for 32GB.

**AutoGLM-Phone-9B** (Zhipu AI, December 2025) targets mobile phone automation specifically. Built on GLM-4.1V-9B-Thinking (not a Qwen derivative), it was trained with WebRL — a self-evolving online curriculum RL method. It operates across Chinese and English mobile apps via WiFi-based device control, scoring **36.2% on AndroidLab** (surpassing GPT-4o and Claude). Weights plus a multilingual variant are available (`zai-org/AutoGLM-Phone-9B`, `zai-org/AutoGLM-Phone-9B-Multilingual`). At 20.6GB FP16, it fits on 32GB, with official GGUF quants from ggml-org (Q4_K_M at 6.17GB).

**GUI-Libra-3B / 4B / 7B / 8B** (Microsoft Research, February 2026) tackles a specific problem: chain-of-thought reasoning degrades grounding accuracy in GUI agents. Its fix is two-stage: action-aware SFT (ASFT) that reweights loss to emphasize action tokens, then KL-regularized GRPO that prevents the policy from drifting too far. The 4B (Qwen3-VL) and 8B (Qwen3-VL) variants beat GPT-4o on AndroidWorld and Online-Mind2Web. Code and training recipes are released on GitHub (`GUI-Libra/GUI-Libra`); HuggingFace model weights were not confirmed at time of research.

**AgentCPM-GUI-8B** (THUNLP / OpenBMB, initial May 2025, EMNLP November 2025) is notable as the first open-source GUI agent tuned for **30+ Chinese mobile apps** using a three-stage pipeline: grounding-aware pretraining on 12M bilingual Android screenshots, SFT on 55K Chinese+English trajectories, and GRPO fine-tuning. Achieves **96.9% Type-Match** on CAGUI. Weights are Apache 2.0 (`openbmb/AgentCPM-GUI`) at 16.2GB FP16 — fits on 32GB.

---

## Grounding-only models for coordinate prediction

These models take a screenshot and a natural-language instruction and return screen coordinates. They do not plan multi-step workflows — pair them with a reasoning model (o3, GPT-5, Claude) for full agent behavior.

**POINTS-GUI-G-8B** (Tencent WeChat AI, February 2026) stands out architecturally: it uses Tencent's custom POINTS-1.5 VLM (Qwen3 7B LLM + NaViT vision encoder), not a fine-tuned Qwen-VL. Trained with a three-pillar recipe — refined data engineering with difficulty grading, continuous vision encoder fine-tuning, and **RL with verifiable rewards** — it scores **59.9% on ScreenSpot-Pro** and **66.0% on OSWorld-G** (both SOTA among grounding-only models at release). Weights are on HuggingFace (`tencent/POINTS-GUI-G`) under a custom license. Fits at FP16 on 32GB.

**Holo1.5-3B / 7B / 72B** (H Company, France, September 2025) is a grounding and UI-VQA perception model fine-tuned from Qwen2.5-VL with SFT + GRPO. The 7B scores **57.94% on ScreenSpot-Pro** and supports resolutions up to 3840×2160. The 7B is Apache 2.0 (`Hcompany/Holo1.5-7B`); the 72B is CC-BY-NC-4.0. The 7B fits easily at FP16; the 72B does not fit on 32GB.

**GUI-Actor-2B / 3B / 7B** (Microsoft, NeurIPS 2025) introduced coordinate-free grounding via an attention-based `<ACTOR>` token — instead of generating coordinate text, it reads grounding locations from attention maps. The 7B (Qwen2.5-VL base) scores **44.6% on ScreenSpot-Pro**, surpassing UI-TARS-72B's baseline of 38.1%. Weights are available (`microsoft/GUI-Actor-7B-Qwen2.5-VL`). All sizes fit on 32GB.

**Phi-Ground-4B / 7B** (Microsoft, July 2025) is the only non-Qwen grounding model, built on Phi-4-MM. Trained with SFT on 40M+ samples plus DPO, it achieves **55.0% on ScreenSpot-Pro** in an agent setting (paired with o4-mini as planner) and **43.2% end-to-end**. Designed for the Windows Copilot pipeline. Available via GitHub. Fits easily on 32GB.

**UI-Ins-7B / 32B** (Alibaba Tongyi, October 2025) uses an "Instruction-as-Reasoning" paradigm where the model analyzes grounding instructions from multiple perspectives. Trained with SFT + GRPO, the 7B achieves **74.1% success rate on AndroidWorld** when used as the grounding backbone for a larger agent system. The 7B is the practical choice for 32GB deployment.

**GUI-G²-3B / 7B** (Zhejiang University, August 2025 code / AAAI 2026 paper) applies GRPO with **Gaussian reward modeling** instead of binary point-in-box rewards — using Gaussian point reward, coverage reward, and adaptive variance. Improves over standard binary-reward GRPO on ScreenSpot-Pro and ScreenSpot-v2. Weights are on HuggingFace.

**ScreenVLM-316M** (IBM Research, February 2026) is an ultra-lightweight screen parsing model combining SigLIP-2 with a Granite-165M decoder. At just **316M parameters**, it produces structured markup (ScreenTag format) with bounding boxes, 55-class UI element types, and text for all visible elements. Designed for on-device/low-latency deployment. No confirmed HuggingFace release yet, but trivially fits any GPU.

---

## The GRPO training revolution for GUI grounding

DeepSeek-R1's popularization of GRPO in January 2025 triggered a wave of RL-trained grounding models. The Salesforce GTA1 team's "GRPO for GUI Grounding Done Right" blog crystallized key findings: **thinking tokens are not required** for static grounding (they can hurt), click-based binary rewards suffice, no SFT cold start is needed with strong base models, and KL regularization should be avoided for coordinate flexibility. Thinking *does* help in dynamic environments like AndroidWorld, where trajectory history matters.

For the **mobile/Android ADB use case** specifically, three models stand out among GRPO/RL-trained options:

- **AgentCPM-GUI-8B** uses a three-stage GRPO pipeline trained on 12M Android screenshots, specifically designed for Chinese + English mobile apps. It has the most complete Android-specific training.
- **AutoGLM-Phone-9B** uses WebRL (not GRPO per se, but online curriculum RL) and operates via WiFi-based device control with support for apps like Gmail, Google Maps, WeChat, and Taobao.
- **MAI-UI-8B** was trained with online RL in live Android environments scaled to 512 concurrent instances. Its **76.7% AndroidWorld** score (235B variant) represents the SOTA, though the locally-deployable 8B variant is also strong.

Additional RL-trained grounding models relevant to mobile include **GUI-ARP-7B** (adaptive multi-stage GRPO, SOTA among 7B on ScreenSpot-Pro), **MobileGUI-RL** (online GRPO with trajectory-aware advantages, ICLR 2026, weights not yet public), and **OmegaUse** (30B-A3B MoE, SFT+GRPO, 96.3% ScreenSpot-V2, weights not public).

---

## The OSWorld-Verified leaderboard as of March 2026

Human performance on OSWorld-Verified is estimated at **~72.4%**. Two proprietary models have now surpassed this threshold. The landscape since October 2025 has shifted dramatically:

| Rank | Model | Score | Type | Deployable on 32GB? |
|------|-------|-------|------|---------------------|
| 1 | GPT-5.4 | **75.0%** | Proprietary (Mar 2026) | No (API only) |
| 2 | Claude Opus 4.6 | **72.7%** | Proprietary (Feb 2026) | No (API only) |
| 3 | GPT-5.4 mini | **72.1%** | Proprietary (Mar 2026) | No (API only) |
| 4 | GPT-5.3 Codex | **64.7%** | Proprietary (Feb 2026) | No (API only) |
| 5 | Kimi K2.5 | **63.3%** | Open-weight MoE 1T/32B-active (Jan 2026) | No (~500GB INT4) |
| 6 | CoACT-1 | **60.8%** | Agentic framework (proprietary backbone) | No |
| 7 | Qwen3.5-122B-A10B | **58.0%** | Open-weight MoE (2026) | No (too large) |
| 8 | EvoCUA-32B | **56.7%** | Open-weight dense (Jan 2026) | **Yes, Q4** |
| 9 | Agent S2.5 + o3 | **56.0%** | Agentic framework | No (needs o3 API) |
| 10 | Qwen3.5-27B | **56.2%** | Open-weight dense (2026) | **Yes, Q4** |
| 11 | GTA1 + o3 | **53.1%** | Framework + proprietary planner | No (needs o3) |
| 12 | AutoGLM-OS-9B | **48.1%** | Dense 9B (ComputerRL, 2025) | Yes if released (not public) |
| 13 | UI-TARS-2 | **47.5%** | MoE 230B (ByteDance, Sep 2025) | No (not public, too large) |
| 14 | EvoCUA-8B | **46.1%** | Open-weight dense (Jan 2026) | **Yes, FP16** |
| 15 | OpenCUA-72B | **45.0%** | Open-weight dense (2025) | No (too large) |

**New entrants since October 2025** include: GPT-5.4 and variants, Claude Opus 4.6, Kimi K2.5, EvoCUA-8B/32B, Qwen3.5 family, and AutoGLM-OS. The open-weight 32GB-deployable frontier moved from ~38% (Qwen3-VL) to **56.7%** (EvoCUA-32B at Q4) in five months — a **19-point gain**. A critical caveat from Epoch AI: some OSWorld tasks can be completed via terminal commands or Python scripts without GUI interaction, so score differences partly reflect code capabilities rather than pure visual grounding.

---

## Notable models that exist but cannot run locally

**UI-TARS-2** (ByteDance, September 2025) is a **230B MoE** (23B active) with a 532M vision encoder, initialized from Seed-thinking-1.6. It scores 47.5% on OSWorld and 73.3% on AndroidWorld, but weights are **not publicly released** — only UI-TARS-1.5-7B is available. Even if released, the full model needs ~115GB at INT4.

**Kimi K2.5** (Moonshot AI, January 2026) is a **1.04T MoE** (384 experts, 8 active, 32B active parameters) released under Modified MIT license on HuggingFace. It scores **63.3% on OSWorld-Verified** and 92.3% on OCRBench. Despite being open-weight, it requires ~500GB+ even at INT4 for all expert weights. The INT4 QAT version is optimized for Hopper-class multi-GPU clusters.

**UltraCUA-7B/32B** (Apple Research, October 2025) bridges GUI actions with programmatic tool calls across 10 desktop domains. Scores 41.0% on OSWorld (32B). Weights are **not released** — research paper only.

---

## Deployment guide for RTX 5090 (32GB VRAM)

| Model | Params | Recommended Quant | VRAM Est. | HuggingFace | Best Benchmark |
|-------|--------|-------------------|-----------|-------------|----------------|
| **EvoCUA-8B** | 9B dense | FP16 (no quant needed) | ~18GB | `meituan/EvoCUA-8B-20260105` | OSWorld 46.1% |
| **EvoCUA-32B** | 32B dense | Q4_K_M (GGUF) | ~18GB | `meituan/EvoCUA-32B-20260105` | OSWorld 56.7% |
| **MAI-UI-8B** | 9B dense | FP16 or Q5 GGUF | ~17.6GB | `Tongyi-MAI/MAI-UI-8B` | SSPro 65.7% |
| **MAI-UI-2B** | 2B dense | FP16 | ~4GB | `Tongyi-MAI/MAI-UI-2B` | SSPro 57.4% |
| **UI-Venus 1.5-8B** | 8B dense | FP16 | ~16GB | `inclusionAI/UI-Venus-1.5-8B` | AndroidWorld 77.6% |
| **ScaleCUA-7B** | 7B dense | FP16 | ~14GB | `OpenGVLab/ScaleCUA-7B` | SSPro 59.2% (33B) |
| **AutoGLM-Phone-9B** | 9B dense | FP16 or Q4 GGUF | ~20.6GB / 6.2GB | `zai-org/AutoGLM-Phone-9B` | AndroidLab 36.2% |
| **AgentCPM-GUI-8B** | 8B dense | FP16 | ~16.2GB | `openbmb/AgentCPM-GUI` | CAGUI 96.9% |
| **POINTS-GUI-G-8B** | ~8B | FP16 | ~16GB | `tencent/POINTS-GUI-G` | OSWorld-G 66.0% |
| **Holo1.5-7B** | 7B dense | FP16 | ~14GB | `Hcompany/Holo1.5-7B` | SSPro 57.9% |
| **GUI-Actor-7B** | 7B + action head | FP16 | ~15GB | `microsoft/GUI-Actor-7B-Qwen2.5-VL` | SSPro 44.6% |
| **Phi-Ground-7B** | ~7B | FP16 | ~14GB | GitHub (microsoft) | SSPro 55.0% (agent) |
| **GUI-G²-7B** | 7B | FP16 | ~14GB | HuggingFace (ZJU) | SSPro improved |

For a **grounding + planner** stack on a single 32GB GPU: run a Q4-quantized grounding model (e.g., MAI-UI-8B at ~5GB GGUF) alongside a small reasoning model, or use a cloud API (o3, GPT-5) as the planner with a local grounding model as the executor. For a **single end-to-end agent**: EvoCUA-32B at Q4 gives the highest OSWorld score achievable on one consumer GPU.

---

## Conclusion

The October 2025 – March 2026 window marks the period when GUI agents crossed from research curiosity to practical capability. Three developments define this moment. First, **RL post-training became table stakes** — every competitive new model uses some form of GRPO, DPO, or online RL, often with self-evolving data pipelines that eliminate the need for human annotation at scale. Second, **Qwen-VL has become the de facto backbone**: of the 18 new models surveyed, 15 are built on Qwen2.5-VL or Qwen3-VL. The exceptions are AutoGLM-Phone (GLM-4), POINTS-GUI-G (custom POINTS-1.5), and Phi-Ground (Phi-4). Third, **the 7B–9B parameter class has become the sweet spot for local deployment** — models like EvoCUA-8B, MAI-UI-8B, and UI-Venus 1.5-8B now match or exceed what 72B models achieved six months ago, and all fit comfortably on a 32GB GPU at full precision.

For the ADB/Android automation use case specifically, the strongest locally-deployable option is **UI-Venus 1.5-8B** (77.6% AndroidWorld) or **MAI-UI-8B** (from the same ecosystem that produced the 76.7% AndroidWorld SOTA), both paired with either their own chain-of-thought reasoning or a cloud planner. For desktop OSWorld-class tasks, **EvoCUA-32B at Q4** represents the frontier of what a single RTX 5090 can run. The gap between this local deployment ceiling (56.7%) and frontier proprietary models (75.0%) remains substantial but is closing at roughly 3–4 points per month.

---

## codex: can you write these in here to investigate?> # GUI...

can you write these in here to investigate?> # GUI agent models exploded between October 2025 and March 2026

**At least 18 new or significantly updated GUI agent and grounding models** shipped in the six months since October 2025, nearly all built atop Qwen2.5-VL or Qwen3-VL backbones. The field has bifurcated clearly: proprietary frontier models (GPT-5.4, Claude Opus 4.6) now exceed human performance on OSWorld-Verified at **75%** and **72.7%** respectively, while open-weight models deployable on a single RTX 5090 have crossed **56.7%** (EvoCUA-32B) — roughly where frontier proprietary models stood just six months ago. GRPO-style reinforcement learning has become the dominant post-training recipe for grounding models, and Alibaba's MAI-UI family has set new state-of-the-art scores on **ScreenSpot-Pro (73.5%)** and **AndroidWorld (76.7%)**. Every model listed below ships with public weights on HuggingFace unless noted otherwise, and every 7B–9B variant fits comfortably on a 32GB GPU at full precision.

---

## Full agent models you can deploy on 32GB VRAM

These models perform end-to-end planning and acting — they interpret a task, reason about the screen, and emit GUI actions (clicks, types, scrolls) without requiring a separate planner.

**EvoCUA-8B / 32B** (Meituan, January 2026) is the headline release for local deployment. Built on Qwen3-VL and trained with an iterative self-evolutionary loop — SFT cold start on ~1K trajectories, then rejection fine-tuning, then step-level DPO (STEPO), cycled repeatedly with a verifiable synthesis engine generating synthetic tasks — the 32B variant hit **56.7% on OSWorld-Verified**, making it the #1 open-source single-model result at time of release. The 8B variant scored **46.1%**, surpassing OpenCUA-72B (45.0%) despite being 9× smaller. Weights are on HuggingFace under Apache 2.0 (`meituan/EvoCUA-32B-20260105`, `meituan/EvoCUA-8B-20260105`). The 8B fits at FP16 in ~18GB; the 32B requires **Q4 quantization** (~18GB) to fit in 32GB, with an 8-bit MLX variant also available. Inference uses vLLM natively.

**MAI-UI-2B / 8B** (Alibaba Tongyi-MAI, December 2025 – January 2026) anchors the Alibaba GUI agent ecosystem. Based on Qwen3-VL, it introduced a self-evolving data pipeline plus online RL scaled to 512 parallel Android environments. The 8B model scores **65.7% on ScreenSpot-Pro** (best among all ≤8B models, open or closed) and **73.5%** is the score for the larger 32B variant. The full MAI-UI family extends to a 235B-A22B MoE that achieves **76.7% on AndroidWorld** and **91.3% on MMBench-GUI L2**, but only the 2B and 8B weights are publicly released (`Tongyi-MAI/MAI-UI-8B`, Apache 2.0). The 8B weighs **17.6GB** in FP16 — fits on 32GB with headroom. GGUF quantizations exist via community repos (Q4_K_M at 5GB).

**UI-Venus 1.5-2B / 8B / 30B-A3B** (Ant Group / inclusionAI, February 2026) followed a four-stage pipeline: mid-training, offline RL, online RL, and model merge. The 8B variant scores **69.6% on ScreenSpot-Pro** and **77.6% on AndroidWorld** — the latter representing the current single-model open-weight SOTA for mobile. A 30B-A3B MoE variant (30B total, 3B active) is also available. All weights are on HuggingFace (`inclusionAI/UI-Venus-1.5-8B`). The 8B fits at FP16; the MoE variant needs all expert weights loaded (~60GB FP16), so it requires **Q3 quantization** or offloading for 32GB.

**ScaleCUA-3B / 7B / 33B** (Shanghai AI Lab / OpenGVLab, January 2026) is trained on a massive cross-platform SFT dataset spanning six operating systems (Windows, macOS, Linux, Android, iOS, Web) with 471K GUI understanding samples and 17.1M grounding instances. It supports three inference modes: grounding-only, direct action, and reasoned action with chain-of-thought. The 33B scores **59.2% on ScreenSpot-Pro** and **60.6% on OSWorld-G**. Weights are Apache 2.0 (`OpenGVLab/ScaleCUA-33B`). The 7B fits easily; the 33B needs **Q4 quantization** for 32GB.

**AutoGLM-Phone-9B** (Zhipu AI, December 2025) targets mobile phone automation specifically. Built on GLM-4.1V-9B-Thinking (not a Qwen derivative), it was trained with WebRL — a self-evolving online curriculum RL method. It operates across Chinese and English mobile apps via WiFi-based device control, scoring **36.2% on AndroidLab** (surpassing GPT-4o and Claude). Weights plus a multilingual variant are available (`zai-org/AutoGLM-Phone-9B`, `zai-org/AutoGLM-Phone-9B-Multilingual`). At 20.6GB FP16, it fits on 32GB, with official GGUF quants from ggml-org (Q4_K_M at 6.17GB).

**GUI-Libra-3B / 4B / 7B / 8B** (Microsoft Research, February 2026) tackles a specific problem: chain-of-thought reasoning degrades grounding accuracy in GUI agents. Its fix is two-stage: action-aware SFT (ASFT) that reweights loss to emphasize action tokens, then KL-regularized GRPO that prevents the policy from drifting too far. The 4B (Qwen3-VL) and 8B (Qwen3-VL) variants beat GPT-4o on AndroidWorld and Online-Mind2Web. Code and training recipes are released on GitHub (`GUI-Libra/GUI-Libra`); HuggingFace model weights were not confirmed at time of research.

**AgentCPM-GUI-8B** (THUNLP / OpenBMB, initial May 2025, EMNLP November 2025) is notable as the first open-source GUI agent tuned for **30+ Chinese mobile apps** using a three-stage pipeline: grounding-aware pretraining on 12M bilingual Android screenshots, SFT on 55K Chinese+English trajectories, and GRPO fine-tuning. Achieves **96.9% Type-Match** on CAGUI. Weights are Apache 2.0 (`openbmb/AgentCPM-GUI`) at 16.2GB FP16 — fits on 32GB.

---

## Grounding-only models for coordinate prediction

These models take a screenshot and a natural-language instruction and return screen coordinates. They do not plan multi-step workflows — pair them with a reasoning model (o3, GPT-5, Claude) for full agent behavior.

**POINTS-GUI-G-8B** (Tencent WeChat AI, February 2026) stands out architecturally: it uses Tencent's custom POINTS-1.5 VLM (Qwen3 7B LLM + NaViT vision encoder), not a fine-tuned Qwen-VL. Trained with a three-pillar recipe — refined data engineering with difficulty grading, continuous vision encoder fine-tuning, and **RL with verifiable rewards** — it scores **59.9% on ScreenSpot-Pro** and **66.0% on OSWorld-G** (both SOTA among grounding-only models at release). Weights are on HuggingFace (`tencent/POINTS-GUI-G`) under a custom license. Fits at FP16 on 32GB.

**Holo1.5-3B / 7B / 72B** (H Company, France, September 2025) is a grounding and UI-VQA perception model fine-tuned from Qwen2.5-VL with SFT + GRPO. The 7B scores **57.94% on ScreenSpot-Pro** and supports resolutions up to 3840×2160. The 7B is Apache 2.0 (`Hcompany/Holo1.5-7B`); the 72B is CC-BY-NC-4.0. The 7B fits easily at FP16; the 72B does not fit on 32GB.

**GUI-Actor-2B / 3B / 7B** (Microsoft, NeurIPS 2025) introduced coordinate-free grounding via an attention-based `<ACTOR>` token — instead of generating coordinate text, it reads grounding locations from attention maps. The 7B (Qwen2.5-VL base) scores **44.6% on ScreenSpot-Pro**, surpassing UI-TARS-72B's baseline of 38.1%. Weights are available (`microsoft/GUI-Actor-7B-Qwen2.5-VL`). All sizes fit on 32GB.

**Phi-Ground-4B / 7B** (Microsoft, July 2025) is the only non-Qwen grounding model, built on Phi-4-MM. Trained with SFT on 40M+ samples plus DPO, it achieves **55.0% on ScreenSpot-Pro** in an agent setting (paired with o4-mini as planner) and **43.2% end-to-end**. Designed for the Windows Copilot pipeline. Available via GitHub. Fits easily on 32GB.

**UI-Ins-7B / 32B** (Alibaba Tongyi, October 2025) uses an "Instruction-as-Reasoning" paradigm where the model analyzes grounding instructions from multiple perspectives. Trained with SFT + GRPO, the 7B achieves **74.1% success rate on AndroidWorld** when used as the grounding backbone for a larger agent system. The 7B is the practical choice for 32GB deployment.

**GUI-G²-3B / 7B** (Zhejiang University, August 2025 code / AAAI 2026 paper) applies GRPO with **Gaussian reward modeling** instead of binary point-in-box rewards — using Gaussian point reward, coverage reward, and adaptive variance. Improves over standard binary-reward GRPO on ScreenSpot-Pro and ScreenSpot-v2. Weights are on HuggingFace.

**ScreenVLM-316M** (IBM Research, February 2026) is an ultra-lightweight screen parsing model combining SigLIP-2 with a Granite-165M decoder. At just **316M parameters**, it produces structured markup (ScreenTag format) with bounding boxes, 55-class UI element types, and text for all visible elements. Designed for on-device/low-latency deployment. No confirmed HuggingFace release yet, but trivially fits any GPU.

---

## The GRPO training revolution for GUI grounding

DeepSeek-R1's popularization of GRPO in January 2025 triggered a wave of RL-trained grounding models. The Salesforce GTA1 team's "GRPO for GUI Grounding Done Right" blog crystallized key findings: **thinking tokens are not required** for static grounding (they can hurt), click-based binary rewards suffice, no SFT cold start is needed with strong base models, and KL regularization should be avoided for coordinate flexibility. Thinking *does* help in dynamic environments like AndroidWorld, where trajectory history matters.

For the **mobile/Android ADB use case** specifically, three models stand out among GRPO/RL-trained options:

- **AgentCPM-GUI-8B** uses a three-stage GRPO pipeline trained on 12M Android screenshots, specifically designed for Chinese + English mobile apps. It has the most complete Android-specific training.
- **AutoGLM-Phone-9B** uses WebRL (not GRPO per se, but online curriculum RL) and operates via WiFi-based device control with support for apps like Gmail, Google Maps, WeChat, and Taobao.
- **MAI-UI-8B** was trained with online RL in live Android environments scaled to 512 concurrent instances. Its **76.7% AndroidWorld** score (235B variant) represents the SOTA, though the locally-deployable 8B variant is also strong.

Additional RL-trained grounding models relevant to mobile include **GUI-ARP-7B** (adaptive multi-stage GRPO, SOTA among 7B on ScreenSpot-Pro), **MobileGUI-RL** (online GRPO with trajectory-aware advantages, ICLR 2026, weights not yet public), and **OmegaUse** (30B-A3B MoE, SFT+GRPO, 96.3% ScreenSpot-V2, weights not public).

---

## The OSWorld-Verified leaderboard as of March 2026

Human performance on OSWorld-Verified is estimated at **~72.4%**. Two proprietary models have now surpassed this threshold. The landscape since October 2025 has shifted dramatically:

| Rank | Model | Score | Type | Deployable on 32GB? |
|------|-------|-------|------|---------------------|
| 1 | GPT-5.4 | **75.0%** | Proprietary (Mar 2026) | No (API only) |
| 2 | Claude Opus 4.6 | **72.7%** | Proprietary (Feb 2026) | No (API only) |
| 3 | GPT-5.4 mini | **72.1%** | Proprietary (Mar 2026) | No (API only) |
| 4 | GPT-5.3 Codex | **64.7%** | Proprietary (Feb 2026) | No (API only) |
| 5 | Kimi K2.5 | **63.3%** | Open-weight MoE 1T/32B-active (Jan 2026) | No (~500GB INT4) |
| 6 | CoACT-1 | **60.8%** | Agentic framework (proprietary backbone) | No |
| 7 | Qwen3.5-122B-A10B | **58.0%** | Open-weight MoE (2026) | No (too large) |
| 8 | EvoCUA-32B | **56.7%** | Open-weight dense (Jan 2026) | **Yes, Q4** |
| 9 | Agent S2.5 + o3 | **56.0%** | Agentic framework | No (needs o3 API) |
| 10 | Qwen3.5-27B | **56.2%** | Open-weight dense (2026) | **Yes, Q4** |
| 11 | GTA1 + o3 | **53.1%** | Framework + proprietary planner | No (needs o3) |
| 12 | AutoGLM-OS-9B | **48.1%** | Dense 9B (ComputerRL, 2025) | Yes if released (not public) |
| 13 | UI-TARS-2 | **47.5%** | MoE 230B (ByteDance, Sep 2025) | No (not public, too large) |
| 14 | EvoCUA-8B | **46.1%** | Open-weight dense (Jan 2026) | **Yes, FP16** |
| 15 | OpenCUA-72B | **45.0%** | Open-weight dense (2025) | No (too large) |

**New entrants since October 2025** include: GPT-5.4 and variants, Claude Opus 4.6, Kimi K2.5, EvoCUA-8B/32B, Qwen3.5 family, and AutoGLM-OS. The open-weight 32GB-deployable frontier moved from ~38% (Qwen3-VL) to **56.7%** (EvoCUA-32B at Q4) in five months — a **19-point gain**. A critical caveat from Epoch AI: some OSWorld tasks can be completed via terminal commands or Python scripts without GUI interaction, so score differences partly reflect code capabilities rather than pure visual grounding.

---

## Notable models that exist but cannot run locally

**UI-TARS-2** (ByteDance, September 2025) is a **230B MoE** (23B active) with a 532M vision encoder, initialized from Seed-thinking-1.6. It scores 47.5% on OSWorld and 73.3% on AndroidWorld, but weights are **not publicly released** — only UI-TARS-1.5-7B is available. Even if released, the full model needs ~115GB at INT4.

**Kimi K2.5** (Moonshot AI, January 2026) is a **1.04T MoE** (384 experts, 8 active, 32B active parameters) released under Modified MIT license on HuggingFace. It scores **63.3% on OSWorld-Verified** and 92.3% on OCRBench. Despite being open-weight, it requires ~500GB+ even at INT4 for all expert weights. The INT4 QAT version is optimized for Hopper-class multi-GPU clusters.

**UltraCUA-7B/32B** (Apple Research, October 2025) bridges GUI actions with programmatic tool calls across 10 desktop domains. Scores 41.0% on OSWorld (32B). Weights are **not released** — research paper only.

---

## Deployment guide for RTX 5090 (32GB VRAM)

| Model | Params | Recommended Quant | VRAM Est. | HuggingFace | Best Benchmark |
|-------|--------|-------------------|-----------|-------------|----------------|
| **EvoCUA-8B** | 9B dense | FP16 (no quant needed) | ~18GB | `meituan/EvoCUA-8B-20260105` | OSWorld 46.1% |
| **EvoCUA-32B** | 32B dense | Q4_K_M (GGUF) | ~18GB | `meituan/EvoCUA-32B-20260105` | OSWorld 56.7% |
| **MAI-UI-8B** | 9B dense | FP16 or Q5 GGUF | ~17.6GB | `Tongyi-MAI/MAI-UI-8B` | SSPro 65.7% |
| **MAI-UI-2B** | 2B dense | FP16 | ~4GB | `Tongyi-MAI/MAI-UI-2B` | SSPro 57.4% |
| **UI-Venus 1.5-8B** | 8B dense | FP16 | ~16GB | `inclusionAI/UI-Venus-1.5-8B` | AndroidWorld 77.6% |
| **ScaleCUA-7B** | 7B dense | FP16 | ~14GB | `OpenGVLab/ScaleCUA-7B` | SSPro 59.2% (33B) |
| **AutoGLM-Phone-9B** | 9B dense | FP16 or Q4 GGUF | ~20.6GB / 6.2GB | `zai-org/AutoGLM-Phone-9B` | AndroidLab 36.2% |
| **AgentCPM-GUI-8B** | 8B dense | FP16 | ~16.2GB | `openbmb/AgentCPM-GUI` | CAGUI 96.9% |
| **POINTS-GUI-G-8B** | ~8B | FP16 | ~16GB | `tencent/POINTS-GUI-G` | OSWorld-G 66.0% |
| **Holo1.5-7B** | 7B dense | FP16 | ~14GB | `Hcompany/Holo1.5-7B` | SSPro 57.9% |
| **GUI-Actor-7B** | 7B + action head | FP16 | ~15GB | `microsoft/GUI-Actor-7B-Qwen2.5-VL` | SSPro 44.6% |
| **Phi-Ground-7B** | ~7B | FP16 | ~14GB | GitHub (microsoft) | SSPro 55.0% (agent) |
| **GUI-G²-7B** | 7B | FP16 | ~14GB | HuggingFace (ZJU) | SSPro improved |

For a **grounding + planner** stack on a single 32GB GPU: run a Q4-quantized grounding model (e.g., MAI-UI-8B at ~5GB GGUF) alongside a small reasoning model, or use a cloud API (o3, GPT-5) as the planner with a local grounding model as the executor. For a **single end-to-end agent**: EvoCUA-32B at Q4 gives the highest OSWorld score achievable on one consumer GPU.

---

## Conclusion

The October 2025 – March 2026 window marks the period when GUI agents crossed from research curiosity to practical capability. Three developments define this moment. First, **RL post-training became table stakes** — every competitive new model uses some form of GRPO, DPO, or online RL, often with self-evolving data pipelines that eliminate the need for human annotation at scale. Second, **Qwen-VL has become the de facto backbone**: of the 18 new models surveyed, 15 are built on Qwen2.5-VL or Qwen3-VL. The exceptions are AutoGLM-Phone (GLM-4), POINTS-GUI-G (custom POINTS-1.5), and Phi-Ground (Phi-4). Third, **the 7B–9B parameter class has become the sweet spot for local deployment** — models like EvoCUA-8B, MAI-UI-8B, and UI-Venus 1.5-8B now match or exceed what 72B models achieved six months ago, and all fit comfortably on a 32GB GPU at full precision.

For the ADB/Android automation use case specifically, the strongest locally-deployable option is **UI-Venus 1.5-8B** (77.6% AndroidWorld) or **MAI-UI-8B** (from the same ecosystem that produced the 76.7% AndroidWorld SOTA), both paired with either their own chain-of-thought reasoning or a cloud planner. For desktop OSWorld-class tasks, **EvoCUA-32B at Q4** represents the frontier of what a single RTX 5090 can run. The gap between this local deployment ceiling (56.7%) and frontier proprietary models (75.0%) remains substantial but is closing at roughly 3–4 points per month.
