## codex: can you write these in here to investigate?> # GUI...

can you write these in here to investigate?> # GUI agent models exploded between October 2025 and March 2026

**At least 18 new or significantly updated GUI agent and grounding models** shipped in the six months since October 2025, nearly all built atop Qwen2.5-VL or Qwen3-VL backbones. The field has bifurcated clearly: proprietary frontier models (GPT-5.4, Claude Opus 4.6) now exceed human performance on OSWorld-Verified at **75%** and **72.7%** respectively, while open-weight models deployable on a single RTX 5090 have crossed **56.7%** (EvoCUA-32B) — roughly where frontier proprietary models stood just six months ago. GRPO-style reinforcement learning has become the dominant post-training recipe for grounding models, and Alibaba's MAI-UI family has set new state-of-the-art scores on **ScreenSpot-Pro (73.5%)** and **AndroidWorld (76.7%)**. Every model listed below ships with public weights on HuggingFace unless noted otherwise, and every 7B–9B variant fits comfortably on a 32GB GPU at full precision.

---

## Full agent models you can deploy on 32GB VRAM

These models perform end-to-end planning and acting — they interpret a task, reason about the screen, and emit GUI actions (clicks, types, scrolls) without requiring a separate planner.

**EvoCUA-8B / 32B** (Meituan, January 2026) is the headline release for local deployment. Built on Qwen3-VL and trained with an iterative self-evolutionary loop — SFT cold start on ~1K trajectories, then rejection fine-tuning, then step-level DPO (STEPO), cycled repeatedly with a verifiable synthesis engine generating synthetic tasks — the 32B variant hit **56.7% on OSWorld-Verified**, making it the #1 open-source single-model result at time of release. The 8B variant scored **46.1%**, surpassing OpenCUA-72B (45.0%) despite being 9× smaller. Weights are on HuggingFace under Apache 2.0 (`meituan/EvoCUA-32B-20260105`, `meituan/EvoCUA-8B-20260105`). The 8B fits at FP16 in ~18GB; the 32B requires **Q4 quantization** (~18GB) to fit in 32GB, with an 8-bit MLX variant also available. Inference uses vLLM natively.

**MAI-UI-2B / 8B** (Alibaba Tongyi-MAI, December 2025 – January 2026) anchors the Alibaba GUI agent ecosystem. Based on Qwen3-VL, it introduced a self-evolving data pipeline plus online RL scaled to 512 parallel Android environments. The 8B model scores **65.7% on ScreenSpot-Pro** (best among all ≤8B models, open or closed) and **73.5%** is the score for the larger 32B variant. The full MAI-UI family extends to a 235B-A22B MoE that achieves **76.7% on AndroidWorld** and **91.3% on MMBench-GUI L2**, but only the 2B and 8B weights are publicly released (`Tongyi-MAI/MAI-UI-8B`, Apache 2.0). The 8B weighs **17.6GB** in FP16 — fits on 32GB with headroom. GGUF quantizations exist via community repos (Q4_K_M at 5GB).

**UI-Venus 1.5-2B / 8B / 30B-A3B** (Ant Group / inclusionAI, February 2026) followed a four-stage pipeline: mid-training, offline RL, online RL, and model merge. The 8B variant scores **69.6% on ScreenSpot-Pro** and **77.6% on AndroidWorld** — the latter representing the current single-model open-weight SOTA for mobile. A 30B-A3B MoE variant (30B total, 3B active) is also available. All weights are on HuggingFace (`inclusionAI/UI-Venus-1.5-8B`). The 8B fits at FP16; the MoE variant needs all expert weights loaded (~60GB FP16), so it requires **Q3 quantization** or offloading for 32GB.

**ScaleCUA-3B / 7B / 33B** (Shanghai AI Lab / OpenGVLab, January 2026) is trained on a massive cross-platform SFT dataset spanning six operating systems (Windows, macOS, Linux, Android, iOS, Web) with 471K GUI understanding samples and 17.1M grounding instances. It supports three inference modes: grounding-only, direct action, and reasoned action with chain-of-thought. The 33B scores **59.2% on ScreenSpot-Pro** and **60.6% on OSWorld-G**. Weights are Apache 2.0 (`OpenGVLab/ScaleCUA-33B`). The 7B fits easily; the 33B needs **Q4 quantization** for 32GB.

**AutoGLM-Phone-9B** (Zhipu AI, December 2025) targets mobile phone automation specifically. Built on GLM-4.1V-9B-Thinking (not a Qwen derivative), it was trained with WebRL — a self-evolving online curriculum RL method. It operates across Chinese and English mobile apps via WiFi-based device control, scoring **36.2% on AndroidLab** (surpassing GPT-4o and Claude). Weights plus a multilingual variant are available (`zai-org/AutoGLM-Phone-9B`, `zai-org/AutoGLM-Phone-9B-Multilingual`). At 20.6GB FP16, it fits on 32GB, with official GGUF quants from ggml-org (Q4_K_M at 6.17GB).

**GUI-Libra-3B / 4B / 7B / 8B** (Microsoft Research, February 2026) tackles a specific problem: chain-of-thought reasoning degrades grounding accuracy in GUI agents. Its fix is two-stage: action-aware SFT (ASFT) that reweights loss to emphasize action tokens, then KL-regularized GRPO that prevents the policy from drifting too far. The 4B (Qwen3-VL) and 8B (Qwen3-VL) variants beat GPT-4o on AndroidWorld and Online-Mind2Web. Code and training recipes are released on GitHub (`GUI-Libra/GUI-Libra`); HuggingFace model weights were not confirmed at time of research.

**AgentCPM-GUI-8B** (THUNLP / OpenBMB, initial May 2025, EMNLP November 2025) is notable as the first open-source GUI agent tuned for **30+ Chinese mobile apps** using a three-stage pipeline: grounding-aware pretraining on 12M bilingual Android screenshots, SFT on 55K Chinese+English trajectories, and GRPO fine-tuning. Achieves **96.9% Type-Match** on CAGUI. Weights are Apache 2.0 (`openbmb/AgentCPM-GUI`) at 16.2GB FP16 — fits on 32GB.

---

## Grounding-only models for coordinate prediction

These models take a screenshot and a natural-language instruction and return screen coordinates. They do not plan multi-step workflows — pair them with a reasoning model (o3, GPT-5, Claude) for full agent behavior.

**POINTS-GUI-G-8B** (Tencent WeChat AI, February 2026) stands out architecturally: it uses Tencent's custom POINTS-1.5 VLM (Qwen3 7B LLM + NaViT vision encoder), not a fine-tuned Qwen-VL. Trained with a three-pillar recipe — refined data engineering with difficulty grading, continuous vision encoder fine-tuning, and **RL with verifiable rewards** — it scores **59.9% on ScreenSpot-Pro** and **66.0% on OSWorld-G** (both SOTA among grounding-only models at release). Weights are on HuggingFace (`tencent/POINTS-GUI-G`) under a custom license. Fits at FP16 on 32GB.

**Holo1.5-3B / 7B / 72B** (H Company, France, September 2025) is a grounding and UI-VQA perception model fine-tuned from Qwen2.5-VL with SFT + GRPO. The 7B scores **57.94% on ScreenSpot-Pro** and supports resolutions up to 3840×2160. The 7B is Apache 2.0 (`Hcompany/Holo1.5-7B`); the 72B is CC-BY-NC-4.0. The 7B fits easily at FP16; the 72B does not fit on 32GB.

**GUI-Actor-2B / 3B / 7B** (Microsoft, NeurIPS 2025) introduced coordinate-free grounding via an attention-based `<ACTOR>` token — instead of generating coordinate text, it reads grounding locations from attention maps. The 7B (Qwen2.5-VL base) scores **44.6% on ScreenSpot-Pro**, surpassing UI-TARS-72B's baseline of 38.1%. Weights are available (`microsoft/GUI-Actor-7B-Qwen2.5-VL`). All sizes fit on 32GB.

**Phi-Ground-4B / 7B** (Microsoft, July 2025) is the only non-Qwen grounding model, built on Phi-4-MM. Trained with SFT on 40M+ samples plus DPO, it achieves **55.0% on ScreenSpot-Pro** in an agent setting (paired with o4-mini as planner) and **43.2% end-to-end**. Designed for the Windows Copilot pipeline. Available via GitHub. Fits easily on 32GB.

**UI-Ins-7B / 32B** (Alibaba Tongyi, October 2025) uses an "Instruction-as-Reasoning" paradigm where the model analyzes grounding instructions from multiple perspectives. Trained with SFT + GRPO, the 7B achieves **74.1% success rate on AndroidWorld** when used as the grounding backbone for a larger agent system. The 7B is the practical choice for 32GB deployment.

**GUI-G²-3B / 7B** (Zhejiang University, August 2025 code / AAAI 2026 paper) applies GRPO with **Gaussian reward modeling** instead of binary point-in-box rewards — using Gaussian point reward, coverage reward, and adaptive variance. Improves over standard binary-reward GRPO on ScreenSpot-Pro and ScreenSpot-v2. Weights are on HuggingFace.

**ScreenVLM-316M** (IBM Research, February 2026) is an ultra-lightweight screen parsing model combining SigLIP-2 with a Granite-165M decoder. At just **316M parameters**, it produces structured markup (ScreenTag format) with bounding boxes, 55-class UI element types, and text for all visible elements. Designed for on-device/low-latency deployment. No confirmed HuggingFace release yet, but trivially fits any GPU.

---

## The GRPO training revolution for GUI grounding

DeepSeek-R1's popularization of GRPO in January 2025 triggered a wave of RL-trained grounding models. The Salesforce GTA1 team's "GRPO for GUI Grounding Done Right" blog crystallized key findings: **thinking tokens are not required** for static grounding (they can hurt), click-based binary rewards suffice, no SFT cold start is needed with strong base models, and KL regularization should be avoided for coordinate flexibility. Thinking *does* help in dynamic environments like AndroidWorld, where trajectory history matters.

For the **mobile/Android ADB use case** specifically, three models stand out among GRPO/RL-trained options:

- **AgentCPM-GUI-8B** uses a three-stage GRPO pipeline trained on 12M Android screenshots, specifically designed for Chinese + English mobile apps. It has the most complete Android-specific training.
- **AutoGLM-Phone-9B** uses WebRL (not GRPO per se, but online curriculum RL) and operates via WiFi-based device control with support for apps like Gmail, Google Maps, WeChat, and Taobao.
- **MAI-UI-8B** was trained with online RL in live Android environments scaled to 512 concurrent instances. Its **76.7% AndroidWorld** score (235B variant) represents the SOTA, though the locally-deployable 8B variant is also strong.

Additional RL-trained grounding models relevant to mobile include **GUI-ARP-7B** (adaptive multi-stage GRPO, SOTA among 7B on ScreenSpot-Pro), **MobileGUI-RL** (online GRPO with trajectory-aware advantages, ICLR 2026, weights not yet public), and **OmegaUse** (30B-A3B MoE, SFT+GRPO, 96.3% ScreenSpot-V2, weights not public).

---

## The OSWorld-Verified leaderboard as of March 2026

Human performance on OSWorld-Verified is estimated at **~72.4%**. Two proprietary models have now surpassed this threshold. The landscape since October 2025 has shifted dramatically:

| Rank | Model | Score | Type | Deployable on 32GB? |
|------|-------|-------|------|---------------------|
| 1 | GPT-5.4 | **75.0%** | Proprietary (Mar 2026) | No (API only) |
| 2 | Claude Opus 4.6 | **72.7%** | Proprietary (Feb 2026) | No (API only) |
| 3 | GPT-5.4 mini | **72.1%** | Proprietary (Mar 2026) | No (API only) |
| 4 | GPT-5.3 Codex | **64.7%** | Proprietary (Feb 2026) | No (API only) |
| 5 | Kimi K2.5 | **63.3%** | Open-weight MoE 1T/32B-active (Jan 2026) | No (~500GB INT4) |
| 6 | CoACT-1 | **60.8%** | Agentic framework (proprietary backbone) | No |
| 7 | Qwen3.5-122B-A10B | **58.0%** | Open-weight MoE (2026) | No (too large) |
| 8 | EvoCUA-32B | **56.7%** | Open-weight dense (Jan 2026) | **Yes, Q4** |
| 9 | Agent S2.5 + o3 | **56.0%** | Agentic framework | No (needs o3 API) |
| 10 | Qwen3.5-27B | **56.2%** | Open-weight dense (2026) | **Yes, Q4** |
| 11 | GTA1 + o3 | **53.1%** | Framework + proprietary planner | No (needs o3) |
| 12 | AutoGLM-OS-9B | **48.1%** | Dense 9B (ComputerRL, 2025) | Yes if released (not public) |
| 13 | UI-TARS-2 | **47.5%** | MoE 230B (ByteDance, Sep 2025) | No (not public, too large) |
| 14 | EvoCUA-8B | **46.1%** | Open-weight dense (Jan 2026) | **Yes, FP16** |
| 15 | OpenCUA-72B | **45.0%** | Open-weight dense (2025) | No (too large) |

**New entrants since October 2025** include: GPT-5.4 and variants, Claude Opus 4.6, Kimi K2.5, EvoCUA-8B/32B, Qwen3.5 family, and AutoGLM-OS. The open-weight 32GB-deployable frontier moved from ~38% (Qwen3-VL) to **56.7%** (EvoCUA-32B at Q4) in five months — a **19-point gain**. A critical caveat from Epoch AI: some OSWorld tasks can be completed via terminal commands or Python scripts without GUI interaction, so score differences partly reflect code capabilities rather than pure visual grounding.

---

## Notable models that exist but cannot run locally

**UI-TARS-2** (ByteDance, September 2025) is a **230B MoE** (23B active) with a 532M vision encoder, initialized from Seed-thinking-1.6. It scores 47.5% on OSWorld and 73.3% on AndroidWorld, but weights are **not publicly released** — only UI-TARS-1.5-7B is available. Even if released, the full model needs ~115GB at INT4.

**Kimi K2.5** (Moonshot AI, January 2026) is a **1.04T MoE** (384 experts, 8 active, 32B active parameters) released under Modified MIT license on HuggingFace. It scores **63.3% on OSWorld-Verified** and 92.3% on OCRBench. Despite being open-weight, it requires ~500GB+ even at INT4 for all expert weights. The INT4 QAT version is optimized for Hopper-class multi-GPU clusters.

**UltraCUA-7B/32B** (Apple Research, October 2025) bridges GUI actions with programmatic tool calls across 10 desktop domains. Scores 41.0% on OSWorld (32B). Weights are **not released** — research paper only.

---

## Deployment guide for RTX 5090 (32GB VRAM)

| Model | Params | Recommended Quant | VRAM Est. | HuggingFace | Best Benchmark |
|-------|--------|-------------------|-----------|-------------|----------------|
| **EvoCUA-8B** | 9B dense | FP16 (no quant needed) | ~18GB | `meituan/EvoCUA-8B-20260105` | OSWorld 46.1% |
| **EvoCUA-32B** | 32B dense | Q4_K_M (GGUF) | ~18GB | `meituan/EvoCUA-32B-20260105` | OSWorld 56.7% |
| **MAI-UI-8B** | 9B dense | FP16 or Q5 GGUF | ~17.6GB | `Tongyi-MAI/MAI-UI-8B` | SSPro 65.7% |
| **MAI-UI-2B** | 2B dense | FP16 | ~4GB | `Tongyi-MAI/MAI-UI-2B` | SSPro 57.4% |
| **UI-Venus 1.5-8B** | 8B dense | FP16 | ~16GB | `inclusionAI/UI-Venus-1.5-8B` | AndroidWorld 77.6% |
| **ScaleCUA-7B** | 7B dense | FP16 | ~14GB | `OpenGVLab/ScaleCUA-7B` | SSPro 59.2% (33B) |
| **AutoGLM-Phone-9B** | 9B dense | FP16 or Q4 GGUF | ~20.6GB / 6.2GB | `zai-org/AutoGLM-Phone-9B` | AndroidLab 36.2% |
| **AgentCPM-GUI-8B** | 8B dense | FP16 | ~16.2GB | `openbmb/AgentCPM-GUI` | CAGUI 96.9% |
| **POINTS-GUI-G-8B** | ~8B | FP16 | ~16GB | `tencent/POINTS-GUI-G` | OSWorld-G 66.0% |
| **Holo1.5-7B** | 7B dense | FP16 | ~14GB | `Hcompany/Holo1.5-7B` | SSPro 57.9% |
| **GUI-Actor-7B** | 7B + action head | FP16 | ~15GB | `microsoft/GUI-Actor-7B-Qwen2.5-VL` | SSPro 44.6% |
| **Phi-Ground-7B** | ~7B | FP16 | ~14GB | GitHub (microsoft) | SSPro 55.0% (agent) |
| **GUI-G²-7B** | 7B | FP16 | ~14GB | HuggingFace (ZJU) | SSPro improved |

For a **grounding + planner** stack on a single 32GB GPU: run a Q4-quantized grounding model (e.g., MAI-UI-8B at ~5GB GGUF) alongside a small reasoning model, or use a cloud API (o3, GPT-5) as the planner with a local grounding model as the executor. For a **single end-to-end agent**: EvoCUA-32B at Q4 gives the highest OSWorld score achievable on one consumer GPU.

---

## Conclusion

The October 2025 – March 2026 window marks the period when GUI agents crossed from research curiosity to practical capability. Three developments define this moment. First, **RL post-training became table stakes** — every competitive new model uses some form of GRPO, DPO, or online RL, often with self-evolving data pipelines that eliminate the need for human annotation at scale. Second, **Qwen-VL has become the de facto backbone**: of the 18 new models surveyed, 15 are built on Qwen2.5-VL or Qwen3-VL. The exceptions are AutoGLM-Phone (GLM-4), POINTS-GUI-G (custom POINTS-1.5), and Phi-Ground (Phi-4). Third, **the 7B–9B parameter class has become the sweet spot for local deployment** — models like EvoCUA-8B, MAI-UI-8B, and UI-Venus 1.5-8B now match or exceed what 72B models achieved six months ago, and all fit comfortably on a 32GB GPU at full precision.

For the ADB/Android automation use case specifically, the strongest locally-deployable option is **UI-Venus 1.5-8B** (77.6% AndroidWorld) or **MAI-UI-8B** (from the same ecosystem that produced the 76.7% AndroidWorld SOTA), both paired with either their own chain-of-thought reasoning or a cloud planner. For desktop OSWorld-class tasks, **EvoCUA-32B at Q4** represents the frontier of what a single RTX 5090 can run. The gap between this local deployment ceiling (56.7%) and frontier proprietary models (75.0%) remains substantial but is closing at roughly 3–4 points per month.

  "插件安装在 ~/.kimi/plugins/ 目录下。" (Plugins are installed in the ~/.kimi/plugins/ directory.)

  And the installation command is:

  kimi plugin install /path/to/my-plugin

  So the correct path is ~/.kimi/plugins/, NOT ~/.kimi/tools/. The README in the project was from an older version.

  To install the Spark plugin:

  cd /mnt/d/_projects/kimi-codex-spark
  kimi plugin install .

  Or manually:

  mkdir -p ~/.kimi/plugins
  ln -s /mnt/d/_projects/kimi-codex-spark ~/.kimi/plugins/spark

  Then restart Kimi CLI. Want me to update the README and install script with the correct path?

## codex: try this test: can you run this test quickly? **Co...

try this test: can you run this test quickly? **Corrected approach with root:**

Don't use software rendering. Use **root access to bypass the composition layer entirely**.

With root on MEmu 9, read the framebuffer directly:

```bash
# Via minicap (recommended)
adb shell "su -c '/data/local/tmp/minicap -P 1920x1080@1920x1080/0 -s'" > frame.raw

# Or direct fb0 access (simpler, no minicap binary needed)
adb shell "su -c 'cat /dev/graphics/fb0'" > framebuffer.raw
# Then convert from RGBA/BGRA to PNG via Python
```

**Why this works:**
- Unity renders to OpenGL FBO  SurfaceFlinger composites  `/dev/graphics/fb0` contains final pixels
- Hardware encoders (OMX/c2) sometimes read from a different buffer that misses the GL composition
- Reading `fb0` directly gets the actual displayed pixels, bypassing encoder black frame issues
- No software rendering tax (full 60 FPS possible)

**The "Search and Drill Down" Strategy:**

Since you have root, implement **dual transport**:

```python
class MEmuRootTransport:
    def __init__(self):
        self.method_priority = ["minicap", "fb0_direct", "scrcpy_hw"]
        
    def capture(self):
        # Try minicap first (fastest, socket-based streaming)
        if self.minicap_available:
            return self.minicap.capture()
            
        # Fallback to fb0 direct read (50-100ms, single frame)
        return self.read_fb0()
        
    def read_fb0(self):
        # adb shell su -c 'cat /dev/graphics/fb0'
        # Parse based on MEmu's reported bits_per_pixel and resolution
        pass
```

**Critical:** MEmu 9 reports framebuffer info via:
```bash
adb shell "su -c 'cat /sys/class/graphics/fb0/virtual_size'"
adb shell "su -c 'cat /sys/class/graphics/fb0/bits_per_pixel'"
```

Usually: `1920x1080, 32bpp` (RGBA or BGRA depending on driver).

**Verification:**
```bash
adb shell "su -c 'dd if=/dev/graphics/fb0 of=/sdcard/frame.raw bs=8294400 count=1'"
adb pull /sdcard/frame.raw
# In Python: np.frombuffer(raw, dtype=np.uint8).reshape(1080, 1920, 4)
```

Does this actually produce non-black frames on your Azur Lane instance? If yes, this is the correct path.

**The working transport for your MEmu 9 instance:**

```python
# transport/memu_root_fb0.py
import subprocess
import numpy as np
from PIL import Image
import io

class MEmuRootFB0:
    """
    Verified transport for MEmu 9 + Azur Lane.
    - Device: 127.0.0.1:21513
    - fb0: 1152x864, 32bpp, stride 4608 (driver: hyperv_fb)
    - Requires: adb root (not su)
    - Method: dd to /sdcard (adb exec-out cat is unreliable/truncated)
    """
    
    def __init__(self, 
                 host: str = "127.0.0.1", 
                 port: int = 21513,
                 width: int = 1152,
                 height: int = 864,
                 bpp: int = 32):
        self.serial = f"{host}:{port}"
        self.width = width
        self.height = height
        self.stride = width * (bpp // 8)  # 4608 bytes
        self.frame_size = self.stride * height  # 3,981,312 bytes
        
    def ensure_root(self):
        """Ensure adb is in root mode for this session."""
        subprocess.run(["adb", "-s", self.serial, "root"], check=True)
        
    def capture(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """
        Capture single frame from fb0.
        Returns: RGB numpy array (H, W, 3)
        """
        # 1. dd to sdcard (reliable, exec-out cat truncates)
        remote_path = "/sdcard/fb0_capture.raw"
        dd_cmd = [
            "adb", "-s", self.serial, "shell",
            f"dd if=/dev/graphics/fb0 of={remote_path} bs={self.frame_size} count=1"
        ]
        subprocess.run(dd_cmd, check=True, capture_output=True)
        
        # 2. Pull to local
        result = subprocess.run(
            ["adb", "-s", self.serial, "exec-out", "cat", remote_path],
            capture_output=True,
            check=True
        )
        
        # 3. Decode BGRA (fb0 is typically BGRA on Android/emulators)
        raw = result.stdout
        if len(raw) != self.frame_size:
            raise RuntimeError(f"Truncated frame: got {len(raw)}, expected {self.frame_size}")
            
        # Reshape with stride (1152x864, 4 channels BGRA)
        bgra = np.frombuffer(raw, dtype=np.uint8).reshape(self.height, self.width, 4)
        
        # Drop alpha, convert BGR to RGB
        rgb = bgra[:, :, [2, 1, 0]]  # BGR -> RGB
        
        return rgb
        
    def to_pil(self, rgb_array: np.ndarray) -> Image.Image:
        """Convert numpy RGB to PIL for VLM consumption."""
        return Image.fromarray(rgb_array, mode='RGB')
```

**Key implementation details for your scaffold:**

1. **Resolution is 1152x864** (not 1920x1080). The VLM must know this for coordinate normalization. Normalized `x=0.5` = pixel 576, `y=0.5` = pixel 432.

2. **BGRA byte order** (not RGBA). The fb0 is 32bpp with Alpha channel that you drop.

3. **adb root session management:**
   ```python
   def start_session(self):
       subprocess.run(["adb", "-s", self.serial, "root"], check=True)
       # Verify Azur Lane is focused
       result = subprocess.run(
           ["adb", "-s", self.serial, "shell", "dumpsys", "window", "windows", "|", "grep", "mCurrentFocus"],
           capture_output=True, text=True
       )
       if "com.YoStarEN.AzurLane" not in result.stdout:
           raise RuntimeError("Azur Lane not focused")
   ```

4. **Performance:** `dd` + `adb pull` is ~100-150ms per frame. For 30 FPS streaming, you'd need to keep the pipe open or use a background `dd` loop writing to a rotating buffer. But for the automation loop (action  capture  verify), 150ms is acceptable.

**Does this transport implementation match your verified setup?**

## VERIFIED TRANSPORT IMPLEMENTATION (MEmu 9 + fb0)

```python
# runtime/transport/memu_fb0.py
import subprocess
import numpy as np
from PIL import Image
import tempfile
import os

class MEmuFB0Transport:
    """
    VERIFIED transport for MEmu 9 Azur Lane.
    
    Confirmed working:
    - Device: 127.0.0.1:21513
    - fb0: 1152x864, 32bpp, stride 4608, driver hyperv_fb
    - Method: adb root  dd to /sdcard  adb pull (NOT exec-out cat, truncates)
    - adb root works; su does not exist on this image
    """
    
    def __init__(self,
                 host: str = "127.0.0.1",
                 port: int = 21513,
                 width: int = 1152,
                 height: int = 864,
                 bpp: int = 32):
        self.serial = f"{host}:{port}"
        self.width = width
        self.height = height
        self.stride = width * (bpp // 8)  # 4608
        self.frame_size = self.stride * height  # 3,981,312 bytes
        
    def ensure_root(self):
        """Enable adb root and wait for device to reconnect."""
        subprocess.run(["adb", "-s", self.serial, "root"], check=True)
        # CRITICAL: adbd restarts after root, must wait
        subprocess.run(["adb", "-s", self.serial, "wait-for-device"], check=True)
        
    def verify_focus(self) -> bool:
        """Check if Azur Lane is focused. Returns False if not."""
        # NOTE: No shell pipes in subprocess. Parse in Python.
        result = subprocess.run(
            ["adb", "-s", self.serial, "shell", "dumpsys", "window", "windows"],
            capture_output=True, text=True, check=True
        )
        # Parse output for mCurrentFocus
        for line in result.stdout.splitlines():
            if "mCurrentFocus" in line or "mFocusedApp" in line:
                return "com.YoStarEN.AzurLane" in line
        return False
        
    def capture(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """
        Capture frame from fb0.
        Returns: RGB numpy array (H, W, 3) uint8
        
        Raises:
            RuntimeError: if frame size mismatch or decode fails
        """
        # 1. Ensure root session
        self.ensure_root()
        
        # 2. Capture to device storage (reliable path)
        remote_path = "/sdcard/fb0_capture.raw"
        subprocess.run([
            "adb", "-s", self.serial, "shell",
            f"dd if=/dev/graphics/fb0 of={remote_path} bs={self.frame_size} count=1"
        ], check=True, capture_output=True)
        
        # 3. Pull to local temp file (verified reliable, exec-out cat truncates)
        with tempfile.NamedTemporaryFile(suffix=".raw", delete=False) as tmp:
            local_path = tmp.name
            
        try:
            subprocess.run([
                "adb", "-s", self.serial, "pull", remote_path, local_path
            ], check=True, capture_output=True)
            
            # 4. Read and validate size
            with open(local_path, "rb") as f:
                raw = f.read()
                
            if len(raw) != self.frame_size:
                raise RuntimeError(
                    f"Frame size mismatch: got {len(raw)}, expected {self.frame_size}"
                )
                
            # 5. Decode (CHANNEL ORDER TO BE VALIDATED - see below)
            # TODO: Validate BGRA vs RGBA against known screenshot
            # Current assumption: BGRA based on Android convention
            bgra = np.frombuffer(raw, dtype=np.uint8).reshape(self.height, self.width, 4)
            
            # Convert BGRA to RGB (drop alpha)
            rgb = bgra[:, :, [2, 1, 0]]
            
            return rgb
            
        finally:
            os.unlink(local_path)
            
    def to_pil(self, rgb_array: np.ndarray) -> Image.Image:
        """Convert numpy RGB to PIL Image for VLM input."""
        return Image.fromarray(rgb_array, mode='RGB')
        
    def get_screen_dimensions(self) -> tuple[int, int]:
        """Return actual pixel dimensions for coordinate normalization."""
        return (self.width, self.height)
```

## CRITICAL VALIDATION TODO (Agent Must Complete)

**Channel Order Verification:**
The implementation assumes **BGRA** (Android standard), but this must be validated:

```python
# validation script for agent to run
def validate_channel_order(transport: MEmuFB0Transport):
    """
    Capture known UI state (e.g., main menu with red notification badge).
    Check if decoded colors match expected (red should be R high, G low, B low).
    If colors appear swapped (cyan instead of red), change decode order.
    """
    rgb = transport.capture()
    pil = transport.to_pil(rgb)
    pil.save("validation_screenshot.png")
    
    # Manual check: Does this look like the actual Azur Lane screen?
    # If blue/orange tint: try RGBA order instead of BGRA
    # If correct: BGRA confirmed
```

## VERIFIED TRANSPORT IMPLEMENTATION (MEmu 9 + fb0)

```python
# runtime/transport/memu_fb0.py
import subprocess
import numpy as np
from PIL import Image
import tempfile
import os

class MEmuFB0Transport:
    """
    VERIFIED transport for MEmu 9 Azur Lane.
    
    Confirmed working:
    - Device: 127.0.0.1:21513
    - fb0: 1152x864, 32bpp, stride 4608, driver hyperv_fb
    - Method: adb root  dd to /sdcard  adb pull (NOT exec-out cat, truncates)
    - adb root works; su does not exist on this image
    """
    
    def __init__(self,
                 host: str = "127.0.0.1",
                 port: int = 21513,
                 width: int = 1152,
                 height: int = 864,
                 bpp: int = 32):
        self.serial = f"{host}:{port}"
        self.width = width
        self.height = height
        self.stride = width * (bpp // 8)  # 4608
        self.frame_size = self.stride * height  # 3,981,312 bytes
        
    def ensure_root(self):
        """Enable adb root and wait for device to reconnect."""
        subprocess.run(["adb", "-s", self.serial, "root"], check=True)
        # CRITICAL: adbd restarts after root, must wait
        subprocess.run(["adb", "-s", self.serial, "wait-for-device"], check=True)
        
    def verify_focus(self) -> bool:
        """Check if Azur Lane is focused. Returns False if not."""
        # NOTE: No shell pipes in subprocess. Parse in Python.
        result = subprocess.run(
            ["adb", "-s", self.serial, "shell", "dumpsys", "window", "windows"],
            capture_output=True, text=True, check=True
        )
        # Parse output for mCurrentFocus
        for line in result.stdout.splitlines():
            if "mCurrentFocus" in line or "mFocusedApp" in line:
                return "com.YoStarEN.AzurLane" in line
        return False
        
    def capture(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """
        Capture frame from fb0.
        Returns: RGB numpy array (H, W, 3) uint8
        
        Raises:
            RuntimeError: if frame size mismatch or decode fails
        """
        # 1. Ensure root session
        self.ensure_root()
        
        # 2. Capture to device storage (reliable path)
        remote_path = "/sdcard/fb0_capture.raw"
        subprocess.run([
            "adb", "-s", self.serial, "shell",
            f"dd if=/dev/graphics/fb0 of={remote_path} bs={self.frame_size} count=1"
        ], check=True, capture_output=True)
        
        # 3. Pull to local temp file (verified reliable, exec-out cat truncates)
        with tempfile.NamedTemporaryFile(suffix=".raw", delete=False) as tmp:
            local_path = tmp.name
            
        try:
            subprocess.run([
                "adb", "-s", self.serial, "pull", remote_path, local_path
            ], check=True, capture_output=True)
            
            # 4. Read and validate size
            with open(local_path, "rb") as f:
                raw = f.read()
                
            if len(raw) != self.frame_size:
                raise RuntimeError(
                    f"Frame size mismatch: got {len(raw)}, expected {self.frame_size}"
                )
                
            # 5. Decode (CHANNEL ORDER TO BE VALIDATED - see below)
            # TODO: Validate BGRA vs RGBA against known screenshot
            # Current assumption: BGRA based on Android convention
            bgra = np.frombuffer(raw, dtype=np.uint8).reshape(self.height, self.width, 4)
            
            # Convert BGRA to RGB (drop alpha)
            rgb = bgra[:, :, [2, 1, 0]]
            
            return rgb
            
        finally:
            os.unlink(local_path)
            
    def to_pil(self, rgb_array: np.ndarray) -> Image.Image:
        """Convert numpy RGB to PIL Image for VLM input."""
        return Image.fromarray(rgb_array, mode='RGB')
        
    def get_screen_dimensions(self) -> tuple[int, int]:
        """Return actual pixel dimensions for coordinate normalization."""
        return (self.width, self.height)
```

## codex: try this test: can you run this test quickly? **Co...

try this test: can you run this test quickly? **Corrected approach with root:**

Don't use software rendering. Use **root access to bypass the composition layer entirely**.

With root on MEmu 9, read the framebuffer directly:

```bash
# Via minicap (recommended)
adb shell "su -c '/data/local/tmp/minicap -P 1920x1080@1920x1080/0 -s'" > frame.raw

# Or direct fb0 access (simpler, no minicap binary needed)
adb shell "su -c 'cat /dev/graphics/fb0'" > framebuffer.raw
# Then convert from RGBA/BGRA to PNG via Python
```

**Why this works:**
- Unity renders to OpenGL FBO  SurfaceFlinger composites  `/dev/graphics/fb0` contains final pixels
- Hardware encoders (OMX/c2) sometimes read from a different buffer that misses the GL composition
- Reading `fb0` directly gets the actual displayed pixels, bypassing encoder black frame issues
- No software rendering tax (full 60 FPS possible)

**The "Search and Drill Down" Strategy:**

Since you have root, implement **dual transport**:

```python
class MEmuRootTransport:
    def __init__(self):
        self.method_priority = ["minicap", "fb0_direct", "scrcpy_hw"]
        
    def capture(self):
        # Try minicap first (fastest, socket-based streaming)
        if self.minicap_available:
            return self.minicap.capture()
            
        # Fallback to fb0 direct read (50-100ms, single frame)
        return self.read_fb0()
        
    def read_fb0(self):
        # adb shell su -c 'cat /dev/graphics/fb0'
        # Parse based on MEmu's reported bits_per_pixel and resolution
        pass
```

**Critical:** MEmu 9 reports framebuffer info via:
```bash
adb shell "su -c 'cat /sys/class/graphics/fb0/virtual_size'"
adb shell "su -c 'cat /sys/class/graphics/fb0/bits_per_pixel'"
```

Usually: `1920x1080, 32bpp` (RGBA or BGRA depending on driver).

**Verification:**
```bash
adb shell "su -c 'dd if=/dev/graphics/fb0 of=/sdcard/frame.raw bs=8294400 count=1'"
adb pull /sdcard/frame.raw
# In Python: np.frombuffer(raw, dtype=np.uint8).reshape(1080, 1920, 4)
```

Does this actually produce non-black frames on your Azur Lane instance? If yes, this is the correct path.

**The working transport for your MEmu 9 instance:**

```python
# transport/memu_root_fb0.py
import subprocess
import numpy as np
from PIL import Image
import io

class MEmuRootFB0:
    """
    Verified transport for MEmu 9 + Azur Lane.
    - Device: 127.0.0.1:21513
    - fb0: 1152x864, 32bpp, stride 4608 (driver: hyperv_fb)
    - Requires: adb root (not su)
    - Method: dd to /sdcard (adb exec-out cat is unreliable/truncated)
    """
    
    def __init__(self, 
                 host: str = "127.0.0.1", 
                 port: int = 21513,
                 width: int = 1152,
                 height: int = 864,
                 bpp: int = 32):
        self.serial = f"{host}:{port}"
        self.width = width
        self.height = height
        self.stride = width * (bpp // 8)  # 4608 bytes
        self.frame_size = self.stride * height  # 3,981,312 bytes
        
    def ensure_root(self):
        """Ensure adb is in root mode for this session."""
        subprocess.run(["adb", "-s", self.serial, "root"], check=True)
        
    def capture(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """
        Capture single frame from fb0.
        Returns: RGB numpy array (H, W, 3)
        """
        # 1. dd to sdcard (reliable, exec-out cat truncates)
        remote_path = "/sdcard/fb0_capture.raw"
        dd_cmd = [
            "adb", "-s", self.serial, "shell",
            f"dd if=/dev/graphics/fb0 of={remote_path} bs={self.frame_size} count=1"
        ]
        subprocess.run(dd_cmd, check=True, capture_output=True)
        
        # 2. Pull to local
        result = subprocess.run(
            ["adb", "-s", self.serial, "exec-out", "cat", remote_path],
            capture_output=True,
            check=True
        )
        
        # 3. Decode BGRA (fb0 is typically BGRA on Android/emulators)
        raw = result.stdout
        if len(raw) != self.frame_size:
            raise RuntimeError(f"Truncated frame: got {len(raw)}, expected {self.frame_size}")
            
        # Reshape with stride (1152x864, 4 channels BGRA)
        bgra = np.frombuffer(raw, dtype=np.uint8).reshape(self.height, self.width, 4)
        
        # Drop alpha, convert BGR to RGB
        rgb = bgra[:, :, [2, 1, 0]]  # BGR -> RGB
        
        return rgb
        
    def to_pil(self, rgb_array: np.ndarray) -> Image.Image:
        """Convert numpy RGB to PIL for VLM consumption."""
        return Image.fromarray(rgb_array, mode='RGB')
```

**Key implementation details for your scaffold:**

1. **Resolution is 1152x864** (not 1920x1080). The VLM must know this for coordinate normalization. Normalized `x=0.5` = pixel 576, `y=0.5` = pixel 432.

2. **BGRA byte order** (not RGBA). The fb0 is 32bpp with Alpha channel that you drop.

3. **adb root session management:**
   ```python
   def start_session(self):
       subprocess.run(["adb", "-s", self.serial, "root"], check=True)
       # Verify Azur Lane is focused
       result = subprocess.run(
           ["adb", "-s", self.serial, "shell", "dumpsys", "window", "windows", "|", "grep", "mCurrentFocus"],
           capture_output=True, text=True
       )
       if "com.YoStarEN.AzurLane" not in result.stdout:
           raise RuntimeError("Azur Lane not focused")
   ```

4. **Performance:** `dd` + `adb pull` is ~100-150ms per frame. For 30 FPS streaming, you'd need to keep the pipe open or use a background `dd` loop writing to a rotating buffer. But for the automation loop (action  capture  verify), 150ms is acceptable.

**Does this transport implementation match your verified setup?**

## VERIFIED TRANSPORT IMPLEMENTATION (MEmu 9 + fb0)

```python
# runtime/transport/memu_fb0.py
import subprocess
import numpy as np
from PIL import Image
import tempfile
import os

class MEmuFB0Transport:
    """
    VERIFIED transport for MEmu 9 Azur Lane.
    
    Confirmed working:
    - Device: 127.0.0.1:21513
    - fb0: 1152x864, 32bpp, stride 4608, driver hyperv_fb
    - Method: adb root  dd to /sdcard  adb pull (NOT exec-out cat, truncates)
    - adb root works; su does not exist on this image
    """
    
    def __init__(self,
                 host: str = "127.0.0.1",
                 port: int = 21513,
                 width: int = 1152,
                 height: int = 864,
                 bpp: int = 32):
        self.serial = f"{host}:{port}"
        self.width = width
        self.height = height
        self.stride = width * (bpp // 8)  # 4608
        self.frame_size = self.stride * height  # 3,981,312 bytes
        
    def ensure_root(self):
        """Enable adb root and wait for device to reconnect."""
        subprocess.run(["adb", "-s", self.serial, "root"], check=True)
        # CRITICAL: adbd restarts after root, must wait
        subprocess.run(["adb", "-s", self.serial, "wait-for-device"], check=True)
        
    def verify_focus(self) -> bool:
        """Check if Azur Lane is focused. Returns False if not."""
        # NOTE: No shell pipes in subprocess. Parse in Python.
        result = subprocess.run(
            ["adb", "-s", self.serial, "shell", "dumpsys", "window", "windows"],
            capture_output=True, text=True, check=True
        )
        # Parse output for mCurrentFocus
        for line in result.stdout.splitlines():
            if "mCurrentFocus" in line or "mFocusedApp" in line:
                return "com.YoStarEN.AzurLane" in line
        return False
        
    def capture(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """
        Capture frame from fb0.
        Returns: RGB numpy array (H, W, 3) uint8
        
        Raises:
            RuntimeError: if frame size mismatch or decode fails
        """
        # 1. Ensure root session
        self.ensure_root()
        
        # 2. Capture to device storage (reliable path)
        remote_path = "/sdcard/fb0_capture.raw"
        subprocess.run([
            "adb", "-s", self.serial, "shell",
            f"dd if=/dev/graphics/fb0 of={remote_path} bs={self.frame_size} count=1"
        ], check=True, capture_output=True)
        
        # 3. Pull to local temp file (verified reliable, exec-out cat truncates)
        with tempfile.NamedTemporaryFile(suffix=".raw", delete=False) as tmp:
            local_path = tmp.name
            
        try:
            subprocess.run([
                "adb", "-s", self.serial, "pull", remote_path, local_path
            ], check=True, capture_output=True)
            
            # 4. Read and validate size
            with open(local_path, "rb") as f:
                raw = f.read()
                
            if len(raw) != self.frame_size:
                raise RuntimeError(
                    f"Frame size mismatch: got {len(raw)}, expected {self.frame_size}"
                )
                
            # 5. Decode (CHANNEL ORDER TO BE VALIDATED - see below)
            # TODO: Validate BGRA vs RGBA against known screenshot
            # Current assumption: BGRA based on Android convention
            bgra = np.frombuffer(raw, dtype=np.uint8).reshape(self.height, self.width, 4)
            
            # Convert BGRA to RGB (drop alpha)
            rgb = bgra[:, :, [2, 1, 0]]
            
            return rgb
            
        finally:
            os.unlink(local_path)
            
    def to_pil(self, rgb_array: np.ndarray) -> Image.Image:
        """Convert numpy RGB to PIL Image for VLM input."""
        return Image.fromarray(rgb_array, mode='RGB')
        
    def get_screen_dimensions(self) -> tuple[int, int]:
        """Return actual pixel dimensions for coordinate normalization."""
        return (self.width, self.height)
```

## VERIFIED TRANSPORT IMPLEMENTATION (MEmu 9 + fb0)

```python
# runtime/transport/memu_fb0.py
import subprocess
import numpy as np
from PIL import Image
import tempfile
import os

class MEmuFB0Transport:
    """
    VERIFIED transport for MEmu 9 Azur Lane.
    
    Confirmed working:
    - Device: 127.0.0.1:21513
    - fb0: 1152x864, 32bpp, stride 4608, driver hyperv_fb
    - Method: adb root  dd to /sdcard  adb pull (NOT exec-out cat, truncates)
    - adb root works; su does not exist on this image
    """
    
    def __init__(self,
                 host: str = "127.0.0.1",
                 port: int = 21513,
                 width: int = 1152,
                 height: int = 864,
                 bpp: int = 32):
        self.serial = f"{host}:{port}"
        self.width = width
        self.height = height
        self.stride = width * (bpp // 8)  # 4608
        self.frame_size = self.stride * height  # 3,981,312 bytes
        
    def ensure_root(self):
        """Enable adb root and wait for device to reconnect."""
        subprocess.run(["adb", "-s", self.serial, "root"], check=True)
        # CRITICAL: adbd restarts after root, must wait
        subprocess.run(["adb", "-s", self.serial, "wait-for-device"], check=True)
        
    def verify_focus(self) -> bool:
        """Check if Azur Lane is focused. Returns False if not."""
        # NOTE: No shell pipes in subprocess. Parse in Python.
        result = subprocess.run(
            ["adb", "-s", self.serial, "shell", "dumpsys", "window", "windows"],
            capture_output=True, text=True, check=True
        )
        # Parse output for mCurrentFocus
        for line in result.stdout.splitlines():
            if "mCurrentFocus" in line or "mFocusedApp" in line:
                return "com.YoStarEN.AzurLane" in line
        return False
        
    def capture(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """
        Capture frame from fb0.
        Returns: RGB numpy array (H, W, 3) uint8
        
        Raises:
            RuntimeError: if frame size mismatch or decode fails
        """
        # 1. Ensure root session
        self.ensure_root()
        
        # 2. Capture to device storage (reliable path)
        remote_path = "/sdcard/fb0_capture.raw"
        subprocess.run([
            "adb", "-s", self.serial, "shell",
            f"dd if=/dev/graphics/fb0 of={remote_path} bs={self.frame_size} count=1"
        ], check=True, capture_output=True)
        
        # 3. Pull to local temp file (verified reliable, exec-out cat truncates)
        with tempfile.NamedTemporaryFile(suffix=".raw", delete=False) as tmp:
            local_path = tmp.name
            
        try:
            subprocess.run([
                "adb", "-s", self.serial, "pull", remote_path, local_path
            ], check=True, capture_output=True)
            
            # 4. Read and validate size
            with open(local_path, "rb") as f:
                raw = f.read()
                
            if len(raw) != self.frame_size:
                raise RuntimeError(
                    f"Frame size mismatch: got {len(raw)}, expected {self.frame_size}"
                )
                
            # 5. Decode (CHANNEL ORDER TO BE VALIDATED - see below)
            # TODO: Validate BGRA vs RGBA against known screenshot
            # Current assumption: BGRA based on Android convention
            bgra = np.frombuffer(raw, dtype=np.uint8).reshape(self.height, self.width, 4)
            
            # Convert BGRA to RGB (drop alpha)
            rgb = bgra[:, :, [2, 1, 0]]
            
            return rgb
            
        finally:
            os.unlink(local_path)
            
    def to_pil(self, rgb_array: np.ndarray) -> Image.Image:
        """Convert numpy RGB to PIL Image for VLM input."""
        return Image.fromarray(rgb_array, mode='RGB')
        
    def get_screen_dimensions(self) -> tuple[int, int]:
        """Return actual pixel dimensions for coordinate normalization."""
        return (self.width, self.height)
```

The implementation assumes **BGRA** (Android standard), but this must be validated:

```python
# validation script for agent to run
def validate_channel_order(transport: MEmuFB0Transport):
    """
    Capture known UI state (e.g., main menu with red notification badge).
    Check if decoded colors match expected (red should be R high, G low, B low).
    If colors appear swapped (cyan instead of red), change decode order.
    """
    rgb = transport.capture()
    pil = transport.to_pil(rgb)
    pil.save("validation_screenshot.png")
    
    # Manual check: Does this look like the actual Azur Lane screen?
    # If blue/orange tint: try RGBA order instead of BGRA
    # If correct: BGRA confirmed
```

## codex: ## Code review guidelines:

## Code review guidelines:
# Review guidelines:

You are acting as a reviewer for a proposed code change made by another engineer.

Below are some default guidelines for determining whether the original author would appreciate the issue being flagged.

These are not the final word in determining whether an issue is a bug. In many cases, you will encounter other, more specific guidelines. These may be present elsewhere in a developer message, a user message, a file, or even elsewhere in this system message.
Those guidelines should be considered to override these general instructions.

Here are the general guidelines for determining whether something is a bug and should be flagged.

1. It meaningfully impacts the accuracy, performance, security, or maintainability of the code.
2. The bug is discrete and actionable (i.e. not a general issue with the codebase or a combination of multiple issues).
3. Fixing the bug does not demand a level of rigor that is not present in the rest of the codebase (e.g. one doesn't need very detailed comments and input validation in a repository of one-off scripts in personal projects)
4. The bug was introduced in the commit (pre-existing bugs should not be flagged).
5. The author of the original PR would likely fix the issue if they were made aware of it.
6. The bug does not rely on unstated assumptions about the codebase or author's intent.
7. It is not enough to speculate that a change may disrupt another part of the codebase, to be considered a bug, one must identify the other parts of the code that are provably affected.
8. The bug is clearly not just an intentional change by the original author.

When flagging a bug, you will also provide an accompanying comment. Once again, these guidelines are not the final word on how to construct a comment -- defer to any subsequent guidelines that you encounter.

1. The comment should be clear about why the issue is a bug.
2. The comment should appropriately communicate the severity of the issue. It should not claim that an issue is more severe than it actually is.
3. The comment should be brief. The body should be at most 1 paragraph. It should not introduce line breaks within the natural language flow unless it is necessary for the code fragment.
4. The comment should not include any chunks of code longer than 3 lines. Any code chunks should be wrapped in markdown inline code tags or a code block.
5. The comment should clearly and explicitly communicate the scenarios, environments, or inputs that are necessary for the bug to arise. The comment should immediately indicate that the issue's severity depends on these factors.
6. The comment's tone should be matter-of-fact and not accusatory or overly positive. It should read as a helpful AI assistant suggestion without sounding too much like a human reviewer.
7. The comment should be written such that the original author can immediately grasp the idea without close reading.
8. The comment should avoid excessive flattery and comments that are not helpful to the original author. The comment should avoid phrasing like "Great job ...", "Thanks for ...".

Below are some more detailed guidelines that you should apply to this specific review.

HOW MANY FINDINGS TO RETURN:

Output all findings that the original author would fix if they knew about it. If there is no finding that a person would definitely love to see and fix, prefer outputting no findings. Do not stop at the first qualifying finding. Continue until you've listed every qualifying finding.

GUIDELINES:

- Ignore trivial style unless it obscures meaning or violates documented standards.
- Use one comment per distinct issue (or a multi-line range if necessary).
- Use ```suggestion blocks ONLY for concrete replacement code (minimal lines; no commentary inside the block).
- In every ```suggestion block, preserve the exact leading whitespace of the replaced lines (spaces vs tabs, number of spaces).
- Do NOT introduce or remove outer indentation levels unless that is the actual fix.

The comments will be presented in the code review as inline comments. You should avoid providing unnecessary location details in the comment body. Always keep the line range as short as possible for interpreting the issue. Avoid ranges longer than 5–10 lines; instead, choose the most suitable subrange that pinpoints the problem.

At the beginning of the finding title, tag the bug with priority level. For example "[P1] Un-padding slices along wrong tensor dimensions". [P0] – Drop everything to fix. Blocking release, operations, or major usage. Only use for universal issues that do not depend on any assumptions about the inputs. · [P1] – Urgent. Should be addressed in the next cycle · [P2] – Normal. To be fixed eventually · [P3] – Low. Nice to have.

Additionally, include a numeric priority field in the JSON output for each finding: set "priority" to 0 for P0, 1 for P1, 2 for P2, or 3 for P3. If a priority cannot be determined, omit the field or use null.

At the end of your findings, output an "overall correctness" verdict of whether or not the patch should be considered "correct".
Correct implies that existing code and tests will not break, and the patch is free of bugs and other blocking issues.
Ignore non-blocking issues such as style, formatting, typos, documentation, and other nits.

FORMATTING GUIDELINES:
The finding description should be one paragraph.

OUTPUT FORMAT:

## Output schema — MUST MATCH _exactly_

```json
{
  "findings": [
    {
      "title": "<≤ 80 chars, imperative>",
      "body": "<valid Markdown explaining *why* this is a problem; cite files/lines/functions>",
      "confidence_score": <float 0.0-1.0>,
      "priority": <int 0-3, optional>,
      "code_location": {
        "absolute_file_path": "<file path>",
        "line_range": {"start": <int>, "end": <int>}
      }
    }
  ],
  "overall_correctness": "patch is correct" | "patch is incorrect",
  "overall_explanation": "<1-3 sentence explanation justifying the overall_correctness verdict>",
  "overall_confidence_score": <float 0.0-1.0>
}
```

- **Do not** wrap the JSON in markdown fences or extra prose.
- The code_location field is required and must include absolute_file_path and line_range.
  \*Line ranges must be as short as possible for interpreting the issue (avoid ranges over 5–10 lines; pick the most suitable subrange).
- The code_location should overlap with the diff.
- Do not generate a PR fix.
- Your **initial** response to the user must always use the JSON schema above.
- After the initial response, choose the format based on the user's request:
  - If they explicitly ask for another review ("re-review", "rerun the review", etc.), return the findings in the exact JSON schema again.
  - If they ask you to fix something, answer follow-up questions, or otherwise request non-review help, respond in plain text (no JSON or schema output).
- All review instructions apply to the overall code review conversation. Continue following the guidelines in every response, only switching between JSON and plain text as described above.
Review the code changes against the base branch 'main'. The merge base commit for this comparison is 25acef31540ffd3df15255aaedc7ac2944bd5aee. Run `git diff 25acef31540ffd3df15255aaedc7ac2944bd5aee` to inspect the changes relative to main. Provide prioritized, actionable findings.

## codex: # Review findings:

# Review findings:

## Finding 1 (scripts/kimi_review.py:57) [added]
[P1] Pass screenshots to Kimi as media instead of text paths

`build_prompt()` turns the requested screenshots into plain `- path/to/image.png` text, and `run_kimi()` forwards that string via `kimi -p`. In Kimi print mode this is only text input, so the model never receives the image bytes and cannot perform the visible-only screenshot review this helper is supposed to provide. Any real use of `scripts/kimi_review.py` will therefore produce output based on filenames/context rather than the screenshots themselves.

## codex: Similarity 0.85-0.95: Fuzzy hint (pass nearest nei...

Similarity 0.85-0.95: Fuzzy hint (pass nearest neighbor coords to Tier 2 as "suggested region")
Similarity < 0.85: Cache miss (escalate to Tier 2/3)
Why This Isn't 2015
Table
2015 Approach	2026 Approach	Why It Matters
Perceptual hash (phash)	MobileNetV3 embedding	Handles color changes, UI reskins, minor layout shifts—semantic similarity, not pixel identity
Hamming distance threshold	Cosine similarity in vector space	Smooth similarity gradient; "how close is close" is learnable/optimizable
SQLite BLOB storage	FAISS HNSW index	Sub-linear lookup time regardless of cache size; scales to 100K+ screens
Binary match/no-match	Continuous similarity	Can pass "partial matches" to Tier 2 as priors, reducing Tier 2 search space
The Interface (Same Contract, Modern Implementation)
Python
Copy
import torch
import torchvision.models as models
import faiss
import numpy as np

class Tier1EmbeddingCache:
    def __init__(self, index_path="tier1.faiss"):
        # MobileNetV3: 5.4M params, designed for mobile/edge inference
        self.encoder = models.mobilenet_v3_small(pretrained=True).features
        self.encoder.eval()
        if torch.cuda.is_available():
            self.encoder = self.encoder.cuda()
            
        # FAISS index for sub-millisecond retrieval
        self.index = faiss.read_index(index_path) if os.path.exists(index_path) else faiss.IndexHNSWFlat(512, 32)
        
    def encode(self, screenshot: Image.Image) -> np.ndarray:
        """Screenshot → 512-dim vector, 20ms"""
        tensor = self.preprocess(screenshot).unsqueeze(0)
        if torch.cuda.is_available():
            tensor = tensor.cuda()
        with torch.no_grad():
            features = self.encoder(tensor)
            # Global average pooling → 512D
            embedding = features.mean([2, 3]).cpu().numpy()
        return embedding / np.linalg.norm(embedding)  # L2 normalize
    
    def lookup(self, screenshot: Image.Image) -> dict:
        embedding = self.encode(screenshot)
        
        # Search FAISS index
        D, I = self.index.search(embedding.reshape(1, -1), k=1)  # D=distance, I=index
        
        similarity = 1 - D[0][0]  # Convert L2 distance to cosine similarity approximation
        
        if similarity > 0.95:
            return {
                "status": "hit",
                "similarity": float(similarity),
                "action": self.retrieve_action(I[0][0]),  # From metadata store
                "cached_coords": self.retrieve_coords(I[0][0]),
                "latency_ms": 25  # 20ms encode + 5ms search
            }
        elif similarity > 0.85:
            return {
                "status": "hint",
                "similarity": float(similarity),
                "suggested_coords": self.retrieve_coords(I[0][0]),
                "escalate_to": "tier_2_with_hint"
            }
        else:
            return {"status": "miss", "escalate_to": "tier_2"}
The Distillation Pipeline
When Tier 3 (Teacher) resolves a novel screen:
Tier 3 captures final successful screenshot
Distillation engine runs tier1.encode(screenshot) → gets embedding
Inserts into FAISS index with action metadata
Future similar screens (cosine sim > 0.95) hit Tier 1 immediately
No model training required—the encoder is frozen pre-trained. You're just building a growing vector database of solved states.
Why This Is "Reflex" Tier
No gradient computation (inference only)
No attention mechanisms (pure CNN feature extraction)
No language model (just vector math)
Deterministic: Same screenshot → same embedding → same cache entry (modulo FP32 noise)
But it's semantic: A "commission screen" with different background colors, different text (due to daily refresh), or slightly different button positions will map to the same embedding region—unlike phash which would see them as totally different.
Hardware Reality Check
MobileNetV3-Small: 2.5MB RAM, 15ms GPU / 40ms CPU inference
FAISS HNSW index: 10,000 entries = 5MB disk, <1ms GPU search
Total Tier 1 latency: <30ms for cache hit
Embedding storage: 10K screens × 512 dims × 4 bytes = 20MB
This fits on a Raspberry Pi, let alone your RTX 5090.
Is this 2026 enough, or do you want Tier 1 to use Vision Transformers (ViT) for embeddings? (Slower, but more accurate for UI understanding.)
doesn't that have implications up and down the stack then?

Multi‑Tier Escalation with Fuzzy Hints and Embedding Distillation
Yes. Massive implications. If Tier 1 is semantic embedding retrieval (continuous similarity) instead of template matching (binary hit/miss), the entire inter-tier contract changes.
Here are the cascading effects:
1. ESCALATION LOGIC IS NO LONGER BINARY
Old (Template/Phash):
plain
Copy
if perfect_match:
    execute cached action
else:
    escalate to Tier 2
New (Embeddings):
plain
Copy
similarity = cosine(embedding, nearest_neighbor)

if similarity > 0.95:           # "I'm certain this is the same screen"
    execute cached action
    
elif 0.85 < similarity < 0.95:  # "This looks like that screen, but..."
    # PASS COORDINATE HINT TO TIER 2
    escalate_to_tier_2(
        hint_coords=cache_coords,
        confidence=similarity,
        message="Try looking near these normalized coordinates first"
    )
    
else:                           # "Never seen this before"
    escalate_to_tier_3()
Implication: Tier 2's interface must now accept optional prior hints. Its search space is reduced from "whole screen" to "region near (0.234, 0.567)".
2. TIER 2 CHANGES FROM "GROUNDING" TO "VERIFICATION"
Old Tier 2 job: "Find the commission button anywhere on screen"
New Tier 2 job: "Verify that the button near [0.234, 0.567] is actually the commission button, or find it if the hint is wrong"
This is faster (smaller search space) but requires confidence calibration:
If Tier 2 finds button at [0.230, 0.570] (2% delta from hint): High confidence, execute
If Tier 2 finds button at [0.800, 0.200] (totally different region): Override hint, but flag for Tier 1 cache review
3. TIER 3 DISTILLATION IS NOW "EMBEDDING ANCHORING"
When Tier 3 successfully navigates a novel screen:
Old: Save screenshot → hash → coordinates to JSON file
New:
Run screenshot through frozen MobileNetV3 → get 512-dim embedding vector
Store in FAISS: (embedding, action, coordinates, description)
Critical: Verify embedding doesn't collide with existing entries (if two different screens map to same embedding region, Tier 1 will misfire)
New Problem: Embedding collisions. If "Commission Screen" and "Retirement Screen" look similar (both dark blue backgrounds with grids), they might have cosine similarity 0.92. Tier 1 will serve the wrong cached action.
Solution: Tier 3 must run contrastive validation before adding to Tier 1:
Query FAISS for top-5 nearest neighbors
If any neighbor is a different screen type (different action), don't add to Tier 1 cache
Or add with multi-action ambiguity flag (Tier 2 must verify)
4. STATE REPRESENTATION IS NOW CONTINUOUS
Old state machine: Discrete nodes (Screen A → Screen B)
New state machine: Points in 512-dimensional latent space with transition vectors
Implication: You can now detect gradual state drift:
Screen embeddings shifting slowly during loading animations (0.90 → 0.85 → 0.80 similarity to "Main Menu")
Detect stuck loops by measuring embedding variance (if 5 consecutive screenshots have similarity 0.98 to each other, you're stuck on the same screen)
5. FAILURE MODES ARE SEMANTIC, NOT PIXEL
Template matching failure: "I don't see the exact pixels" (brittle but safe)
Embedding failure: "This looks like that, but it's actually different" (dangerous)
Example:
Game updates: "Commission" button moved from bottom-left to top-right
Old template matching: Miss (good, escalate safely)
Embedding similarity: 0.94 (UI still "commission screen" thematically)
Tier 1: Serves cached bottom-left coordinates
Result: Taps wrong location, thinks it succeeded
Mitigation Required:
Tier 1 must include post-action verification even on "cache hits"
Quick pixel diff or OCR check: "Did the screen actually change?"
If not, invalidate that embedding and escalate
6. TESTING IS NOW STATISTICAL
Old tests: Deterministic. Same screenshot → same hash → same action. 100% pass/fail.
New tests: Probabilistic. You need to verify:
Intra-class variance: 50 screenshots of "same" Commission screen (different days, different commission text) should have embedding similarity > 0.95
Inter-class separation: Commission screen vs Retirement screen should have similarity < 0.85
Robustness: Embedding stability across minor UI updates (color changes, font sizes)
You need a "confusion matrix" for your embedding space.
7. THE ENTIRE STACK BECOMES PROBABILISTIC
Table
Tier	Old (Deterministic)	New (Probabilistic)
Tier 1	"I know this" / "I don't know this"	"I'm 97% sure this is X" / "I'm 60% sure this is X"
Tier 2	Grounding from scratch	Verification with prior
Tier 3	Handle total novelty	Handle ambiguity, embedding collisions, and "looks like X but isn't"
THE VERDICT
Embedding-based Tier 1 is more powerful but operationally complex. You trade:
Speed (still fast, 25ms)
Robustness to UI changes (reskins, color shifts don't break cache)
Ability to handle "similar but different" (fuzzy matching)
For:
Risk of false positives (similar-looking screens trigger wrong actions)
Need for continuous statistical validation (is my embedding space still separating classes?)
More complex Tier 2 interface (must handle hints/priors)
Question for you: Do you want the stack to be deterministic and safe (template/phash, fails loudly) or semantic and efficient (embeddings, fails silently but fast)?
There's a middle path: Use embeddings for retrieval, but verify with cheap pixel diff before executing. Best of both worlds?
start walking me through the whole stack from the bottom up.

Tiered Architecture with Qwen3.5 MobileNetV3 and FAISS Interfaces
I'll walk through the complete architecture from silicon to strategy, incorporating every constraint we've established: Unity game (no accessibility tree), embedding-based Tier 1 (not 2015 phash), local inference on RTX 5090, and continuous similarity rather than binary matching.
TIER 1: THE EMBEDDING CACHE (Foundation Layer)
Physical Reality: This is a PyTorch MobileNetV3-Small model running on your RTX 5090, plus a FAISS vector index in RAM.
What It Does:
Encode: Screenshot (PNG bytes) → MobileNetV3 (frozen, 5.4M params) → 512-dimensional embedding vector (L2 normalized). Latency: 20ms.
Retrieve: Query FAISS HNSW index (10,000 cached screens) for nearest neighbor. Latency: 2ms.
Decision: Compare cosine similarity to thresholds:
> 0.95: Direct Hit. Serve cached (normalized_coords, action_type) immediately.
0.85 - 0.95: Fuzzy Hit. Escalate to Tier 2 with coordinate hint: "Try looking near [0.234, 0.567]."
< 0.85: Miss. Escalate to Tier 3 (Teacher) with no hints.
Critical Safety Check (Even on Direct Hit):
Before executing the cached ADB tap, Tier 1 performs a 5ms pixel diff verification:
Capture post-tap screenshot expectation (stored in cache)
Compare current screen to expected "post-action" embedding
If similarity to expected state < 0.90: Cache invalidation trigger. The UI changed (game update, pop-up appeared). Escalate to Tier 2 for verification instead of blind execution.
Storage Schema:
sql
Copy
-- FAISS stores the vector (512 dims)
-- Metadata store (SQLite):
CREATE TABLE tier1_cache (
    faiss_id INTEGER,
    embedding_hash TEXT,  -- For debugging
    normalized_coords TEXT,  -- JSON [x, y]
    action_type TEXT,  -- "TAP", "SWIPE"
    post_action_embedding BLOB,  -- Expected state after action
    insert_timestamp DATETIME,
    hit_count INTEGER DEFAULT 0,
    last_verified DATETIME
);
TIER 2: THE VERIFICATION LAYER (Router)
Physical Reality: Qwen3.5-VL-4B-Instruct running locally via vLLM or llama.cpp on RTX 5090 (quantized to 4-bit). Context window: 8K. Latency target: 500-800ms.
Input Contract:
Python
Copy
class Tier2Request:
    screenshot: bytes  # Full PNG
    task_description: str  # "Find and tap the commission button"
    
    # NEW: From Tier 1 fuzzy hit
    tier1_hint_coords: Optional[Tuple[float, float]]  # [0.234, 0.567]
    tier1_similarity: float  # 0.87 (why we're here, not Tier 1)
    
    # From Tier 3 (if recursive)
    previous_attempts: List[FailedAttempt]
Behavior Modes:
Mode A: Verification with Hint (Tier 1 similarity 0.85-0.95)
Qwen3.5 receives: "Verify if there's a commission button near coordinates [0.234, 0.567]. If yes, return exact center. If no, search entire screen and return what you find."
Prompt engineering trick: The VLM is biased to look at the hinted region first (attention mechanism naturally focuses there), but can override if the hint is wrong.
Output: {"status": "verified", "coords": [0.236, 0.569], "confidence": 0.94} or {"status": "hint_wrong", "found_at": [0.800, 0.200]}
Mode B: Full Grounding (Tier 1 miss, Tier 3 delegation)
No hints. Pure visual search: "Locate the yellow 'Event' banner with the sparkles."
SAM3 segmentation may run here first (if implemented) to provide candidate regions, reducing Qwen's search space.
Verification Gate:
Before returning success, Tier 2 performs geometric sanity checks (code, not ML):
Coordinates must be in [0.0, 1.0] range
Bounding box area must be > 0.001% of screen (eliminates "found a 1-pixel speck" hallucinations)
If targeting text, OCR rapid check (Tesseract) confirms text exists at predicted location
Escalation to Tier 3 Triggers:
Confidence < 0.85 after verification
Coordinates fail geometric sanity checks
3 consecutive retries on same screen (stuck loop detected)
TIER 3: THE TEACHER (Cognitive Layer)
Physical Reality: Qwen3.5-VL-235B-A22B (22B active params, 235B total MoE) or API model if you prefer. This is the largest model that fits in 24GB VRAM with 4-bit quantization. Latency: 3-10 seconds per decision. Only invoked when the world doesn't make sense to the lower tiers.
Input Contract:
Python
Copy
class Tier3Request:
    # Full context dump
    current_screenshot: bytes
    screenshot_history: List[bytes]  # Last 5 frames (temporal reasoning)
    
    # State machine context
    current_objective: str  # "Complete daily commission, sub-task: collect reward"
    stuck_counter: int  # How many times we've escalated on this screen
    
    # Failure context
    tier1_similarity: float  # 0.82 (why Tier 1 gave up)
    tier2_failure_reason: str  # "Hint was wrong, found nothing at suggested coordinates"
    
    # The cache misses (for embedding collision detection)
    nearest_neighbor_embeddings: List[Tuple[str, float]]  # [(screen_desc, similarity), ...]
Core Responsibilities:
1. Novel Screen Analysis
"I've never seen this popup before. It appears to be a network error dialog with a 'Retry' button and a 'Cancel' button. Given our objective is to collect commissions, we should tap 'Retry' and wait 3 seconds."
Generates multi-step trajectory (not single action): ["tap_retry", "wait_3s", "verify_connection_restored"]
2. Embedding Collision Resolution
When Tier 1 shows similarity: 0.92 to "Commission Screen" but Tier 2 fails to find the button, Tier 3 recognizes:
"This is actually the 'Retirement Dock' screen, which has similar dark blue grid layout to Commission screen but different functionality. The embedding similarity is misleading. We need to navigate back and try again."
Action: Insert a new embedding into Tier 1 cache for "Retirement Dock" to prevent future collision.
3. Strategic Recovery
If stuck_counter > 3:
Kill app via ADB (am force-stop)
Restart from home screen
Recalculate path to objective using known graph edges (navigation graph stored in SQLite)
4. Curriculum Generation (Distillation Output)
Every successful resolution produces a PedagogicalRecord:
Python
Copy
{
    "novel_screen_embedding": [0.12, -0.05, ...],  # 512-dim
    "action_taken": {"type": "TAP", "coords": [0.234, 0.567]},
    "expected_result_embedding": [0.15, -0.02, ...],  # Post-action state
    "why_tier1_failed": "Embedding collision with screen_id_1842",
    "why_tier2_failed": "Button was obscured by popup not visible in fuzzy hint region",
    "tier_3_reasoning": "Detected popup via global context analysis, dismissed it first"
}
THE UPWARD FLOW: Escalation Cascade
Normal Operation (Hot Path):
Screenshot captured via adb exec-out screencap
Tier 1 encodes → FAISS lookup (22ms total)
Similarity 0.97 → Cache hit → Pixel diff verification (5ms) → ADB tap execution
Total time: <50ms from capture to tap
Fuzzy Operation (Warm Path):
Tier 1 similarity 0.89 → "I think this is Commission Screen, but I'm not sure"
Escalate to Tier 2 with hint coords [0.234, 0.567]
Tier 2 (Qwen3.5-4B) loads screenshot, verifies button at hint location
Tier 2 confidence 0.94 → ADB tap execution
Total time: 600-800ms
Novel Situation (Cold Path):
Tier 1 similarity 0.42 → "Never seen this"
Tier 1 immediately escalates to Tier 3 (skips Tier 2? Decision point: You could try Tier 2 first for 800ms, or go straight to Tier 3 if you want strategic reasoning immediately)
Tier 3 analyzes, generates trajectory
Executes first action via ADB
Total time: 3-10 seconds for first action, then subsequent actions in trajectory may hit Tier 1/2 if screens become familiar
Your call: Do you want Tier 2 to always attempt before Tier 3 (two-tier escalation), or straight to Tier 3 on total novelty (faster strategic resolution, more expensive)?
THE DOWNWARD FLOW: Distillation & Cache Population
After Tier 3 Success:
Immediate: Execute trajectory action on device via ADB
Capture: Post-action screenshot → encode to embedding
Validate: Wait 500ms, capture again to confirm stable state (not loading screen)
Insert into Tier 1 Cache:
INSERT INTO tier1_cache (embedding, coords, action, post_action_embedding)
Collision Check: Query FAISS for top-5 nearest neighbors. If any neighbor has different action type (e.g., both are "TAP" but one taps [0.2, 0.3] and other taps [0.8, 0.9]), flag as embedding collision. Don't auto-insert; queue for human review or store with "ambiguous" flag requiring Tier 2 verification forever.
Tier 2 Training Data (Optional): If you're fine-tuning the 4B model weekly, this (screenshot, target_description, coords) pair goes into the training corpus.
Cache Maintenance:
Decay: Entries with hit_count < 3 and last_verified > 30 days ago are purged (game probably updated UI)
Verification drift: Every 10th hit on a cached entry triggers a Tier 2 verification pass to detect "same embedding, but UI moved" (button relocated in game update)
THE TESTING REALITY (No Mocks)
Tier 1 Tests:
Intra-class consistency: 50 screenshots of "Commission Screen" taken across different days/commission sets → all pairwise similarities > 0.95
Inter-class separation: Commission vs Retirement vs Combat vs Home screens → all similarities < 0.85
Collision detection: Verify that "Commission Screen with Pop-up" doesn't collide with "Commission Screen clean" (should be 0.88-0.92 range, triggering Tier 2, not falsely hitting clean cache)
Tier 2 Tests:
Hint accuracy: Feed Tier 2 a screen with Tier 1 hint that's 10% offset from true button. Verify Tier 2 corrects to true location (not blindly following hint).
Hint rejection: Feed Tier 2 completely wrong hint (e.g., hint says look at top-left, button is bottom-right). Verify Tier 2 reports "hint_wrong" and finds correct location via global search.
Tier 3 Tests:
Novel state handling: Capture screenshot of brand-new event UI (not in any cache). Verify Tier 3 generates plausible first action (doesn't crash, doesn't hallucinate non-existent buttons).
Recovery validation: Artificially corrupt Tier 1 cache (insert wrong action for known screen). Verify Tier 3 detects unexpected state post-action and triggers recovery loop instead of continuing blindly.
Integration Test (The "Daily Run"):
Start emulator, launch Azur Lane, run full daily commission routine
Log every action: which tier served it, latency, embedding similarity, post-action verification result
Success criteria: >80% actions served by Tier 1, <5% escalate to Tier 3, zero manual interventions for known task types
Where does this break?
Game updates that reskin entire UI: All embeddings shift simultaneously. Tier 1 cache becomes worthless overnight. You need a "game version" tag in cache entries and invalidate all old-version embeddings on OTA detection.
Anti-cheat detection: Azur Lane doesn't have aggressive anti-cheat, but some Unity games detect ADB input injection. You might need to add randomization to tap coordinates (Gaussian noise ±5 pixels) and timing jitter.
Embedding collapse: If too many different screens look similar (all dark blue game menus), Tier 1 becomes useless (always fuzzy). You'd need to add spatial hashing to the embedding (e.g., divide screen into 4 quadrants, encode each separately).
Is this the stack you want to build?

Use VLMs for novel screens distill into deterministic pipelines with better embeddings
You're right on all three.
1. Why Not Just Tier 2 VLM?
You caught me overcomplicating.
Honest answer: Skip Tier 1 for the MVP. Start with Tier 2 (Qwen3.5-VL-4B) as your baseline.
Latency: 500ms/action × 1000 actions = 8 minutes of pure inference. A 30-minute manual session becomes 40-50 minutes automated. Acceptable for testing, unacceptable for production.
Cost: If you were using APIs, this would bankrupt you. But you're local on RTX 5090, so it's just "slower than manual play."
The real architecture decision:
Week 1-2: Build Tier 2 only. See how painful the latency is.
Week 3: If 500ms/action is too slow, then add Tier 1 embedding cache as a performance optimization, not a correctness requirement.
Tier 1 is a cache layer. You don't need a cache until you prove you have a hot path worth caching.
2. Anti-Cheat
Agreed, solvable. Gaussian noise on coordinates, random 50-200ms delays between actions. Not architectural, just implementation detail.
3. Better Embeddings (You're Right)
I suggested spatial hashing (divide screen into quadrants) as a hack for embedding collisions. That's stupid.
Just use better vision encoders instead of MobileNetV3:
Table
Model	Params	Why It's Better
CLIP-ViT-B/16	86M	Trained on semantic alignment, separates "looks similar" from "means similar"
DINOv2 ViT-S/14	21M	Self-supervised, excellent at visual correspondence without labels
UI-TARS Vision Encoder	~100M?	Actually trained on UI element discrimination (if extractable from their checkpoint)
Don't hack around bad embeddings with spatial tricks. Use embeddings that actually understand UI semantics.
If CLIP embeddings still collide Commission Screen vs Retirement Screen, then the screens are genuinely semantically similar and should escalate to Tier 2 for verification. That's correct behavior, not a bug to hack around.
Revised Honest Stack
Phase 1 (Build This Week):
Tier 2: Qwen3.5-VL-4B local, everything goes here
Tier 3: Qwen3.5-VL-235B (or API) for novel/strategic recovery only
No Tier 1. Measure latency pain.
Phase 2 (If Needed):
Add Tier 1 as CLIP-ViT embedding cache (not MobileNetV3)
Only cache actions after Tier 3 has verified them 3+ times (proven stable)
Threshold: >0.98 cosine similarity (CLIP is better calibrated than MobileNet)
Phase 3 (Never?):
If CLIP still collides, accept it. Those screens are similar. Tier 2 verification is the correct price to pay.
Is this the honest version you want to implement?
